Here begin investigations: the commentator, as per his custom, starts a series of objections against the author. First objection: the purpose was to define fiqh as it is a technical term among the people, but the author's definition cannot be the technical fiqh because it is, according to them, a name for a specific science, like other sciences are specific sciences. According to what the author mentioned, fiqh would be a name for a universal concept that changes with times and eras and increases day by day until the end of the prophetic era, because in the time of the Prophet, revelation came down gradually, so according to that the knowledge of fiqh would increase day by day; then after the Prophet, it would continue to increase due to the occurrence of ijma'. Also it would decrease according to abrogating verses, because in the time of the Prophet abrogation occurred, so in one respect it decreases; and after the Prophet, if ijma' goes against a solitary report, that report would be abrogated, so with its abrogation a decrease occurs. In any case, according to the author's definition, fiqh is not a specific and determined science, whereas it is a specific and determined science. Answer to the first objection: what does the commentator mean by 'a name for a specific science'? If he means specific in a personal sense (ta'yin shakhsi) that is limited to a fixed number of rulings not subject to increase, this meaning is not correct because all compiled sciences are universal sciences that are subject to increase from time to time with the succession of thoughts. That is why the names of sciences are called generic proper nouns (a'lam jinsiyya), not personal proper nouns. If by 'specific' he means specific in a generic sense (ta'yin naw'i), i.e., it discusses the essential attributes of one subject by which it is distinguished from other sciences, then this kind of specificity is not contradictory to change over times and eras; rather, it can admit increase and decrease. After all, the Companions who are agreed upon as jurists: their knowledge used to increase gradually according to the revelation of rulings, and when a ruling was abrogated, a decrease occurred. So increase and decrease do not contravene generic specificity. Moreover, in the case of abrogation, knowledge of the abrogating and abrogated is necessary for the mujtahid jurist, so in that case there is no actual decrease in knowledge, and increase in sciences continues to happen, which cannot be denied. Second objection: this definition does not apply to the fiqh of the Companions because during the life of the Prophet there was no ijma', yet the author made knowledge of rulings upon which ijma' occurred a necessary part of fiqh. Therefore, the definition does not apply to the Companions who were jurists in the Prophet's time. [It is as if] the author intended that fiqh is only knowledge of what is revealed if there is no ijma'; but if there is ijma', then fiqh becomes knowledge of what is revealed and knowledge of what is agreed upon. Such doubts are far-fetched in definitions. The answer is that the author's intention is indeed this meaning, as he stated in al-Tawdih, and there is no oddity in such a definition, because it is well-known that during the Prophet's time the Companions had fiqh and ijtihad even though ijma' did not exist then. From this it becomes clear that the intention is that knowledge of rulings upon which ijma' is concluded is necessary when ijma' exists; if it does not exist, then such knowledge is not a condition. Due to this well-known fact, there is no remoteness in this intention. Besides, the author's statement 'and which are agreed upon' means 'and which are agreed upon when it occurs'. So now the meaning of the definition would be: fiqh is knowledge of what appears with revelation, while it is conjoined with knowledge of rulings upon which ijma' is concluded.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute presenting two objections to the definition of fiqh given by the author (Sadr al-Shariah) and their refutation by the commentator. The first objection argues that the author's definition makes fiqh a universal concept that changes with time, whereas technically fiqh is a specific and fixed science. The response clarifies that 'specific' does not mean person-specific (limited to a fixed number) but genre-specific (distinct subject and essential attributes). All sciences, including fiqh, can increase and decrease without losing their specificity; the Companions' fiqh grew with revelation and decreased with abrogation. The second objection claims the definition fails for the Prophet's time because ijma' did not exist. The answer is that the definition implicitly includes ijma' only when it occurs, as known from the well-established fact that the Companions had fiqh before ijma'. The commentator thus defends the author's definition as logically sound and consistent with the historical development of fiqh.

Key Terms
علم بما ظهر به نزول الوحی (‘ilm bimā ẓahara bihi nuzūl al-waḥy): Knowledge of rulings established through direct revelation to the Prophet (Qur'an and Sunnah).
جماع (ijma'): Consensus of the mujtahids of the Ummah after the Prophet's death on a shari' ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, when is knowledge of ijma' required for a faqih?
A) Always, because the definition includes it unconditionally.
B) Only when ijma' exists (when it occurs).
C) Never, because fiqh is only about revelation.
D) Only during the Prophet's time.

Key Takeaway
The definition of fiqh is conditional: knowledge of ijma' is required only when ijma' exists, preserving the fiqh of earlier generations.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
Speculative Rulings as Certain in Hanafi Usul
Responding to objection that fiqh cannot be called qat'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school elevates speculative rulings to decisive knowledge using the unanimous premise, and analyze the objection and its resolution.

Core Idea
A speculative ruling becomes 'ilm qat'i not in itself, but because acting upon it is certain – a practical certainty derived from consensus.

This passage takes up a fundamental epistemological puzzle: how can fiqh, built on speculative evidence, be called knowledge? It presents an objection, two Hanafi responses, a syllogistic proof, and a critical resolution. The key is the 'unanimous premise' (muqaddima ijma'iyya) that the mujtahid's dominant conjecture must be acted upon. This transforms zanni evidence into qat'i for practical purposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine whether a speculative ruling (hukm maznun) can be called 'ilm qat'i (decisive knowledge). The objector says no, the Hanafi position says yes in a practical sense.
This is a dispute about the definition of 'ilm and the status of fiqh.
2
Examine the objection
The objector argues that decisive knowledge requires no possibility of error in reality. Since speculative evidence always carries such possibility, calling it decisive is incorrect.
This objection relies on a strict ontological definition of certainty.
3
Analyze the first Hanafi response
The term 'ilm is used broadly, as opposed to mere speculation (zann). Under this definition, a ruling that is zanni in reality can still be called 'ilm if it is not mere conjecture.
This response redefines 'ilm in a practical, not ontological, sense.
4
Analyze the second response: the syllogistic argument
The second response combines speculative evidence with the unanimous premise (muqaddima ijma'iyya): 'Every ruling dominant in the mujtahid's conjecture is obligatory to act upon.' This premise is certain by consensus. Using syllogism: the speculative ruling is decisively obligatory to act upon; everything decisively obligatory to act upon is decisively known to be Allah's ruling; therefore, the speculative ruling is decisively known.
The syllogism is formalized in the passage; the unanimous premise is the key that bridges zann and qat'.
5
Evaluate the resolution (hall)
The commentator rejects the universal premise that 'every ruling obligatory to act upon is known to be Allah's ruling' because it is itself the point of dispute. If accepted, the conclusion is only particular. However, if one adopts the view of taswib (every mujtahid is correct), then the universal premise holds and the whole discussion becomes unnecessary.
The resolution shows the limits of the syllogism and highlights the role of taswib.

عمل کرنا لازم ہو جائے گا وہ علی الثانی ثانی سے مراد ہو ثابت بالنظر الی الدلیل ہے اس پر یہ اشکال والہ دکیا کہ اس شق پر یہ لازم آتا ہے کہ جو حکم دلیل ظنی کے لحاظ سے ثابت ہو جائے اگرچہ اس کے ثبوت واقعی اگر اس کی بنیاد اس پر ہو کہ ہر مظنون مجتہد قطعا حکم الہی ہوتا ہے كما هو راى البعض یعنی جیسے ان حضرات کی رائے ہے جو ہر مجتہد کی تصویب کے قاتل ہیں تو يكون ذكر وجوب العمل ضائعا لا معنى له اصلا کیونکہ اس جبکہ شارح کے تمام اعتراضات کے جوابات سابقاً مذکور ہو چکے ہیں ۔ مظہر ماذکرنا من تحقیق الکلام ان لیس ماذكر البعض غاية ما امكن في هذا المقام-
It will be obligatory to act, and that is according to the second meaning, established by looking at the evidence. An objection was raised on this: that according to this clause, it follows that a ruling established by speculative evidence, even if its actual reality is not known, is called decisive, even though this is not correct because decisive proof is that in which there is no possibility of non-existence in reality and in itself, and here it is not like that, rather there is a possibility of non-existence in reality. One answer given is that here 'ilm (knowledge) in the rulings [؟] means as opposed to speculation, i.e., a decisive ruling whether it corresponds to reality or not. In summary, since knowledge and affirmation include speculation, ignorance, imitation, and certainty and conviction, so here 'ilm is meant as opposed to speculation, and it includes all categories except speculation, so the decisive ruling, whether it corresponds to reality or not, both will be included under knowledge. Or it may be said that 'by looking at the evidence' does not mean the evidence alone, but together with the unanimous premise, i.e., every ruling that is dominant in the conjecture of the mujtahid is obligatory to act upon, or it is established by it, so this unanimous premise together with the speculative evidence becomes productive of certainty, as is well known that a solitary report surrounded by circumstantial evidence becomes productive of certainty. And the utmost possible effort in this regard that has been made to place these speculative matters as certain matters is what some investigators have mentioned in Sharh al-Minhaj: that the speculative ruling for the mujtahid is decisively obligatory to act upon. This is the minor premise; the major premise is coming ahead, which together with it will produce the desired result. 'By the decisive evidence' – this is the proof of the establishment of this minor premise, and by this decisive evidence is meant consensus and solitary reports that are meaning-wise mutawatir. 'Every ruling which is decisively obligatory to act upon, it is known decisively that it is the ruling of Allah' – this is the second minor premise, and 'and what is not obligatory to act upon' – this is the proof of the establishment of the second minor premise. The summary is that as long as there is no certainty about a ruling being the ruling of Allah, acting upon it is not obligatory. From this it became clear that every ruling that is obligatory to act upon, there is decisive knowledge about it that it is the ruling of Allah. 'And everything that is known decisively that it is the ruling of Allah, it is known decisively' – this is the major premise of the second minor premise, whose conclusion is that a ruling about which there is decisive knowledge that it is the ruling of Allah cannot remain speculative, rather it reaches the level of decisively known. So 'every ruling that is decisively obligatory to act upon is decisively known' – this is the result after combining the second minor premise with its major premise by eliminating the middle term. Now make this result a major premise for the first minor premise: 'The speculative ruling for the mujtahid is decisively obligatory to act upon, and everything that is decisively obligatory to act upon is decisively known.' The result is what the commentator mentioned: 'So the speculative ruling for the mujtahid is decisively known.' This is the desired result which was our main objective. From this it became clear that fiqh is decisive knowledge, i.e., fiqh is decisive, not speculative. Therefore, applying the word 'knowledge' which is specific to certainties to it is correct. 'And speculation is a means to it' – and speculation is a means and instrument to reach it, and the desired towards which attainment is achieved is decisive, not speculative. 'And its resolution: we do not concede' – with this resolution, the commentator intends to reject this possible effort, and he denies a specific premise, i.e., 'every ruling that is decisively obligatory to act upon is known decisively that it is the ruling of Allah' – we do not concede this universal, because why is it not possible that acting upon a ruling becomes decisively obligatory while only a conjecture that it is the ruling of Allah? So it was not established that every obligatory ruling is decisively known. And what some investigators presented as proof for this universal, i.e., 'and what is not obligatory to act upon' is exactly the point of dispute, so presenting it as a proof is begging the question and circular. So the second minor premise did not remain universal; in that case, the result will be particular. Thus, it was not established that every speculative ruling of the mujtahid is decisively known universally, whereas the desired was the universal. 'And if it is based on the fact that every speculative ruling of the mujtahid is decisively the ruling of Allah' – as is the view of some who hold that every mujtahid is correct – 'then mentioning the obligation of action becomes useless, having no meaning at all', because at that time, to establish fiqh as decisive knowledge, it would have been sufficient that it is a speculative ruling for the mujtahid and every speculative ruling for the mujtahid is decisively known that it is the ruling of Allah decisively. In reality, the need for all this 'utmost possible' and its resolution would not have arisen, while all the commentator's objections have already been answered previously. It appears from what we have mentioned of the investigation of the statement that what some have mentioned is not the utmost possible in this regard.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute about whether fiqh (Islamic jurisprudence) can be called 'ilm qat'i (decisive knowledge) even though it is based on speculative (zanni) evidences. The author first presents an objection: if a ruling is established by speculative evidence, calling it decisive is incorrect because decisive implies no possibility of error in reality, whereas speculative evidence always carries that possibility. The author then gives two responses. First, the term 'ilm (knowledge) in this context is used broadly to include certainty and also what is contrary to speculation, so a ruling can be called 'ilm even if it might not correspond to reality. Second, the speculative evidence combined with the unanimous premise (that the mujtahid's dominant conjecture must be acted upon) yields certainty. He then presents a more elaborate argument from some scholars that the speculative ruling is decisively obligatory to act upon, and using syllogistic reasoning, he concludes that such a ruling is decisively known. After this, he presents a resolution (hall) which contests the major premise that every ruling obligatory to act upon is known to be Allah's ruling. The objector argues that this premise is not universally accepted; it is the very point of dispute. Thus, the attempt to make all speculative rulings decisively known fails. Finally, he notes that if one accepts the view that every mujtahid's ruling is correct (taswib), then the whole discussion is unnecessary because then every speculative ruling is automatically known to be Allah's ruling. The passage ends by stating that the earlier objections have already been answered. This is a sophisticated Hanafi usul argument about the epistemological status of fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
حكم مظنون (hukm maznun): A ruling that is established by speculative evidence (zann), i.e., not certain in itself
علم قطعي ('ilm qat'i): Decisive knowledge that carries no possibility of error in the actual reality
مقدمہ اجماعیہ (muqaddima ijma'iyya): A unanimously accepted premise that the mujtahid's dominant conjecture must be acted upon

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the argument presented, what makes a speculative ruling (hukm maznun) become 'ilm qat'i?
A) The evidence itself becomes certain
B) The unanimous premise that the mujtahid's dominant conjecture must be acted upon
C) The mujtahid's personal conviction
D) The ruling being mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms that fiqh is decisive knowledge because the obligation to act on strong conjecture is itself certain, established by consensus.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
Defense of Tawassul for the Muqallid and the Implied Genitive in Usul
Refutes the commentator's objection and explains the implicit genitive in the matn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the author's speculative generalization from a substantive claim and explain the hadhf mudaf construction in the definition of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Tawassul for the muqallid is only a remote possibility, and 'proofs' in usul means 'states of proofs' via deletion.

In this passage, the commentator al-Taftazani objects to a statement by Sadr al-Shari'ah regarding tawassul, and the defense clarifies that it was only a speculative remark. Additionally, the passage explains a common ellipsis in Arabic whereby the word 'states' is omitted but understood when defining the subject matter of usul al-fiqh. This lesson helps you recognize how careful reading of matn and shahr reveals both substantive and rhetorical nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the commentator's objection
Read the objection that the generalization of tawassul to muqallid is far-fetched because no scholar holds it.
The commentator uses 'al-zahir annahu ba'id' to stress the apparent improbability.
2
Understand the author's defense
Note that the author only presented it as a 'contrary-to-apparent probability' (khilaf zahir), not as a definitive claim.
The defense relies on the fact that acknowledging a remote possibility is not objectionable.
3
Grasp the principle of subject matter in a science
Every science investigates the 'states' (ahwal) of its subject, not the subject's essence.
This is why the author's phrase 'an al-adillah' must imply 'an ahwal al-adillah'.
4
Apply the concept of haf mudaf
Recognize that the genitive noun 'ahwal' is deleted but understood, a common Arabic rhetorical device.
The deletion is idiomatic and not specific to usul al-fiqh.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح في التلويج قوله ولا يبعد ان يقال الظاهر انه بعيد مصنف کے توسل الی الفقہ کے اندر تعمیم کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ یہ بعید نہیں ہے کہ مجتہد اور مقلد دونوں کے لئے توصل ہو تو اس پر شارح نے یہ اعتراض کر دیا کہ الظاہرا نہ بعید یعنی یہ تعمیم کہ مجتہد اور مقلد دونوں کے لئے توصل کا قول کرنا بعید ہے اذ لم يذهب الیه ای الی هذا التصمیم در حقیقت مصنف پر یہ اعتراض واقع نہیں ہو سکتا کہ دنکہ مصنف نے احتمال اول کو ظاہر قرار دیا ہے اور یہ احتمال ثانی خلاف ظاہر ہے جس کا مصنف کو خود اعتراف ہے اور خلاف ظاہر احتمال کو بدرجہ احتمال پیش کر دینا قابل اعتراض نہیں ہے۔ و المتعرضون لمباحث التقليد یہ جواب ہے اس اعتراض کا کہ جب اس تعمیم کی طرف کوئی بھی نہیں گیا تو پھر کتب اصول مباحث تقلید کا ذکر کیوں ہے تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ جن حضرات نے اپنی کتب میں ان مباحث کا تعرض کیا ہے ان سے تصریح موجود ہے کہ ان مبات کا وقوع بمقابلہ اجتہاد ہے نہ بایں حیثیت کہ یہ مباحث فن ہیں۔ قوله علم انه يبحث في هذا العلم عن الادلة التي مصنف نے فرمایا کہ اس علم میں اولہ اور احکام سے بحث کی جائے گی تو شارح یعنی عن احوالہما کہ کہ حذف مضاف کی طرف اشارہ کیا کیونکہ اولہ اور احکام اس علم کے لئے موضوع ہیں اور کوئی فن اپنے موضوع کے نفس اور ذات سے بحث نہیں کرتا بلکہ موضوع کے احوال و عوارض سے بحث کرتا ہے لہذا مصنف کی مراد بھی عن احوال الادلة والاحکام ہے اور حذف مضاف عبارت قوم میں شائع اور ذائع ہے باوجود محذوف ہونے کے معنی
The commentator in al-Talwih said: 'His statement: and it is not far to say the apparent is far.' The author, while generalizing tawassul ila al-fiqh, said it is not far that both mujtahid and muqallid can have tawassul. The commentator objected that this generalization is far because no one holds it. The response: the author only presented it as a contrary-to-apparent probability, which is not objectionable. As for why books on usul discuss taqlid, it is because these topics are in contrast to ijtihad, not because they are part of the science. Then the author said: 'Know that in this science one investigates the proofs.' The commentator indicates that 'an ahwal al-adillah wa al-ahkam is implied because no science investigates its subject itself, but its states and accidents.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct but related points. First, the commentator (al-Taftazani) in al-Talwih objects to the author's (Sadr al-Shari'ah) suggestion that tawassul (access to deriving rulings) can be generalized to both mujtahid and muqallid. The defense argues that the author only mentioned it as a remote probability, and since he explicitly acknowledged it is contrary to the apparent, it is not a claim that requires proof. The second point addresses why discussions of taqlid (imitation) appear in usul books: they are presented in contrast to ijtihad, not as core topics. Finally, the passage explains that the expression 'investigates the proofs' actually implies 'investigates the states of proofs and rulings,' because no science studies the essence of its subject, only its accidental properties. This is a standard principle in Islamic sciences: the mawdu' (subject matter) is not studied per se; rather, its ahwal (states) are. The deletion of the genitive noun (حذف مضاف) is a common rhetorical device in Arabic.

Key Terms
حذف مضاف (hadhf mudaf): The deletion of the first noun in a genitive construction, where the intended meaning is understood from context.
توسل (tawassul): Access or means to derive fiqh rulings; the author considered it possible for both mujtahid and muqallid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator object to the author's statement about tawassul?
A) Because it is a weak hadith
B) Because no scholar holds that muqallids have tawassul
C) Because it contradicts the Quran
D) Because it is a matter of ijma

Key Takeaway
In usul texts, apparent claims may only be speculative possibilities, and elliptical expressions like 'about proofs' must be understood as 'about the states of proofs' due to the principle that sciences study accidents of their subject.

Defending the Inclusion of Taqlid in Usul al-Fiqh
Defending the inclusion of taqlid discussions as a contrast to ijtihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul works include discussions on taqlid and evaluate the objection that such discussions are extraneous.

Core Idea
Taqlid discussions in usul are a pedagogical foil for ijtihad, not a core subject—their inclusion is defended as a legitimate contrast.

This passage presents a defense of why usul al-fiqh books contain discussions on taqlid, despite taqlid not being an integral part of the science. Critics argue that such discussions are out of place, but the commentator explains that they are included only in contrast to ijtihad. By working through this dispute, you will understand the principle of maintaining disciplinary boundaries while using contrast as a teaching tool.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Find the critic's claim: that the author's generalization of tawassul to both mujtahid and muqallid is far-fetched because no one holds that view, and that discussing taqlid in usul books is inappropriate.
The objection has two parts: one about the author's specific statement, and one about the general inclusion of taqlid topics.
2
Analyze the defense of the author
See how the commentator defends the author: the author only presented a second, less apparent probability, which is not objectionable since it was presented as a possibility, not a claim.
This shows scholarly rigor in distinguishing between asserting a view and presenting a possibility.
3
Relate the broader objection
Understand the second objection: if taqlid is not part of usul, why do usul books discuss it at all? The critic implies the science should be pure.
This is a methodological critique about the scope of a discipline.
4
State the Hanafi response
Learn the Hanafi response: the discussions are explicitly marked as occurring 'bi-muqabila al-ijtihad' (in contrast to ijtihad), not as core topics. They serve a pedagogical purpose.
The key phrase is 'بمقابلة الاجتهاد' which indicates contrast, not inclusion.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical consequence: Hanafi usul texts include taqlid sections, while other schools may not. This difference reflects a methodological choice about how to teach usul.
The inclusion does not affect the substance of usul principles; it is a matter of presentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح في التلويج قوله ولا يبعد ان يقال الظاهر انه بعيد مصنف کے توسل الی الفقہ کے اندر تعمیم کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ یہ بعید نہیں ہے کہ مجتہد اور مقلد دونوں کے لئے توصل ہو تو اس پر شارح نے یہ اعتراض کر دیا کہ الظاہرا نہ بعید یعنی یہ تعمیم کہ مجتہد اور مقلد دونوں کے لئے توصل کا قول کرنا بعید ہے اذ لم يذهب الیه ای الی هذا التصمیم در حقیقت مصنف پر یہ اعتراض واقع نہیں ہو سکتا کہ دنکہ مصنف نے احتمال اول کو ظاہر قرار دیا ہے اور یہ احتمال ثانی خلاف ظاہر ہے جس کا مصنف کو خود اعتراف ہے اور خلاف ظاہر احتمال کو بدرجہ احتمال پیش کر دینا قابل اعتراض نہیں ہے۔ و المتعرضون لمباحث التقليد یہ جواب ہے اس اعتراض کا کہ جب اس تعمیم کی طرف کوئی بھی نہیں گیا تو پھر کتب اصول مباحث تقلید کا ذکر کیوں ہے تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ جن حضرات نے اپنی کتب میں ان مباحث کا تعرض کیا ہے ان سے تصریح موجود ہے کہ ان مبات کا وقوع بمقابلہ اجتہاد ہے نہ بایں حیثیت کہ یہ مباحث فن ہیں۔
The commentator said in Al-Talwih: his statement 'it is not far-fetched to say that it is apparent that it is far-fetched' — the author, in his Tawassul ila al-Fiqh, made a generalization saying that it is not far-fetched that tawassul is for both the mujtahid and the muqallid. So the commentator objected: 'al-zahir annahu ba'id', i.e., this generalization — saying that tawassul is for both mujtahid and muqallid — is far-fetched, because no one has held this view. In reality, this objection cannot be leveled against the author, because the author considered the first probability as apparent, and this second probability is contrary to the apparent, which the author himself acknowledges. And presenting a contrary-to-apparent probability as a probability is not objectionable. 'And those who discuss the topics of taqlid' — this is the answer to the objection that if no one has held this generalization, then why do books of usul mention the topics of taqlid? The answer is that those scholars who discussed these topics in their books have explicitly stated that these topics are presented in opposition to ijtihad, not as topics of the science itself.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a dispute regarding the inclusion of discussions on taqlid (following a mujtahid) in usul al-fiqh. The author of the original matn (Al-Tawdih) suggested, in his work Tawassul ila al-Fiqh, that the concept of tawassul (a means to acquire fiqh) could apply to both the mujtahid and the muqallid. The commentator (from Al-Talwih) objects, saying this is far-fetched because no scholar has endorsed such a generalization. The apologist, however, defends the author by noting that the author himself presented this only as a second, less apparent probability, which is not objectionable. The second part addresses why usul works discuss taqlid if it is not part of the science: the answer is that these discussions occur in contrast to ijtihad, not as integral topics of usul. This reflects the Hanafi approach of maintaining the boundaries of the discipline while still addressing related issues for completeness.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlid): Following a mujtahid in legal rulings without knowing the evidence.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Independent legal reasoning within the principles of the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do usul al-fiqh books discuss matters of taqlid according to the passage?
A) Because taqlid is a core subject of usul.
B) Because the author made a mistake in including them.
C) In contrast to ijtihad, not as topics of the science itself.
D) Only in later Hanafi works, not in early ones.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul works include taqlid discussions only as a contrast to ijtihad, not as a core subject—this maintains disciplinary boundaries while providing conceptual clarity.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Basis for Distinguishing Sciences: Subject vs Essential Attributes
Analyzing the debate on the basis of distinguishing sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi argument that sciences can be distinguished by their essential attributes (predicates) and critique the opposing view that only the subject matter suffices.

Core Idea
Essential attributes can distinguish sciences even when the subject is shared.

In the classification of sciences, a key debate arises: should disciplines be distinguished by their subject matter or by the essential attributes they investigate? The author of our passage argues that predicates (essential accidents) can serve as a basis for differentiation, while the commentator insists on the primacy of the subject. This lesson unpacks that dispute, examining the proof structures and the epistemological status of subject versus predicate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
What exactly are the two positions? (Distinction of sciences: by subject only or also by predicates?)
2
State the Hanafi position (author)
The author holds that difference in predicates (essential accidents) can distinguish sciences even if subject is same.
3
Analyze the opposing argument
The commentator invokes philosophers' practice (one subject = one science) and the claim that subject is known while predicates are unknown.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The author rebuts by showing that essential accidents are known in themselves, and both subject and predicate have unknown details.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: whether two disciplines studying the same entity (e.g., man can be subject of both physics and metaphysics) remain distinct based on the attributes they discuss.

Source Text

فن طبعی میں زیر بحث لائی جاتی ہے تو مصنف کے نزدیک یہ حیثیت بیان اعراض کے لئے ہے اور شارح کے نزدیک قید للعروض ہے کما صرح به القوم وابن سينا - وههنا نظر اما اولاً الم شارح نے مصنف پر اعتراضات حسب عادت شروع کر دئیے ہیں اولا یہ کہ مصنف کا امتیاز بين العلمين با وجود وحدت موضوع اختلاف محمولات پر مبنی کرنا یہ اس پر مبنی ہے جو مصنف نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ حیثیت کبھی جزء موضوع ہوئی جو زیر بحث نہیں لائی جاتی اور کبھی اعراض ذاتیہ مبحوثہ کا بیان ہوتی ہے اسی حیثیت کو بیانیہ بنانے کی وجہ سے اعراض مبحوثہ فی الفین مختلف بحسب النوع ہوکر اختلاف محمولات اور اختلاف مسائل کی وجہ بنا کر اختلاف علمین کا باعث قرار دیا گیا ہے وقد عرفت مانیہ یعنی اس میں ایک تو مصنف پر یہ الزام دیا تھا کہ تشارک علمين في موضوع واحد لازم آجاتا ہے اور حالانکہ یہ امر کوئی باعث اشکال نہیں ہے جب کہ ان علمین کے مابین حیثیت بیانیہ اور اختلاف معمول کی وجہ سے امتیاز قائم ہے پھر شارح نے جو قید للموضوعیہ بنائی تھی اس پر اشکال کے جواب میں جو تکلف اختیار کیا تھا وہ بھی آپ کو معلوم ہو چکا ہے داما ثانیا خلاصہ اس اعتراض کا یہ ہے کہ اہل حکمت نے جب اعیان موجودات یعنی موجودات خارجیہ کے احوال معلوم کرنے کی قصد کی تو ان حقائق کے کچھ انواع اور اجناس مقرر کئے اور ان کے اعراض ذاتیہ کا جہاں تک وہ علمی حیثیت سے احاطہ کر سکے بحث کی فحصلت لهم مسائل كثيرة تو اس صورت میں ان کے لئے مسائل کثیرہ حاصل ہوئے جو اس بارہ میں متحد تھے کہ ایک ہی موضوع کے احوال کی بحث ہے اگر چہ ان کے محمول مختلف تھے اسی وحدۃ موضوع کے اعتبار سے اس کو علم واحد قرار دے کر اس کی تدوین اور تسمیہ میں منفرد قرار دیا وجوز و الکل واحد پھر ہر ایک کے لئے جائز قرار دیا کہ اس موضوع کے جتنا احوال پر مطلع ہوں اس کے ساتھ اضافہ کرتے چلے جائیں خان المعتبر فی العلم کیونکہ ہر علم کے اندر یہ معتبر ہوتا ہے کہ اس علم کے موضوع کے جتنا عوارض ذاتیہ جہاں تک طاقہ انسانیہ محیط ہو سکتی ہے ان جمیع سے بحث کی جائے اس لئے ہر ایک کو اجازت ہوتی ہے کہ جتنا احوال پر اطلاع حاصل ہوتی جائے ان کا اس علم میں وہ اضافہ کرتا چلا جائے۔ فلا معنی للعلم الواحد اب علم واحد کا مفہوم و معنی اس کے سوا اور کچھ نہیں ہے کہ کسی ایک شئی کو یا چند اشیاء متناسبہ کو بطور موضوع کے متعین کر لیا جائے اور ان کے جتنے اعراض ذاتیہ ہو سکتے ہیں تمام کی بحث کی جائے اور تمام کو طلب اور تلاش کر لیا جائے ۔
ولا معنی تمایز العلوم الخ اور تمایز علوم کا معنی ہی یہی ہے کہ ایک علیم ایک مخصوص شتی کے احوال و اعراض میں نگاہ رکھتا ہے اور دوسرا علم دوسری مخصوص شئی کے احوال میں اور ان دو اشیا جن کے احوال علمین کی نظر میں میں ان کے اندر ضروری ہے کہ ایک دوسرے کے ساتھ یا تو مغایر بالذات ہوں یا بالا عتبار بان يوخد فى احد العلمين مطلقاً یہ مغایر باعتبار ہونے کی صورتیں ہیں یعنی ایک علم میں وہ شئی ماخود بالاطلاق ہو اور دوسرے میں مقید بالقید ہو یا ہر ایک میں الگ الگ قید کے ساتھ مقید ہو اور یہی موضوع ہے جو موجب امتیاز ہے۔ و تلك الاحوال وہ احوال و اعراض جو مسئلہ میں محمول بنتے وہ تو امور مجہولہ ہوتے میں جن کی طلب ہوتی ہے بخلاف موضوع کے کہ یہ معلوم اور بین الوجود ہوتا یہی امر معلوم ہی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے کہ سبب امتیاز ہو نہ وہ احوال مجہولہ مطلوبہ جن کو مصنف نے موجب امتیاز قرار دیا ہے ۔ شارح کی جانب سے یہ تمام تطویل بلا طائل ہے حاصل اس کا یہ ہے کہ موضوع ایک ذات ہوتی ہے جس کے لئے اثبات صفات مطلوب ہوتا ہے تو اسی کو سبب امتیاز ہونا چاہئے اگر شارح کی مراد یہ ہے امتیاز علوم بالموضوعات اولی اور انسب ہے تو پھر یہ بات مسلم ہے لیکن یہ اس کی متقاضی نہیں ہے کہ باعتبار اعراض کے جو صفات محمولہ ہوتی ہیں موجب امتیاز نہ ہو سکیں بلکہ تمایز صفات کے ساتھ بھی امتیازہ قائم رہ سکتا ہے اگر اس کی مراد یہ ہے کہ امتیاز صرف تمایز موضوعات کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے تو یہی دعوی ہے جو کہ عین نزاع ہے پھر اس کا اعادہ مفید مطلوب نہیں ہو سکتا۔ باقی رہی یہ بات کہ موضوع معلوم ہے اور احوال اعراض مجہول میں موجب امتیاز امر معلوم ہو سکتا ہے نہ کہ مجہول اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ نفس محمول جو کہ عرض ذاتی ہے وہ بھی موضوع جیسا معلوم ہے البتہ عرض ذاتی کی تفاصیل جو منتسب الى الموضوع ہوتی ہیں یہ مجہول ہیں اور عرض ذاتی فی حد دانہ مجہول نہیں ہے لہذا یہ موجب امتیازہ ہو سکتا ہے اور اسی طرح تو تفاصیل موضوع بھی بحیثیت مثبت لہا ہونے کے مجہول ہیں کیونکہ موضوع مسائل صرف موضوع فن نہیں ہوتا بلکہ موضوع فن کے انواع اور اعراض ذاتیہ اور اعراض ذاتیہ کے انواع بھی موضوع مسائل ہو سکتے ہیں تو جیسے تفاصیل محمول مجہول ہیں اسی طرح تفاصیل موضوع بھی مجہول ہیں اگر یہ جہالت امتیاز کے منافی ہے تو یہ موضوع و محمول دونوں میں برابر درجے کی موجود ہے پھر موضوع بھی موجب امتیاز نہیں
In natural science, when it is discussed, according to the author this consideration (haythiyya) is for expressing accidents, and according to the commentator it is a restriction for the subject-matter, as stated by the people and Ibn Sina. And here there is a consideration: firstly, the commentator has started objections as usual. Firstly, that the author's distinction between the two sciences despite unity of subject is based on difference of predicates. This is based on what the author mentioned: that consideration is sometimes a part of the subject that is not discussed, and sometimes it is an expression of the essential accidents under discussion. Because this consideration is made expressive, the essential accidents under discussion in the two disciplines differ in type, becoming a cause for difference of predicates and difference of issues, making it a cause for difference of the two sciences. And you have known its meaning: that in this, one charge against the author was that it necessitates the sharing of two sciences in one subject, while this matter is not a cause for difficulty since the distinction between the two sciences is established through the expressive consideration and difference of usual [matters]. Then the commentator made the restriction for the subject-matter, and the effort he made in answering the objection is known to you. Secondly, the summary of this objection is that when the philosophers intended to know the states of external existents, they determined some species and genera of those realities and discussed their essential accidents as far as they could encompass scientifically, so they obtained many issues which were united in that they were a discussion of the states of one subject, although their predicates were different. Due to this unity of subject, they made it a single science, singling it out in its codification and naming, and they allowed each one to add as many states of that subject as they become acquainted with, because the accepted [practice] in science is that all essential accidents of the subject of that science are discussed as far as human power can encompass. Therefore each is permitted to add to that science whatever information about states they obtain. So the meaning of a single science is nothing other than to determine one thing or several proportionate things as subject, and to discuss all their possible essential accidents and to seek and search for all of them. And there is no meaning for the distinction of sciences except that one science looks at the states and accidents of a specific thing and another science looks at the states and accidents of another specific thing, and these two things whose states are in the view of the sciences must be either different in essence or in consideration, such that they are taken in one science absolutely and in another restricted by a restriction, or each restricted by a different restriction, and this is the subject which is the cause of distinction. And those states and accidents which become predicates in the issue are unknown matters that are sought, unlike the subject which is known and obvious in existence. This known matter alone has the capacity to be the cause of distinction, not those unknown sought-after states which the author made the cause of distinction. All this elaboration from the commentator is without benefit. The gist of it is that the subject is an essence for which the affirmation of attributes is sought, so it should be the cause of distinction. If the commentator means that distinguishing sciences by subjects is primary and more appropriate, then this is conceded, but it does not require that attributes which are predicates cannot be causes of distinction. Rather, distinction can be established through distinction of attributes as well. If he means that distinction only occurs through distinction of subjects, then this is the very claim which is the point of contention; repeating it cannot benefit the sought. As for the remaining point that the subject is known and the states/accidents are unknown, and the cause of distinction must be known, not unknown, the answer is that the predicate itself, which is an essential accident, is also known like the subject; only the details of the essential accident which are attributed to the subject are unknown, and the essential accident per se is not unknown. Therefore it can be a cause of distinction. Similarly, the details of the subject are also unknown in terms of being affirmed to it, because the subject of the issues is not merely the subject of the discipline, but the species of the subject of the discipline and the essential accidents and the species of essential accidents can also be subjects of issues. So just as the details of the predicate are unknown, likewise the details of the subject are unknown. If ignorance is contrary to distinction, then it exists equally in both subject and predicate, so the subject too would not be a cause of distinction.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a detailed debate between the author (musannif) and the commentator (sharh) on the criterion for distinguishing one science from another. The author holds that sciences can be distinguished by their predicates (mahsulat) or essential attributes (arad dhatiyya), even if they share the same subject. The commentator objects, arguing that distinction must be based on the subject matter (mawdu') itself, not on predicates. The commentator invokes the practice of philosophers (ahl al-hikmah) who studied external existents, classified them into genera and species, and discussed their essential attributes as a single science due to unity of subject. The commentator also argues that the subject is known while the predicates (the essential accidents) are unknown and sought after, so only the known subject can serve as the basis of distinction. The author refutes this by pointing out that the essential accident itself is known (only its details unknown) and that the subject also has unknown details. Therefore, both subject and predicate can be used to distinguish sciences. The passage shows the Hanafi usul methodology of analyzing the structure of sciences and the criteria for classification.

Key Terms
موضوع (mawḍūʿ): The subject matter of a science; the thing whose essential attributes are studied
عرض ذاتی (ʿaraḍ dhātī): An essential accident that is attributable to the subject and studied in a science
محمول (maḥmūl): Predicate; what is affirmed or denied of the subject in a proposition
حیثیت بیانیہ (haythiyya bayāniyya): An expressive consideration that highlights the essential accidents of the subject
حیثیت تقیدیہ (haythiyya taqyīdiyya): A restrictive consideration that specifies the subject under a certain condition

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author (musannif) in this passage, what can be the basis for distinguishing two sciences even if they share the same subject?
A) The different predicates (essential accidents) discussed
B) The different geographical origins of the scholars
C) The different languages used
D) The different time periods of study

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defends the view that sciences can be distinguished not only by their subject matter but also by the essential attributes (predicates) they investigate, as both share an epistemological status of being known in themselves.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi Position on Basmala: Tabarruk, Takfir, and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Expansion of the Hanafi view on Basmala, covering recitation, takfir, and the dispute with Shafi'is.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that scholarly disagreement (shubha) prevents takfir, and explain why the Basmala is considered a single repeated verse according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Scholarly disagreement creates doubt (shubha) that prevents takfir, even when a text's Quranicity is accepted within one school.

The Basmala (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) at the beginning of surahs raises three interconnected issues: permissibility of recitation by one in a state of impurity, whether denying its Quranicity warrants takfir, and the exact nature of the Basmala as a verse. This lesson unpacks each issue through the lens of Hanafi usul al-fiqh, focusing on the role of shubha in preventing takfir and the methodological disagreement between Hanafis and Shafi'is.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish intentions for recitation
Recognize that reciting the Basmala with the intention of tabarruk (seeking blessing) is permissible even for a menstruating woman or one in janabah, whereas recitation with the intention of tilawah (Quranic recitation) is prohibited. The same distinction applies to other phrases like 'Alhamdulillah' when said with the intention of thanks.
This shows that the legal ruling depends on intention (niyyah), a key principle in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Analyze why denial of Basmala's Quranicity does not lead to takfir
Unlike the Basmala in Surah An-Naml (which is unequivocally part of a verse), the Basmala at the beginnings of surahs is subject to scholarly disagreement (ikhtilaf) between Hanafis and Shafi'is. This disagreement creates doubt (shubha) about its status as part of the Quran. In Hanafi usul, shubha derived from valid ikhtilaf prevents takfir, because takfir requires certainty (yaqin) about the denial of a necessarily known part of religion.
The presence of shubha is a legal barrier to takfir, as established in Hanafi legal theory.
3
Trace the Hanafi-Shafi‘i dispute over Basmala verses
The Shafi‘i school holds that the Basmala is a separate verse at the beginning of every surah except Surah Bara'ah, resulting in 113 Basmala verses. The Hanafi school holds that the Basmala is a single verse revealed for the purpose of separation between surahs and for blessing; its repetition at the beginning of each surah is for that purpose, not as a verse of that surah.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is the count of Quranic verses: 113 for Shafi‘is vs. 1 for Hanafis.
4
Note the uniqueness of Basmala repetition
The text emphasizes that this repetition applies exclusively to the Basmala; repeating any other verse (e.g., 'Alhamdulillah Rabbil Alameen') at the beginning of each surah with the intention of blessing is prohibited and would be considered heretical. This highlights that the Basmala has a special status based on revelation and transmission from the Salaf.
This is a further argument that the Basmala is not a normal verse; it was revealed specifically for separation and blessing.

Source Text

اس کی تلاوت جائز ہے حالانکہ قران مجید کی تلاوت حائض اور جنب کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے تو اس کا جواب دیا انما هو على قصد التيمن والتبرك جائز ہے لاعلی قصد التلاوۃ جیسے الحمد لله رب العلمین علی قصد الشکر جنب و حائض کے لئے جائز ہے اور علی قصد التلاوہ ناجائز ہے ۔ وعدم تکفیر یہ تیسرا مسئلہ ہے کہ اگر تسمیہ جزء من القرآن ہے تو جو اس کے قران ہونے کا انکار کرے اس کی تکفیر کیوں نہیں کی جاتی حالانکہ سورہ نمل کے اندر جو لسیم الرحمن الرحیم آیت کا بعض ہے اس کے منکر قران ہونے کی تکفیر کی جاتی ہے تو جواب دیا کہ تسمیہ جو اوائل سور میں ہے اس کی قرانیہ میں شبہ ہے اور آئمہ کا اس میں اختلاف ہے جس نے اس شیعہ کو قومی کر دیا ہے جس کی وجہ سے اس کی قرانیہ مقام وضوح سے نکل کر حیر ز اشکال داشتباہ میں پہونچ چکی ہے اور اس جیسا شبہ مانع عن التکفیر ہوتا ہے ۔ خان قیل خلاصہ سوال یہ ہے کہ متأخرین حنفیہ کے حسب مختار کہ تسمیہ جزء قرآن ہے کیا اس کے باوجود فریقین میں یعنی احناف اور شوافع کے مابین اختلاف باقی رہیگا یا کہ نہیں ۔ قلنا نعم ہاں اختلاف باقی ہے کیونکہ تسمیہ شوافع کے نزدیک ہر سورۃ کی جز اور ایک آیت چونکہ قرآن مجید کی کل سورۃ ایک سو چودہ ہیں اور سورۃ براۃ کی شروع میں تسمیہ نہیں ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک قرآن مجید کی یہ ایک سو تیرہ آیات ہیں جیسے فیاستی آلاء ربکما تکذبان سورة الرحمن کی متعدد آیات ہیں اور عند الحنفیہ قرآن مجید کی یہ صرف ایک آیت ہے اس کا تکرار اوائل سور میں صرف فصل بین السور اور تبرک کی خاطر ہے اور یہ کسی سورۃ کی آیت نہیں ہے اور اس کا تکرار اوائل سور میں اس لئے جائز ہے کہ اس کا نزول اسی خاطر ہے اور سلف سے ایسے منقول ہے۔ بخلاف من اخذ الخ یعنی تسمیہ کے علاوہ بقصد تبرک وغیرہ کسی اور آیت کا تکرار اوائل سور میں جائز نہیں مثلاً کوئی ہر سورۃ کے اول میں بقصد تیرک الحمد الله رب العلمین لکھنا شروع کر دے یہ قطعا جائز نہیں ایسے شخص کو زندیق یا مجنون شمار کیا جائیگا۔
Its recitation is permissible, although recitation of the Noble Quran is not permissible for a menstruating woman or one in major impurity. So the answer was given: it is permissible with the intention of seeking blessing and benediction, not with the intention of recitation. Similarly, 'Alhamdulillah Rabbil Alameen' with the intention of thanks is permissible for menstruating and impure, but with intention of recitation it is not permissible. And the non-declaration of disbelief: this is the third issue: if the Basmala is part of the Quran, then why is the one who denies its being Quran not declared a disbeliever, whereas in Surah An-Naml, 'Bismillahir Rahmanir Rahim' is part of the verse; the one who denies its being Quran is declared a disbeliever? So the answer was given: there is doubt about the Quranicity of the Basmala that is at the beginnings of surahs, and the imams have differed on it, which has made this matter doubtful, due to which its Quranicity has left the level of clarity and reached the level of bewilderment and doubt. And such a doubt prevents takfir. If it is said, the summary of the question is: according to the preferred view of the later Hanafis that the Basmala is part of the Quran, will the disagreement between the two parties, the Hanafis and the Shafi'is, remain or not? We said yes, the disagreement remains. Because the Basmala according to the Shafi'is is part of every surah and one verse. Since the total surahs of the Noble Quran are one hundred and fourteen, and at the beginning of Surah Bara'ah there is no Basmala, therefore according to them these are one hundred and thirteen verses of the Noble Quran. Like 'Fa-bi-ayyi ala' i Rabbikuma tukadhdhiban' of Surah Ar-Rahman are multiple verses. And according to the Hanafis, this is only one verse of the Noble Quran. Its repetition at the beginnings of surahs is only for separation between surahs and for blessing, and it is not a verse of any surah. And its repetition at the beginnings of surahs is permissible because its revelation was for this purpose, and it is so transmitted from the Salaf. Contrary to others, i.e., besides the Basmala, repetition of any other verse at the beginnings of surahs with the intention of blessing etc. is not permissible. For example, if someone at the beginning of every surah, with the intention of blessing, starts writing 'Alhamdulillah Rabbil Alameen', this is absolutely not permissible. Such a person will be considered a heretic or insane.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the legal issues surrounding the Basmala. It addresses three interconnected matters: first, the permissibility of reciting the Basmala with the intention of tabarruk (seeking blessing) by a menstruating woman or one in janabah, as opposed to reciting it with the intention of tilawah (Quranic recitation), which is prohibited. The example of saying 'Alhamdulillah' with the intention of thanks is given as analogous. Second, the issue of takfir (declaring someone a disbeliever) for denying that the Basmala is part of the Quran. The text explains that unlike the Basmala in Surah An-Naml (which is undeniably part of a verse), the Basmala at the beginnings of surahs is subject to scholarly disagreement, creating doubt (shubha) that prevents takfir. Third, the ongoing disagreement between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the number of Basmala verses. The Shafi'is consider the Basmala a separate verse at the beginning of each surah (except Surah Bara'ah), resulting in 113 Basmala verses. The Hanafis hold that it is a single verse revealed for the purpose of separating surahs and seeking blessing, repeated at the beginning of each surah but not belonging to any surah. The passage concludes by emphasizing that this repetition is unique to the Basmala; any other verse cannot be repeated similarly, and doing so would be deemed heretical or insane behavior. The commentary follows the author's sequence, explaining each ruling and its underlying reasoning within the Hanafi school, while acknowledging the opposing view.

Key Terms
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The phrase 'Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim' placed at the beginning of surahs.
تکفیر (takfir): The act of declaring a Muslim a disbeliever (kafir) due to denial of a necessarily known part of religion.
شبہ (shubha): Uncertainty or doubt that arises from disagreement among authoritative scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle explained in the passage, what prevents takfir for someone who denies that the Basmala at the beginning of surahs is part of the Quran?
A) The fact that the Basmala is not actually part of the Quran.
B) The existence of ikhtilaf among scholars, which creates shubha.
C) The person's sincere intention that his denial is based on ijtihad.
D) The Hanafi school's minority position that it is not part of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Scholarly disagreement (ikhtilaf) on a matter creates sufficient doubt (shubha) to prevent takfir, as in the case of the Basmala's Quranic status.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Resolving the Objection of Combining Real and Metaphorical Meanings
Analyzing the objection of jama' bayn al-haqiqah wal-majaz and its Hanafi resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the usul objection of combining real and metaphorical meanings (jama' bayn al-haqiqah wal-majaz) and explain how Hanafi scholars resolve it by distinguishing between explicit textual indication (ibarat al-nass) and implicit indication (dilalat al-nass).

Core Idea
Combining real and metaphorical meanings is prohibited only when both are taken from the same perspective; different textual indications allow separate treatment.

This lesson introduces a key usul al-fiqh objection against the permissibility of reciting the Quran in Persian during prayer. The opponent argues that allowing Persian recitation forces the word 'Quran' to carry both a real meaning (Arabic wording) and a metaphorical meaning (Persian translation) simultaneously — which is prohibited in usul. We will examine the Hanafi responses that distinguish between explicit and implicit textual references.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
State the claim that allowing Persian recitation necessitates jama' bayn al-haqiqah wal-majaz because 'Quran' is used in both its real sense (Arabic) and metaphorical sense (non-Arabic) at once.
This is the starting point of the dispute.
2
Follow the first response
The real meaning is taken from the explicit text (nass) and the metaphorical from analogy (qiyas), so they come from different legal sources and no prohibited combination occurs.
Qiyas is a separate method of derivation.
3
Follow the second response
The real meaning is taken via explicit indication (ibarat al-nass) and the metaphorical via implicit indication (dilalat al-nass), thus from different perspectives.
This is the most detailed Hanafi reply.
4
Note the third response
The word 'Quran' is used in a general metaphorical sense (am al-majaz) meaning any indicative wording, whether Arabic or not, so there is no duality of meaning.
This avoids the jama' issue entirely.
5
Understand the usul principle
Jama' bayn al-haqiqah wal-majaz is only forbidden when both meanings are intended from a single perspective. Here, the perspectives are distinct.
This principle is specific to Hanafi usul.

Source Text

مراد میں جمع بین الحقیقة والمجاز لازم آجائیگی لان القران حقيقة الم یعنی نظم عربی پر قرآن کا اطلاق علی سبیل الحقیقہ ہے اور غیر عربی پر علی سبیل المجاز تو جب اپنے نظم عربی کے ساتھ نظم فارسی کو بھی قرآة قران کے فریضہ میں جائز قرار دے دیا تو لفظ قرآن سے حقیقی اور مجازی دونوں معنی بیک وقت مراد ہوئے ۔ بذا جمع بین الحقیقة والمجاز فی اطلاق واحد وزال يجوز قلنا ممنوع خلاصہ جواب یہ کہ جمع بین الحقیقة والمجاز کا لازم آنا ممنوع ہے یہ تب آتا کہ دونوں معافی من جهة واحدة معتبر ہوتے بلکہ یہاں نص میں قرآن سے صرف حقیقی معنی معتبر ہے اور مجازی معنی منصوصا نہیں بلکہ قیاسا مراد ہے یا حقیقت بطریق عبارة النص اور مجاز بطریق ولالہ النص مراد ہے لہذا الگ الگ اعتبار ہیں لہذا جمع لازم نہیں آتی یا یہ جواب بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ لفظ قرآن سے عموم المجاز مراد ہے یعنی النظم الدال مطلقا اسی سوارکان غربیا او غيره في فلا يلزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز - قوله بغير العربية یہ اشارہ ہے کہ جواز صلوۃ کے بارہ میں صرف نظم فارسی کی خصوصیت نہیں بلکہ عربی کے علاوہ خواہ فارسی ہو یا غیر فارسی سب برابر درجہ میں جائز ہیں ۔ قیل بعض حضرات کے نزدیک یہ خلاف صرف فارسی کے متعلق ہے غیر فارسی کے متعلق نہیں ہے بلکہ غیر فارسی کے اور عجمی السنتہ کے ساتھ قراۃ قرآن نماز میں جائزہ نہیں ہے لان الفارسية قريبة من العربيه في الفصاحة وقيل لانها لسان اهل الجنة كالعربية
قوله ولو قرأ آية اشارة اس میں ادھر اشارہ ہے کہ جنب اور حائض کے لئے قرآة بالفارسیہ پر مداومتہ کرنا اور اس کی عادت بنا لینا جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ مظہر کے لئے بھی مداومتہ اور اعتیاد جائز نہیں ہے لان فيه اخلا لا بتعظیم القرآن فان قبل المتاخرون منشاء سوال لفظ خاصہ ہے خلاصہ سوال یہ کہ متاخرین فقہا تو اس پر متفق ہیں کہ قرآة فارسیہ کی وجہ سے سجدہ تلاوت لازم ہو جائیگا اور جو قرآن فارسی کسان میں لکھا ہوا ہے غیر منتظر کے لئے اس کا نفس کرنا جائز نہیں ہے تو ان مسائل میں بھی نظم عربی و غیر لازم قرار دیا گیا ہے بلکہ یہ احکام معنی مجرد پر وارد کئے گئے ہیں لہذا یہ قول لم يجعل النظم ركناً لا زمانی حق جواز الصلوة خاصة کیسے صحیح ہوگا۔ قلنا خلاصہ جواب یہ کہ مصنف اپنے قول خاصہ کی بنامہ رائے متقدمین پر مبنی کی ہے۔ متقدمین میں سے مسائل مذکورہ کے متعلق کوئی نص موجود نہیں البتہ متاخرین نے بنابر احتیاط ان مسائل مذکورہ میں رائے مذکورہ کو اختیار کیا ہے کیونکہ رکن مقصورہ یعنی معنی چونکہ قائم اور موجود ہے اس لئے احتیاطاً اس پر احکام قرآن مترتب کر دئیے ۔ قوله لكن الاصح لیکن اصح اور زیادہ صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ امام نے اس میں رجوع الی قول الصاحبین کیا ہے یعنی قرآة القرآن بغیر العربیہ نماز کے جواز کے لئے کافی نہیں ہے یہی وایت کیا ہے نوح بن مریم ابو عصمہ قاضی المروني . قال فخر الاسلام لان ما قالہ یہ وجہ رجوع کا بیان ہے استدلال علی الرجوع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر رجوع ثابت بالروایت ہے تو پھر استدلال کی ضرورت نہیں ہے رجوع ثابت نہیں ہے تو یہ استدلال مفید مقصود نہیں ہے کیونکہ قران مجید کی وصف جیسے منزل عربی کے ساتھ ہے ایسے غیر عربی کے ساتھ کیگئی ہے جیسے انه لفی تو بر الاولین تو زبر اول میں اس کا وجود ثابت ہو رہا ہے یہ عربی لسان میں نہ تھا بلکہ غیر عربی میں تھا تو معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قرآن کا اطلاق غیر عربی پر بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ وقال ابو الیسر ابوالیسر فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ مسئلہ بڑا مشکل ہے اور خارج از فہم کیونکہ ابو حنیفہ کا یہ قول کسی کے لئے واضح نہیں ہو سکتا۔ کرخی نے اس مسئلہ میں ایک تصنیف طویل لکھی ہے لیکن دلیل شافی اس میں بھی نہیں ہے۔
The intended meaning: Combining real and metaphorical meanings becomes necessary because the Quran is literally applied to Arabic wording, and metaphorically to non-Arabic wording. So when Persian wording is also permitted as Quran recitation in the obligation of prayer alongside Arabic wording, then the word 'Quran' is intended to have both real and metaphorical meanings at once. Hence, combining real and metaphorical meanings in a single usage occurs, and it is not permissible. We say: This is not allowed. Summary of answer: The occurrence of combining real and metaphorical meanings is prevented. It would occur if both meanings were considered from one perspective. Rather, here in the text, only the real meaning is intended from 'Quran', and the metaphorical meaning is not intended from the text but rather by analogy (qiyas). Or the real meaning is taken by the explicit wording (ibarat al-nass) and the metaphorical by indication (dilalat al-nass). So they are separate considerations, thus combination does not necessarily occur. Or it can be answered that from the word 'Quran' a general metaphorical meaning is intended, i.e., the absolute indicative wording, whether Arabic or other, so combination is not necessary. And his statement: 'in non-Arabic' indicates that the permissibility of prayer is not specific to Persian wording; rather, besides Arabic, whether Persian or non-Persian, all are equally permitted. Some said that this disagreement is only about Persian, not about other non-Arabic languages; rather, reciting Quran in prayer in non-Arabic and other non-Arab tongues is not permissible, because Persian is close to Arabic in eloquence, and it is said because it is the language of the people of Paradise like Arabic. And his statement: 'even if he recites a verse' – there is an indication that for a person in major impurity (junub) and a menstruating woman, continuous recitation in Persian and making it a habit is not permissible, nor is it permissible for others to do so continuously and habitually, because it involves disrespect to the Quran. If it is said: The later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) are agreed that reciting in Persian necessitates prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah), and that touching a Persian Quran is not permissible for one in major impurity. So in these issues, the non-Arabic wording is considered effective, rather these rulings are applied to the mere meaning. Therefore how can the statement 'he did not make the wording a pillar (rukn) except for the permissibility of prayer' be correct? We say: Summary of answer: The author based his statement on the opinion of the early scholars. There is no explicit text from the early scholars regarding these issues; rather, the later scholars adopted these rulings out of caution because the essential pillar (al-rukn al-maqsurah) i.e., the meaning, is established and present, so out of caution they applied the rulings of the Quran to it. But the more correct view (al-ashah) is that the Imam reverted to the opinion of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), i.e., reciting the Quran in non-Arabic is not sufficient for the validity of prayer. This is narrated by Nu'aym ibn Maryam, Abu 'Ismah, Qadi al-Marwazi. Fakhr al-Islam said that this (the statement of the author) is an explanation of the reason for the reversion, not a proof for the reversion. Because if the reversion is established by narration, then there is no need for proof; if it is not established, then this proof does not serve the purpose. Because the description of the Quran, just as it is revealed in Arabic, is also made in non-Arabic, as in the verse 'Indeed it is in the scriptures of the former ones', so its existence is proven in the former scriptures, which were not in the Arabic tongue but in non-Arabic. Thus it appears that the word 'Quran' can be applied to non-Arabic as well. And Abu al-Yusr said: This issue is very difficult and beyond comprehension, because Abu Hanifa's statement cannot be made clear to anyone. Al-Karkhi wrote a long treatise on this issue, but it does not contain a convincing proof.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
Passage type: A usul dispute (ikhtilaf) concerning the application of the principle of combining real and metaphorical meanings (jama' bayn al-haqiqah wal-majaz) to the case of reciting the Quran in Persian during prayer. The commentator first presents an objection: if one allows reciting the Quran in Persian, the word 'Quran' would have to be used simultaneously in its real sense (Arabic wording) and metaphorical sense (Persian translation), which is not permitted in usul. The commentator then provides several responses: (1) The real meaning is taken from the explicit text (nass) and the metaphorical from qiyas or from implicit indication (dilalah), so they are from different perspectives; (2) The word 'Quran' is used in a general metaphorical sense meaning 'indicative wording' absolutely. The text then clarifies that the permission includes all non-Arabic languages, though there is a view that it is specific to Persian due to its eloquence or because it is the language of Paradise. Next, a ruling: continuous recitation in Persian by a junub or menstruating woman is impermissible because it disrespects the Quran. Then, an objection from later scholars: if reciting in Persian necessitates sajdat al-tilawah and touching a Persian Quran is prohibited for the impure, this shows that non-Arabic wording is treated as Quran, contradicting the author's claim that wording is not a pillar except for prayer validity. The response: The early scholars had no explicit text on these secondary issues; later scholars applied these rulings out of caution because the meaning (the true pillar) is present. Finally, the correct view (al-asah) is that Imam Abu Hanifa reverted to the opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, i.e., reciting in non-Arabic is not sufficient. Fakhr al-Islam notes that this reversion is based on narration, not reasoning. The verse 'Innahu lafi zuburi al-awwaleen' is cited to show that the Quran was in non-Arabic scriptures. Abu al-Yusr declares the issue extremely difficult. The commentator follows the order of the matn, addressing each point sequentially with legal and usul reasoning.

Key Terms
الحقیقة والمجاز (al-haqiqah wal-majaz): Real and metaphorical meanings: haqiqah is the literal meaning for which the word was originally coined; majaz is the figurative meaning used for something related due to a connection.
عبارة النص (ibarat al-nass): The explicit wording of the text, directly indicating the intended meaning.
دلالة النص (dilalat al-nass): Implicit indication of the text; the meaning is understood from the context or implication, not from the explicit wording.
نص (nass): The explicit wording of a text (here, the Quranic verse or authoritative statement).
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical deduction: extending a ruling from a foundational text to a new case due to a shared effective cause ('illah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle discussed in this passage, why is combining the real and metaphorical meanings (jama' bayn al-haqiqah wal-majaz) not required when reciting Quran in Persian during prayer?
A) Because the word 'Quran' is only used in its real meaning, and the Persian recitation is not considered Quran.
B) Because the real meaning is taken from the explicit text (ibarah) and the metaphorical from its indication (dilalah), thus they are from different perspectives.
C) Because the Persian recitation is considered the same as Arabic recitation, so there is no duality.
D) Because the principle of jama' bayn al-haqiqah wal-majaz is only applicable to attributes, not to words.

Key Takeaway
Jama' bayn al-haqiqah wal-majaz is not an issue when the two meanings are derived from different types of textual indication.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Ruling on Reciting Quran in Persian During Prayer
Analyzing the substantive ruling on reciting Quran in Persian during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the different Hanafi positions on reciting Quran in Persian during prayer and explain why the final mufta bihi position is that it is not sufficient.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa initially permitted Persian recitation, but the established position is that only Arabic is valid in prayer.

This lesson examines the substantive legal dispute within the Hanafi school about reciting the Quran in Persian (or any non-Arabic language) during prayer. The passage traces Abu Hanifa's original view, his alleged reversion (ruju') to the opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and the later scholars' practical rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify Abu Hanifa's original position
Abu Hanifa permitted reciting the Quran in Persian during prayer, holding that the meaning is the essence.
This is based on the idea that the Quran's purpose is to convey meaning.
2
Note the reversion (ruju')
Abu Hanifa is reported to have reverted to the opinion of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that reciting in non-Arabic is not sufficient for prayer validity.
This reversion is narrated by Nu'aym ibn Maryam, Abu 'Ismah, Qadi al-Marwazi.
3
Examine the evidence for reversion
Fakhr al-Islam notes that the reversion is based on narration, not rational proof. The verse 'Innahu lafi zuburi al-awwaleen' is cited to show that the Quran existed in non-Arabic scriptures, supporting the application of 'Quran' to non-Arabic.
This verse is used as evidence for Abu Hanifa's original view, not for reversion.
4
Understand the later scholars' rulings
Later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) ruled that reciting in Persian necessitates sajdat al-tilawah and prohibits touching the Persian Quran for the impure. This implies that non-Arabic wording is treated as Quran for certain rulings.
These rulings were given out of caution because the meaning is present.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The more correct view (al-asah) is that Imam Abu Hanifa reverted to the opinion of the two companions, so reciting in non-Arabic is not sufficient for prayer validity.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

قوله ولو قرأ آية اشارة اس میں ادھر اشارہ ہے کہ جنب اور حائض کے لئے قرآة بالفارسیہ پر مداومتہ کرنا اور اس کی عادت بنا لینا جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ مظہر کے لئے بھی مداومتہ اور اعتیاد جائز نہیں ہے لان فيه اخلا لا بتعظیم القرآن فان قبل المتاخرون منشاء سوال لفظ خاصہ ہے خلاصہ سوال یہ کہ متاخرین فقہا تو اس پر متفق ہیں کہ قرآة فارسیہ کی وجہ سے سجدہ تلاوت لازم ہو جائیگا اور جو قرآن فارسی کسان میں لکھا ہوا ہے غیر منتظر کے لئے اس کا نفس کرنا جائز نہیں ہے تو ان مسائل میں بھی نظم عربی و غیر لازم قرار دیا گیا ہے بلکہ یہ احکام معنی مجرد پر وارد کئے گئے ہیں لہذا یہ قول لم يجعل النظم ركناً لا زمانی حق جواز الصلوة خاصة کیسے صحیح ہوگا۔ قلنا خلاصہ جواب یہ کہ مصنف اپنے قول خاصہ کی بنامہ رائے متقدمین پر مبنی کی ہے۔ متقدمین میں سے مسائل مذکورہ کے متعلق کوئی نص موجود نہیں البتہ متاخرین نے بنابر احتیاط ان مسائل مذکورہ میں رائے مذکورہ کو اختیار کیا ہے کیونکہ رکن مقصورہ یعنی معنی چونکہ قائم اور موجود ہے اس لئے احتیاطاً اس پر احکام قرآن مترتب کر دئیے ۔ قوله لكن الاصح لیکن اصح اور زیادہ صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ امام نے اس میں رجوع الی قول الصاحبین کیا ہے یعنی قرآة القرآن بغیر العربیہ نماز کے جواز کے لئے کافی نہیں ہے یہی وایت کیا ہے نوح بن مریم ابو عصمہ قاضی المروني . قال فخر الاسلام لان ما قالہ یہ وجہ رجوع کا بیان ہے استدلال علی الرجوع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر رجوع ثابت بالروایت ہے تو پھر استدلال کی ضرورت نہیں ہے رجوع ثابت نہیں ہے تو یہ استدلال مفید مقصود نہیں ہے کیونکہ قران مجید کی وصف جیسے منزل عربی کے ساتھ ہے ایسے غیر عربی کے ساتھ کیگئی ہے جیسے انه لفی تو بر الاولین تو زبر اول میں اس کا وجود ثابت ہو رہا ہے یہ عربی لسان میں نہ تھا بلکہ غیر عربی میں تھا تو معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قرآن کا اطلاق غیر عربی پر بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ وقال ابو الیسر ابوالیسر فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ مسئلہ بڑا مشکل ہے اور خارج از فہم کیونکہ ابو حنیفہ کا یہ قول کسی کے لئے واضح نہیں ہو سکتا۔ کرخی نے اس مسئلہ میں ایک تصنیف طویل لکھی ہے لیکن دلیل شافی اس میں بھی نہیں ہے۔
The intended meaning: Combining real and metaphorical meanings becomes necessary because the Quran is literally applied to Arabic wording, and metaphorically to non-Arabic wording. So when Persian wording is also permitted as Quran recitation in the obligation of prayer alongside Arabic wording, then the word 'Quran' is intended to have both real and metaphorical meanings at once. Hence, combining real and metaphorical meanings in a single usage occurs, and it is not permissible. We say: This is not allowed. Summary of answer: The occurrence of combining real and metaphorical meanings is prevented. It would occur if both meanings were considered from one perspective. Rather, here in the text, only the real meaning is intended from 'Quran', and the metaphorical meaning is not intended from the text but rather by analogy (qiyas). Or the real meaning is taken by the explicit wording (ibarat al-nass) and the metaphorical by indication (dilalat al-nass). So they are separate considerations, thus combination does not necessarily occur. Or it can be answered that from the word 'Quran' a general metaphorical meaning is intended, i.e., the absolute indicative wording, whether Arabic or other, so combination is not necessary. And his statement: 'in non-Arabic' indicates that the permissibility of prayer is not specific to Persian wording; rather, besides Arabic, whether Persian or non-Persian, all are equally permitted. Some said that this disagreement is only about Persian, not about other non-Arabic languages; rather, reciting Quran in prayer in non-Arabic and other non-Arab tongues is not permissible, because Persian is close to Arabic in eloquence, and it is said because it is the language of the people of Paradise like Arabic. And his statement: 'even if he recites a verse' – there is an indication that for a person in major impurity (junub) and a menstruating woman, continuous recitation in Persian and making it a habit is not permissible, nor is it permissible for others to do so continuously and habitually, because it involves disrespect to the Quran. If it is said: The later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) are agreed that reciting in Persian necessitates prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah), and that touching a Persian Quran is not permissible for one in major impurity. So in these issues, the non-Arabic wording is considered effective, rather these rulings are applied to the mere meaning. Therefore how can the statement 'he did not make the wording a pillar (rukn) except for the permissibility of prayer' be correct? We say: Summary of answer: The author based his statement on the opinion of the early scholars. There is no explicit text from the early scholars regarding these issues; rather, the later scholars adopted these rulings out of caution because the essential pillar (al-rukn al-maqsurah) i.e., the meaning, is established and present, so out of caution they applied the rulings of the Quran to it. But the more correct view (al-ashah) is that the Imam reverted to the opinion of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), i.e., reciting the Quran in non-Arabic is not sufficient for the validity of prayer. This is narrated by Nu'aym ibn Maryam, Abu 'Ismah, Qadi al-Marwazi. Fakhr al-Islam said that this (the statement of the author) is an explanation of the reason for the reversion, not a proof for the reversion. Because if the reversion is established by narration, then there is no need for proof; if it is not established, then this proof does not serve the purpose. Because the description of the Quran, just as it is revealed in Arabic, is also made in non-Arabic, as in the verse 'Indeed it is in the scriptures of the former ones', so its existence is proven in the former scriptures, which were not in the Arabic tongue but in non-Arabic. Thus it appears that the word 'Quran' can be applied to non-Arabic as well. And Abu al-Yusr said: This issue is very difficult and beyond comprehension, because Abu Hanifa's statement cannot be made clear to anyone. Al-Karkhi wrote a long treatise on this issue, but it does not contain a convincing proof.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
Passage type: A usul dispute (ikhtilaf) concerning the application of the principle of combining real and metaphorical meanings (jama' bayn al-haqiqah wal-majaz) to the case of reciting the Quran in Persian during prayer. The commentator first presents an objection: if one allows reciting the Quran in Persian, the word 'Quran' would have to be used simultaneously in its real sense (Arabic wording) and metaphorical sense (Persian translation), which is not permitted in usul. The commentator then provides several responses: (1) The real meaning is taken from the explicit text (nass) and the metaphorical from qiyas or from implicit indication (dilalah), so they are from different perspectives; (2) The word 'Quran' is used in a general metaphorical sense meaning 'indicative wording' absolutely. The text then clarifies that the permission includes all non-Arabic languages, though there is a view that it is specific to Persian due to its eloquence or because it is the language of Paradise. Next, a ruling: continuous recitation in Persian by a junub or menstruating woman is impermissible because it disrespects the Quran. Then, an objection from later scholars: if reciting in Persian necessitates sajdat al-tilawah and touching a Persian Quran is prohibited for the impure, this shows that non-Arabic wording is treated as Quran, contradicting the author's claim that wording is not a pillar except for prayer validity. The response: The early scholars had no explicit text on these secondary issues; later scholars applied these rulings out of caution because the meaning (the true pillar) is present. Finally, the correct view (al-asah) is that Imam Abu Hanifa reverted to the opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, i.e., reciting in non-Arabic is not sufficient. Fakhr al-Islam notes that this reversion is based on narration, not reasoning. The verse 'Innahu lafi zuburi al-awwaleen' is cited to show that the Quran was in non-Arabic scriptures. Abu al-Yusr declares the issue extremely difficult. The commentator follows the order of the matn, addressing each point sequentially with legal and usul reasoning.

Key Terms
رجوع (ruju'): Reversion; when an Imam changes his earlier opinion to a later one, often in line with other scholars.
متاخرون (muta'akhkhirun): Later scholars; those after the early generations (mutakaddimun).
احتیاط (ihtiyat): Legal caution; a method where a scholar adopts a stricter ruling to avoid potential violation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible because the meaning is the essence.
B) It is permissible only if one cannot recite Arabic.
C) It is not sufficient; the prayer is invalid.
D) It is permissible but only for Persian, not for other languages.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that reciting Quran in non-Arabic does not fulfill the obligation of qira'ah in prayer.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
