Partial Tuhr in Iddah: Hanafi Refutation of the Shafi'i Position
Refuting the Shafi'i view that partial tuhr suffices for iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that partial tuhr does not count in iddah and evaluate the reductio ad absurdum argument used against the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
If partial tuhr counted, three hours of one tuhr would fulfill iddah – an absurdity rejected by consensus.

This passage presents a classic Hanafi usul argument against the Shafi'i position that any amount of purity (tuhr) can be counted towards the iddah of a divorced woman. The Hanafi scholar uses a two-pronged attack: first, an analogy with the slave woman's iddah where fractions are ignored; second, a logical reductio showing that accepting partial tuhr leads to a conclusion unanimously rejected. Understanding this argument sharpens your ability to use qiyas and rational proof in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The core dispute: when a free woman is divorced during a period of purity (tuhr), does the iddah require three complete tuhrs (Hanafi) or can a part of the third tuhr suffice (Shafi'i)?
The Shafi'i argue that the term 'tuhr' applies to any amount, so a minimal part counts.
2
Analyze the Hanafi analogy with the slave woman
The Hanafi cites the slave woman's iddah: Shari'ah fixed it as two full menses, not one and a half, even though logically it should be half of the free woman's three menses. This shows that fractions are not recognized – a complete unit is required. Apply this to tuhr: a partial tuhr is like a fraction of a menses; it cannot count.
This is qiyas: the illa (effective cause) is the Shari'ah's disregard of fractions.
3
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
The Hanafi argues: if any amount of tuhr counts, then three hours of a single tuhr could be considered three tuhrs. After those three hours, the iddah would end and remarriage would be allowed. But this is against consensus – even the Shafi'is reject it. Therefore, the premise (partial tuhr counts) must be false.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) that a part cannot be treated as the whole.
4
Examine the alternative Hanafi answer
The text mentions another answer: if 'tuhr' means the entire interval between menses, then the tuhr in which divorce occurred is incomplete, so only two tuhrs and part of a third are counted. If 'tuhr' allows any amount, then the absurdity above follows. The Hanafi thus avoids the Shafi'i objection by defining tuhr as the complete interval.
This shows how definitional precision resolves the dispute.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: under Hanafi, a woman must wait three complete tuhrs before remarriage; under Shafi'i, she may remarry after two tuhrs and a small part of the third. The Hanafi view provides certainty and avoids the absurdity of early remarriage.
The disagreement affects the timing of iddah completion.

Source Text

نہیں ہوا کرتا دیکھئے کہ لونڈی کی عدت جو حرہ کی عدت کا نصف ہے تو اس لحاظ سے ڈیڑھ حیض ہونا چاہتے تھا لیکن شریعت نے تجزیہ نہیں کیا بلکہ فرمایا کہ عدة الامہ حیضتان تو ثانی حیض مکمل لازم کر دیا گیا ہے اس لئے صورت متنازعہ میں بھی حیض رابع کامل واجب ہو جائیگا اور اس قسم کا جواب سوافع حضرات نہیں دے سکتے کیونکہ رابع کا نہ بعض اور نہ کل کچھ بھی واجب نہیں کرتے بلکہ بعض حصہ طہر اور اس کے علاوہ دو طہر سے عدت کو ختم کر دیتے ہیں ۔ على ان بعض الطهر یہ ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے دھوان يقال خلاصہ سوال یہ ہے کہ آپ یہ کیوں کہتے ہیں انه اذا احتسب کہ جب طہر اول جس میں طلاق واقع ہوئی ہے اس کو عدت میں شمار کر لیا جائے تو پھر واجب دو طہر اور بعض حصہ طہر کا ہوا تین مکمل نہ ہوئے بلکہ اس صورت میں واجب تین ہوئے لان بعض الظهر ظہر یہ تین ہونے کی دلیل ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ بعض حصہ طہر کا بھی طہر کہلاتا ہے کیونکہ طہر ادنی ما یطلق علیہ الظہر کو کہا جاتا یعنی اونی مقدار جس پر طہر کا اطلاق ہو سکتا ہے مثلا ایک ساعتہ طہر پر طہر کا اطلاق ہو سکتا ہے لہذا اس کو طہر کہا جائے گا وہ بعض حصہ بھی طہر ہو گا لہذا تین طہر ہو گئے عدت مکمل ہو جائے گی فنقول یہ جواب ہے اس اشکال مذکور کا حاصل یہ کہ بعض طہر طہر نہیں ہو سکتا - لانه لو كان كذلك اگر ائے ہو تو پھر اول طہر اور ثالث میں فرق نہیں ہوگا فسلفی فی الثالث پھر تیسرے طہر کے بعض حصہ و ظہر قرار دیا جائے کیونکہ ادنی ما یطلق علیہ الظہر کے لحاظ سے یہ بھی طہر ہے فینبغی انه اذا معنی پھر تو لائق ہے کہ جب طہر ثالث سے کچھ تھوڑا حصہ گزر جائے تو آپ کے حسب قول تین طہر ہو چکے ہیں تو اس عورت کا طہر ثالث کے قلیل مقدار گزر جانے کے ساتھ اس عورت کا دوسرے خاوند کے ساتھ نکاح صحیح ہو جانا چاہتے اور اس عورت کا تزوج حلال ہو۔ وهذا خلاف الاجماع حالانکہ یہ خلاف اجماع ہے ۔ شوافع بھی اس نکاح کو ناجائز قرار دیتے میں هذا الجواب قاطع تو یہ جواب شوافع کے شبہہ کو بالکل قطع کر دیتا ہے وقد تضررت بذا میں اس جواب کے ساتھ متفرد ہوں قوم نے ایک اور جواب بھی دیا تھا وہ یہ ہے کہ اگر طہر مجموع ما تخلل بین الدین کا نام ہے تو پھر آپ کا اشکال وارد ہی نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ میں طہر میں طلاق ہوئی ہے وہ مجموع ما نتخلل سے کم مقدار ہے لہذا اس صورت میں عدت دو طہر اور بعض حصہ طہر کا ہوا اگر طہر مجموع ما يتخلل بین الدین کا نام نہیں بلکہ بعض مقدار کو بھی طہر کہا جاتا ہے تو پھر عدت صرف ایک طہر یا اس سے بھی کم مقدار کے ساتھ عدت مکمل ہو سکتی ہے کیونکہ اس لحاظ سے ایک ہی طہر کے ساعات ثلثہ کو ثلثہ اطہار قرار دیا جا سکتا ہے لہذا تین ساعات من طہر واحد سے گزر جانے کے بعد عدت ختم ہو اور اس کا نکاح زوج نانی کے ساتھ صحیح ہو جائے حالانکہ ایسے نہیں ہے نہ عندنا اور یہ عند کم
It does not happen. See that the 'iddah of a slave woman is half of the 'iddah of a free woman, so accordingly it should be one and a half menses, but the Shari'ah did not make a fraction; rather it said: 'The 'iddah of a slave woman is two menses,' so a complete second menses was made obligatory. Therefore, in the disputed case, a complete fourth menses becomes obligatory. And the opponents (Shafi'is) cannot give this type of answer because they do not make any part or whole of the fourth menses obligatory; rather they end the 'iddah with a part of a tuhr and two other complete tuhrs. As for 'ala anna ba'd al-tuhr, this is an answer to an assumed question. (Summary of the question: Why do you say that if the first tuhr in which divorce occurred is counted in the 'iddah, then only two tuhrs and a part of a tuhr become obligatory, not three complete tuhrs? Rather in this case three become obligatory because ba'd al-tuhr is tuhr. This is proof that it is three. Summary: that a part of tuhr is also called tuhr, because tuhr is called the least amount to which the term 'tuhr' applies, i.e., the minimum amount that can be called tuhr. For example, one hour can be called tuhr, so that part is also tuhr. Thus there are three tuhrs, and the 'iddah is completed.) So we say: This is the answer to this objection. The gist is: A part of tuhr cannot be tuhr - because if that were the case, then there would be no difference between the first tuhr and the third. Then in the third, a part of the tuhr would be considered tuhr, because according to the least that can be called tuhr, it is also tuhr. Therefore it would be appropriate that when a small part of the third tuhr passes, according to your statement, three tuhrs have passed, so it should be permissible for this woman to marry another husband after the passing of a small amount of the third tuhr, and her marriage would be lawful. And this is contrary to consensus. Indeed, this is against consensus. Even the Shafi'is consider this marriage impermissible. I said: This answer decisively cuts off the Shafi'is' doubt. And I am unique in this answer. The people also gave another answer: that if tuhr is the name for the entire period between two menses, then your objection does not arise, because the tuhr in which divorce occurred is less than the entire period, so in this case the 'iddah is two tuhrs and a part of a tuhr. If tuhr is not the name for the entire period between two menses, but rather some amount is also called tuhr, then the 'iddah could be completed with only one tuhr or even less, because accordingly, three hours of a single tuhr could be considered three tuhrs. So after three hours of one tuhr pass, the 'iddah would end and her marriage to the second husband would be valid, whereas it is not so, not according to us and not according to you.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi rebuttal to the Shafi'i position that a partial tuhr (period of purity) can suffice for the 'iddah of a woman divorced during her menstrual purity. The Hanafi argues that just as in the case of a slave woman's 'iddah, where the Shari'ah requires two complete menses instead of one and a half (because fractions are not considered), similarly, in the disputed case of a free woman's 'iddah, partial tuhr cannot be counted. The Shafi'is attempt to argue that a minimal amount of tuhr is sufficient, leading to the absurd consequence that after a small part of the third tuhr, the woman could remarry, which is against consensus. The Hanafi scholar presents two answers: first, using the analogy of the slave woman's 'iddah to show that fractions are disregarded; second, a logical argument that if partial tuhr were acceptable, then even three hours of one tuhr could be counted as three tuhrs, leading to an invalid conclusion. The passage is a classic example of Hanafi use of qiyas (analogy) and the principle of 'adam i'tibar al-ba'd (non-consideration of fractions).

Key Terms
طهر (tuhr): The period of purity between menses; in this context, the validity of counting a part of it as a full tuhr is disputed.
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi argue that a partial tuhr cannot count as a full tuhr in iddah?
A) Because the Quran explicitly requires three complete tuhrs.
B) Because if partial tuhr counted, then three hours of one tuhr would be three tuhrs, an absurdity.
C) Because the Hanafi school follows a different hadith.
D) Because the wife's consent is needed.

Key Takeaway
Partial tuhr does not count in Hanafi iddah; the principle that Shari'ah disregards fractions, supported by analogy and rational proof, prevents an absurd result.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

8 min
The Linguistic Proof for Khul' as Divorce: The Role of Al-Fa'
Analyzing the Quranic argument and linguistic proof regarding khul' as a type of divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on khul' and apply the linguistic argument of al-fa' (the particle of sequence) to determine its legal nature.

Core Idea
The fa' in 'fa-in tallaqaha' proves khul' is a divorce, not an annulment.

This lesson examines a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the legal nature of khul' (divorce by compensation). At stake is whether khul' is a type of divorce (talaq) or an annulment of marriage (faskh). The argument hinges on a single Arabic particle—the fa'—and its implications for the structure of the Quranic verses on divorce. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to analyze textual evidence and appreciate the precision required in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
State the core question: Is khul' a form of talaq or a faskh? Recognize that this determines the legal consequences, such as the possibility of further divorce after khul'.
This is an intra-ikhilaf among mujtahids.
2
Locate the key Quranic verse and the fa'
Find the verse 'fa-in tallaqaha' (Quran 2:230) and note the particle fa'. The Hanafi argument centers on the fa' indicating sequence (ta'qib).
The full context includes 'Divorce is twice' and the khul' verses.
3
Analyze the Hanafi argument from the fa'
The fa' shows that after khul' (iftida'), a subsequent divorce can occur. If khul' were an annulment, the woman would no longer be a wife, making a subsequent talaq impossible, thus invalidating the fa'.
This argument relies on the literal meaning of fa' for sequence.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i counter-argument
Imam al-Shafi'i connects 'fa-in tallaqaha' to 'Divorce is twice' and treats the khul' clause as parenthetical. He argues khul' is an annulment, not a divorce.
This reading avoids a four-divorce scenario if khul' were counted as a divorce.
5
Evaluate which interpretation is textually consistent
Which reading avoids adding a meaning (annulment) not present in the term iftida'? The Hanafi interpretation preserves the Quranic structure without requiring an external concept, and it upholds the function of the fa'.
The passage concludes that the Shafi'i reading either invalidates the fa' or creates a fourth divorce.

بعد عورت محل طلاق نہیں رہی اس لئے فان طلقہا خلع کے ساتھ متصل نہیں ہو سکتا بلکہ اس کا اتصال اول کلام یعنی الطلاق مرتان کے ساتھ ہے اور مسئلہ اقتدار یعنی ضلع جملہ معترضہ ہے۔
It (the 'iddah) can end because in this regard, three hours of a single tuhr can be considered three tuhrs. So after three hours from one tuhr, the waiting period ends and her marriage with the second husband becomes valid, whereas it is not so – neither according to us nor you. And the saying of Allah Most High: 'Then if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him' – the fa' is a specific word, meaning the word fa' is a specific word whose placement is for sequence (ta'qib). And He sequenced the divorce, meaning Allah Most High first mentioned divorce, then after that mentioned iftida' (khul'), and after that iftida' said 'fa-in tallaqaha' (then if he divorces her). So the fa' is for sequence, so by virtue of its specific meaning, it requires that after khul', a clear divorce can occur. If after khul' a clear divorce cannot occur – like Imam al-Shafi'i's school – then the requirement of the specific particle, the sequential fa', would be invalidated, which is not correct. He explained this issue in detail: Allah Most High mentioned divorce that is revocable, meaning the divorce that is two times, two revocable divorces, in His saying 'Divorce is twice, then retention with honor', then He mentioned the woman's iftida', then He mentioned 'then there is no sin upon them for what she ransoms herself with', meaning there is no harm if the woman gives financial compensation to ransom herself. And Allah Most High in 'fima iftadat bihi' mentioned only the woman's action, that she gives financial compensation, and did not mention the man's action, so in it, establishing the man's action upon the previous is clear, and his action in the previous is giving divorce. So Allah Most High mentioned two types of divorce: one without wealth – that is 'Divorce is twice', and the second type is divorce with wealth – He mentioned it in His saying 'then there is no sin upon them for what she ransoms herself with'. So from this, it is known that khul' is a type of divorce, not annulment of marriage. If Imam al-Shafi'i considers it annulment, that would be an addition to the Book of Allah, because the word iftida' does not indicate annulment, so taking the meaning of annulment is an addition from oneself. Unlike acting upon it as divorce, if iftida' is construed as divorce – as is the Hanafi school – then no addition to the Book is necessary, because divorce is already mentioned in the first speech, it is the man's action, no addition from oneself is needed. Then He said 'then if he divorces her' after the two times, meaning after this iftida', He said 'then if he divorces her' meaning if he gives a divorce after the two times, whether without wealth or with wealth, 'then she is not lawful for him'. So 'then if he divorces her' – if it is connected to the first speech and the issue of iftida' is made a parenthetical clause, as is the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i, then there is corruption of structure, because an interruption would occur. Detailing this, he said: Know that al-Shafi'i connected the saying of Allah 'then if he divorces her' to 'Divorce is twice'. And he made the mention of khul' – which is in the saying of Allah 'It is not lawful for you to take back' – a parenthetical clause, and he does not call khul' divorce, rather he considers khul' an annulment of marriage. Otherwise, the first two divorces – i.e., 'Divorce is twice' and then if khul' also is divorce, they would combine to make three divorces, and then 'then if he divorces her' would be a fourth divorce, whereas it is a third. And he (al-Shafi'i) said: Because with khul', the marriage is annulled, so after khul' no explicit divorce can attach, because after annulment the woman is no longer a place for divorce, so 'then if he divorces her' cannot be connected to khul', rather its connection is to the first speech, i.e., 'Divorce is twice', and the issue of iftida' i.e., khul' is a parenthetical clause.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) between Hanafis and Shafi'is over whether khul' (divorce by compensation) is a type of divorce (talaq) or an annulment of marriage (faskh). The Hanafi position, relying on the Quranic verse 'fa-in tallaqaha' (the fa' for sequence), argues that khul' is a divorce because the fa' indicates that after khul', a subsequent divorce can occur. If khul' were an annulment, the woman would cease to be a wife, and the subsequent divorce would be impossible, invalidating the fa'. The Shafi'i view makes the khul' clause parenthetical, connecting 'fa-in tallaqaha' to the initial 'Divorce is twice', but this leads to a fourth divorce which contradicts the Quranic count. The author refutes the Shafi'i position by showing it either invalidates the linguistic function of the fa' or leads to textual contradictions. The Hanafi interpretation maintains the Quranic structure without adding to the text.

Key Terms
الفاء (al-fa'): The letter fa' used as a particle indicating sequence (ta'qib) without delay.
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife through compensation to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main linguistic proof used by Hanafis to argue that khul' is a type of divorce?
A) The word 'khul'' itself implies divorce.
B) The particle 'fa' in 'fa-in tallaqaha' indicates sequence, proving divorce can follow khul'.
C) The verse 'Divorce is twice' includes khul' implicitly.
D) The consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains that khul' is a type of divorce based on the linguistic function of the fa' in the Quran, indicating that a subsequent divorce is possible.

The Hanafi Objection to Shafi'i on Divorce Verses and Khul'
Analyzing and refuting Shafi'i's textual connection of Quranic divorce verses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi objection to Shafi'i's interpretation of Quranic divorce verses by identifying the usul principle of fasl bil-ajnabi and applying it to avoid textual corruption.

Core Idea
Connecting Quranic verses without recognizing parenthetical inserts can create a logical impossibility—the Hanafi objection to Shafi'i's reading of divorce verses.

This passage examines a crucial usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the interpretation of Surah al-Baqarah verses 2:229-230. At stake is the nature of khul' (annulment vs. divorce) and the coherence of the Quranic text. The Hanafis argue that Shafi'i's direct connection of 'فان طلقها' to 'الطلاق مرتان' without recognizing the parenthetical about khul' leads to a structural corruption (fasl bil-ajnabi) and an impossible fourth divorce. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply usul principles to Quranic interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key Quranic phrases
Locate the phrases 'الطلاق مرتان' (divorce is twice) in verse 2:229 and 'فان طلقها' (then if he divorces her) in verse 2:230. Also note the mention of khul' in verse 2:229: 'لا يحل لكم أن تأخذوا مما آتيتموهن شيئا'.
2
Understand Shafi'i's position
Imam al-Shafi'i connects 'فان طلقها' directly to 'الطلاق مرتان' as a continuous sequence, treating the khul' verse as a parenthetical (jumla mu'tarida). He views khul' as a form of divorce, not annulment.
This makes the sequence: two talags → khul' (divorce) → then 'فان طلقها' (another divorce?)
3
Analyze the Hanafi objection
The Hanafis argue that Shafi'i's connection causes two problems: (1) It creates fasl bil-ajnabi (separation by a foreign element) because the khul' content disrupts the natural flow of the divorce count; (2) It leads to a logical impossibility: if the first two talags and khul' (considered a third divorce) are counted, then 'فان طلقها' would be a fourth divorce, whereas the verse intends it as the third.
Hanafis rely on the principle that a continuous speech cannot be broken by an alien element unless it is clearly parenthetical.
4
Examine the Hanafi alternative
According to the Hanafis, khul' is not a divorce but an annulment (faskh) of the marriage. After annulment, the woman is no longer a locus for divorce (محل طلاق). Therefore, 'فان طلقها' cannot apply to a woman after khul'; it applies only to the case where the husband has divorced her twice and then divorces her again (third divorce). The khul' verse is a parenthetical that provides an exception — the wife can ransom herself.
Thus, the connection is: 'الطلاق مرتان' (two talags) → then 'فان طلقها' (third divorce), with the khul' verse inserted as an aside.
5
Assess the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Consider a scenario: Husband divorces wife twice, then she initiates khul' and the marriage dissolves. Under Hanafi ruling, the husband may remarry her with a new contract because khul' is an annulment, not a divorce; under Shafi'i ruling, the khul' counts as a third divorce, making her unlawful until she marries another man.
This concrete difference highlights the impact of the usul disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر اول کلام کے ساتھ متصل کیا جائے اور مسئلہ افترا کو جملہ معترضہ بنایا جائے جیسے امام شافی کا قول ہے تو اس میں فساد ترکیب ہے کیونکہ درمیان میں فصل بالا جنسی لازم آجائیگا ۔ اس کی تفصیل کرتے ہوئے کہا اعلم ان الشافعی وصل الخ یعنی امام شافعی اللہ تعالی کے قول فان طلقہا کو الطلاق مرتان کے ساتھ متصل قرار دیتے ہیں ۔ وجعل ذكر الخلع یعنی ذکر خلع جو یہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول لا يحل لكم ان تاخذوا الایہ میں مذکور ہے اسے جملہ معترضہ قرار دیتے ہیں اور ضلع کو طلاق نہیں کہتے بلکہ خلع کو فسخ نکاح قرار دیتے ہیں ۔ والا یصیر الاولان ورنہ تو دو پہلی طلاقیں یعنی الطلاق مرتان اور اس کے بعد جو ضلع مذکور ہے اگر یہ بھی طلاق ہو تو اس کے ساتھ مل کر تین طلاقیں ہو جائیں گی فیصیر قوله فان طلقہا پس اس کے بعد فان طلقہا یہ طلاق رابع ہو جائے گی حالانکہ یہ طلقہ ثالثہ ہے وقال المختلفة اور فرمایا کہ مختلفہ کا چونکہ خلع کے ساتھ نکاح فسخ ہو چکا ہے اس لئے خلع کے بعد صریح طلاق ملحق نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ فسخ نکاح کے بعد عورت محل طلاق نہیں رہی اس لئے فان طلقہا خلع کے ساتھ متصل نہیں ہو سکتا بلکہ اس کا اتصال اول کلام یعنی الطلاق مرتان کے ساتھ ہے اور مسئلہ اقتدار یعنی ضلع جملہ معترضہ ہے۔
If the first speech (الطلاق مرتان) is connected [to فان طلقها] and the issue of فترا is made a parenthetical sentence, as Imam Shafi'i says, then there is corruption of composition because a separation by a foreign element would become necessary. Explaining this, he said: 'Know that al-Shafi'i connected the words of Allah 'فان طلقها' with 'الطلاق مرتان', and made the mention of khul' (which is in Allah's words 'لا يحل لكم ان تاخذوا') as a parenthetical sentence, and he does not call ضلع a divorce but considers khul' as annulment of marriage. Then the first two divorces (الطلاق مرتان) and the subsequent ضلع if it is also a divorce, then together they become three divorces, so 'فان طلقها' would become a fourth divorce, whereas it is the third divorce. And he said: Since the divorced woman has her marriage annulled by khul', therefore after khul', a clear divorce cannot be attached because after annulment, the woman is no longer a locus for divorce. Therefore, 'فان طلقها' cannot be connected to khul'; rather its connection is to the first speech (الطلاق مرتان), and the issue of فترا (ضلع) is a parenthetical sentence.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i regarding the interpretation of Quranic verses on divorce. The author explains the Hanafi objection to Imam Shafi'i's interpretation that the phrase 'فان طلقها' (then if he divorces her) in verse 2:230 is directly connected to 'الطلاق مرتان' (divorce is twice) in verse 2:229. The Hanafis argue that this leads to a corruption in the text because it would require separating the two verses by an alien subject (khul'), which is not allowed. Moreover, if ضلع (interpreted by some as a type of divorce) is also considered divorce, then the total would be three, making 'فان طلقها' a fourth divorce, which contradicts the Quranic context. The Hanafi position holds that khul' is not a divorce but an annulment (فسخ), so after khul', the wife is no longer a locus for divorce; thus 'فان طلقها' cannot refer to the woman after khul'. This analysis shows the Hanafi commitment to a cohesive and logical reading of the Quranic text, avoiding internal contradiction.

Key Terms
جملہ معترضہ (jumla mu'tarida): A parenthetical sentence inserted in the middle of a speech, which is not part of the main grammatical structure.
فصل بالاجنسی (fasl bil-ajnabi): Separation of a continuous speech by a foreign element (a sentence not directly related to the context), which is considered a corruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi objection to Imam Shafi'i's interpretation, what problem arises if the verse 'فان طلقها' is directly connected to 'الطلاق مرتان' without considering the mention of khul' as a parenthetical?
A) It would make khul' a form of divorce.
B) It would require a fourth divorce after three talags.
C) It would invalidate the verse 'الطلاق مرتان'.
D) It would make the woman a locus for divorce after khul'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi insistence on maintaining textual coherence (avoiding fasl bil-ajnabi) leads to the conclusion that khul' is an annulment, not a divorce, and that 'فان طلقها' applies only after two talags, not after khul'.

The Issue of Mufawwadah: Marriage Without Mentioning Dower
Defining mufawwadah and exposing the point of ikhtilaf on mahr obligation before consummation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings on mahr in a mufawwadah marriage and explain the Hanafi istinbat using the ba of attachment (al-ba al-ilsaq).

Core Idea
Mahr is attached to the contract itself, not to consummation – the ba of attachment in the Quran proves this.

This passage explores the concept of mufawwadah (a woman married without specified dower). It clarifies the linguistic form of the word to pinpoint the actual area of disagreement between the Hanafis and Shafi'is. The core dispute is whether mahr becomes obligatory immediately upon the contract or only upon consummation. The Hanafis use the Quranic particle 'ba' to argue that mahr is attached to the contract itself.

Guided Path
1
Define mufawwadah linguistically
Identify that the word can be an active or passive participle. The correct scenario for disagreement is when the woman delegates to her guardian (passive participle).
If the active participle is used (woman acts alone), Shafi'is invalidate the marriage entirely, so no ikhtilaf exists.
2
Identify the point of agreement
Both schools agree that if consummation (dukhul) occurs, mahr al-mithl is obligatory.
3
State the point of disagreement
The dispute arises when one spouse dies before consummation: Shafi'is say no mahr; Hanafis say mahr al-mithl is obligatory.
4
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The ba al-ilsaq in the verse 'أن تبتغوا بأموالكم' indicates that mahr is attached to the contract itself, so it becomes wajib immediately upon a valid contract.
Hanafi usul: a specific word (khass) gives a definitive ruling.
5
Analyze the Shafi'i counter-dalil
Shafi'is base mahr obligation on consummation; thus no mahr without it. They do not see the ba as a decisive specific word.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و الخلاف هينانى مسالة المفوضة لفظ مفوضہ تفویض سے ماخوذ ہے جس کی استعمال نکاح بلا ذکر المہر اور نکاح علی شرط عدم المہر میں ہوتی ہے مفوضہ اگر اسم فاعل کا صیغہ ہو اور معنی یہ ہو کہ عورت جو اپنا نکاح خود کرتی ہے بلا مہر یا علی شرط عدم المہر تو احناف کے نزدیک اس کا عقد نکاح صحیح ہے بشرطیکہ عاقلہ بالغہ ہو لیکن شوافع کے نزدیک اس کا نکاح اس صورت میں منعقد ہی نہیں ہوگا تو اس صورت میں یہ محل خلاف بین الاحناف والشوافع نہیں ہو سکتی لہذا مفوضہ بصورت اسم فاعل اس کا معنی یہ ہوگا کہ اس نے اپنے ولی کو اذن اور اجازت دیدی ہے کہ اس کا نکاح بلا مہبر یا علی شرط عدم المہر کر دے یا پھر مفوضہ صیغہ اسم مفعول کا ہونا چاہیے معنی یہ ہوگا کہ جس عورت کے ولی نے اس کو بلا مہر یا علی شرط عدم المہر عقد نکاح کے ساتھ زوج کے حوالہ کردی ہے تو ان صورتوں میں یہ مسئلہ خلافیہ بین الا ہوگا حاصل اختلاف یہ ہے کہ ایسی عورت کے ساتھ اگر زوج نے وطی کرلی ہے تو حق المهر واجب ہو جائیگی یعند الحنفیه واكثر الشافعیہ تو گویا یہ مسئلہ متفق علیہا ہوا واختلاف اس صورت میں ہے جب احد الزوجین قبل از دخول وفات پا جائے تو شوافع کے نزدیک کوئی مہر واجب نہیں اور احناف کے نزدیک مہر مثلی واجب ہو جائیگی چونکہ شوافع کے نزدیک مہر کا وجوب بالدخول ہوتا ہے جب دخول نہیں ہے تو مہر واجب نہیں ہوگی احناف کے نزدیک مہر واجب ہو جائیگی کیونکہ با الصاق کے لئے ہے لہذا ابتغا یعنی عقد صحیح کے ساتھ مہر ملصق ہے۔ عقد صحیح منفک عن المہر نہیں ہو سکتا جب عقد صحیح ہوچکا ہے تو مہر مثلی اس عقد کے ساتھ لازم ہو جائے گی ورنہ تو با الصاقیہ جو لفظ خاص تھا اس کا مقتضا پورا نہیں ہوگا حالانکہ خاص موجب حکم ہوتا ہے قطعاً
And the difference here is the issue of al-mufawwadah. The word mufawwadah is derived from tafwid (delegation). Its usage is in marriage without mentioning the dower and marriage on condition of no dower. If mufawwadah is in the form of the active participle, meaning a woman who performs her own marriage without dower or on condition of no dower, then according to the Hanafis, her marriage contract is valid provided she is sane and adult. But according to the Shafi'is, her marriage in this case is not valid at all. So in this case there cannot be a place of difference between Hanafis and Shafi'is. Therefore, mufawwadah in the form of active participle would mean that she has given permission to her guardian to perform her marriage without dower or on condition of no dower. Or perhaps mufawwadah should be in the form of passive participle, meaning a woman whose guardian has handed her over with a marriage contract without dower or on condition of no dower. In these cases, this is a disputed issue between the two schools. The conclusion of the difference is that if the husband has had intercourse with such a woman, then the right of mahr becomes obligatory – according to the Hanafis and most Shafi'is. So this issue is virtually agreed upon. And the difference is in the case where one of the spouses dies before consummation. According to the Shafi'is, no mahr is obligatory; according to the Hanafis, the mahr of the like (mahr mithl) becomes obligatory. Because according to the Shafi'is, the obligation of mahr is based on consummation; when there is no consummation, mahr is not obligatory. According to the Hanafis, mahr is obligatory because the ba of attachment is for attachment; therefore, 'ibtigha' means that with a valid contract, mahr is attached. A valid contract cannot be separated from mahr. When the valid contract has occurred, the mahr mithl becomes necessary with the contract. Otherwise, the requirement of the ba al-ilaq (the specific word) would not be fulfilled, whereas a specific word gives a ruling decisively.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute over the concept of 'mufawwadah' (the woman who delegates her marriage without specifying dower). The author clarifies the linguistic forms of the word to identify the correct scenario of disagreement. If mufawwadah is taken as the active participle (meaning she performs her own marriage without dower), the Shafi'is consider the marriage invalid, so there is no point of difference. Therefore, the actual dispute is when the woman delegates to her guardian (or the guardian acts) to marry her without dower. In that case, both schools agree that if consummation occurs, mahr is due. The real difference is when one spouse dies before consummation: Shafi'is say no mahr (since mahr is only due upon consummation), while Hanafis say mahr mithl is due immediately upon the contract. This is because the Hanafis derive from the verse 'أن تبتغوا بأموالكم' that the mahr is attached to the contract itself, so it becomes obligatory at the time of the contract, not dependent on consummation.

Key Terms
مفوضة (mufawwadah): A woman whose marriage is performed without specifying the dower, either through her own delegation or through her guardian, and the dower is determined by mahr al-mithl.
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to what women of her status receive, used when no dower is specified or when the marriage is without dower.
با الصاق (ba al-ilsaq): The particle 'ba' in the Quranic verse indicating attachment of mahr to the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a mufawwadah marriage where the husband dies before consummation, what is the Hanafi ruling on mahr?
A) No mahr is obligatory because there was no consummation.
B) Mahr al-mithl is obligatory immediately upon the contract.
C) Mahr is obligatory only if specified in the contract.
D) Mahr is half of the specified dower.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the mahr is attached to the marriage contract itself through the ba al-ilsaq, making mahr al-mithl wajib immediately upon a valid contract without specification.

Minimum Mahr: Hanafi Qiyas and the Shafi'i Dispute
Explanation of the minimum dower (mahr) in Hanafi school

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi qiyas that establishes the minimum mahr at ten dirhams and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-position.

Core Idea
The minimum mahr is ten dirhams, derived by qiyas on the hand's compensation in theft.

This lesson explores how the Hanafi school uses analogical reasoning (qiyas) to fix a minimum dower (mahr) at ten dirhams. We will examine the analogy between the hand and the pudendum, and then contrast the Shafi'i view that any valuable can serve as mahr. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate competing usul methodologies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State the Hanafi position on the minimum mahr: ten dirhams.
This is a wajib amount in marriage according to the school.
2
Deconstruct the qiyas
Break down the analogy: asl = theft, hand cut with diya of ten dirhams; far' = mahr for marriage; illa = both hand and pudendum are limbs.
The illa is the shared attribute of being a limb.
3
Examine companion traditions
Note the supporting transmission from Companions: 'لا أقل من عشرة دراهم' (no less than ten dirhams).
Companion reports are considered hujja in Hanafi usul.
4
State the Shafi'i position and its basis
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that any valuable can be mahr, with no fixed minimum. Basis: general permissibility and absence of a restrictive text.
The difference reflects distinct approaches to textual evidence and analogy.
5
Compare the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: Hanafi school requires adjustment if mahr is less than ten dirhams; Shafi'i school accepts any amount.
This ikhtilaf has real-world implications for marriage contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو عشرة دراهم، اور وہ دس درہم ہیں کیونکہ اس کے ساتھ سرقت کے معاملہ میں قطع ید واجب ہو جاتی ہے تو ید بھی ایک عضو ہے جیسے بضع بھی ایک عضو ہے لہذا اس کا ادنی عوض دس درہم سے کم نہیں ہوگا اور ویسے آثار من الصحابہ بھی موجود ہیں لا أقل من عشرة دراهم. وعند الشافعی اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک جو چیز ثمن بن سکتی ہے وہی حق المہر بھی ہو سکتی ہے خواہ قلیل ہو یا کثیر کوئی ادنی مقدار ان کے نزدیک متعین نہیں ہے۔
And it is ten dirhams, and those ten dirhams are [the minimum] because along with it in the case of theft, cutting off the hand becomes obligatory, so the hand is also a limb like the pudendum is also a limb, therefore the minimum compensation for it will not be less than ten dirhams, and similarly there are traditions from the Companions: 'No less than ten dirhams.' According to al-Shafi'i, whatever can serve as a price can also be dower, whether little or much; no minimum amount is specified according to him.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the minimum dower (mahr). The author begins by stating that the minimum is ten dirhams. The reasoning is analogical (qiyas): just as the hand's compensation (diya) in theft is set at ten dirhams (as a minimum for cutting), and the hand is a limb, similarly the pudendum (bada') is a limb, so its compensation — which is the dower — should also be at least ten dirhams. This is supported by transmitted reports from the Companions stating 'no less than ten dirhams.' The author then contrasts this with the Shafi'i position, which holds no fixed minimum; anything that can be used as a price can be dower. This is a clear ikhtilaf (dispute) between the schools.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): Dower paid by the husband to the wife in marriage.
درهم (dirham): Silver coin used as currency; the Hanafi minimum mahr is ten dirhams.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic jurisprudence.
بضع (bada' / bada'a): Pudendum; in context, the female genitalia as the object of mahr.
قطع يد (qat' yad): Cutting off the hand as punishment for theft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A direct Quranic verse
B) Qiyas on the hand's diya in theft
C) Consensus of all scholars
D) Only companion traditions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi minimum mahr of ten dirhams is derived by qiyas on the hand's diya and supported by companion reports, in contrast to the Shafi'i open position.

Hiddam: Does a Second Marriage Nullify Previous Divorces?
Dispute on hiddam for less-than-triple divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on hiddam for less-than-triple divorce and identify the usul principles (interpretation of 'hatta' and a fortiori reasoning) that underlie the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a fortiori reasoning extends the nullification of divorces from triple to lesser counts.

The concept of hiddam addresses whether a valid second marriage and subsequent divorce reset a woman's divorce count to zero, allowing the first husband to start anew. While all schools agree on this for triple divorce, a dispute arises when the divorce was one or two. This lesson explores the usul al-fiqh reasoning behind the Hanafi position, examining the role of Quranic text, hadith, and qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed and disputed cases
The passage states that for triple divorce, hiddam is agreed. The dispute is when the divorce count is less than three (one or two).
This distinction is crucial; the entire ikhtilaf hinges on this difference.
2
State the Shafi'i position and their dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the second marriage does not nullify the previous divorces. His proof is the word 'hatta' in the Quran (2:230), which he interprets as a limit that only terminates an existing prohibition. Since less than triple does not create a prohibition, 'hatta' does not apply and no new dissolution occurs.
The Shafi'i rely on the apparent meaning of the text.
3
State the Hanafi position and their dalil
Hanafis hold that the second marriage nullifies all previous divorces. Their proof is the hadith 'until she tastes his honey' and the hadith cursing the muhallil, which establish new dissolution for triple divorce. They then apply a fortiori reasoning (qiyas awlawi): if it applies to triple, it applies even more to lesser counts.
The Hanafi use external evidence (hadith) to override the apparent limit of 'hatta'.
4
Analyze the usul principles at play
The Shafi'i adhere to the linguistic limit (ghayah) of 'hatta', while the Hanafi use the concept of al-amr bi al-umur and qiyas awlawi. The dispute illustrates how different usul methodologies yield different rulings.
Note that the Hanafi do not claim the Quran is abrogated; they supplement it with hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a woman divorced twice by A, marries B, divorces, and returns to A, Hanafis say A now has full right to three divorces; Shafi'is say A has only one divorce remaining (the one not yet used).
This difference affects legal strategy and counseling.

And Fakhr al-Islam presented some other issues in this chapter of special ruling; I presented those issues at the end of the chapter on abrogation in the discussions of 'addition to the text' except for two issues which Fakhr al-Islam presented at this place, which I completely omitted due to fear of prolongation. One issue is 'hiddam' (demolition): a woman divorced with a triple divorce, after being free from the marriage of the second husband, becomes permissible for the first husband; that is a new dissolution (hall jadid), i.e., the ruling of the first three divorces is completely terminated, and he will again own three divorces over that woman. So this new dissolution completely demolishes the previous triple divorces. This issue is agreed upon. The disagreement is in the case when a woman is divorced without the three [i.e., one or two divorces] and after completing the waiting period from divorce, she marries a second husband, then after some time she is divorced from the second husband, and after her waiting period she marries the first husband. Is this new dissolution demolishing the ruling of the previous divorces or not? Imam al-Shafi‘i does not consider the second marriage with the second husband as demolishing for less than three divorces, contrary to the Hanafis, who consider it as demolishing for previous divorces whether they are triple or fewer. The new dissolution and new ownership will bring the triple divorces. Imam al-Shafi‘i does not accept new dissolution in this case; rather, he holds the old dissolution: the previous one or two divorces he gave remain, and in this marriage the first husband will own the remainder of the three divorces, not full ownership of three. He presents the reasoning that the word 'hatta' in Allah's statement 'until she marries another husband' is specific in meaning of limit; it will terminate the previous prohibition but will not establish new dissolution. In triple divorces, prohibition is proven; 'hatta' will terminate it. In less than triple, prohibition is not proven; 'hatta' is for a limit; how can it terminate when there is no prohibition? Therefore, establishing new dissolution from 'hatta' is abandoning the specific. The answer: New dissolution is proven by the hadith 'even until she tastes his honey' which is famous, and by the hadith 'cursed is the tahleel maker and the one for whom tahleel is made'. The tahleel maker is one who establishes dissolution. When new dissolution is proven for triple, then for less than triple it is proven a fortiori.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage discusses the issue called 'hiddam' – whether a valid second marriage and divorce nullifies the previous divorce count when a woman returns to her first husband. The author notes that Fakhr al-Islam had mentioned this and another issue. The agreed case is when a woman is divorced thrice; all agree the second marriage makes her halal again and the previous divorces are nullified. The dispute is when the first divorce was less than three (one or two). Hanafis hold that the second marriage also nullifies those remaining divorces, so the first husband starts with a fresh right to three divorces. Shafi‘is hold that only the prohibition of triple divorce is terminated; for less than triple, there was no prohibition, so 'hatta' does not create new dissolution; the remaining divorces continue. The Hanafi response uses a hadith and a fortiori argument: if it applies for triple, it applies for less.

Key Terms
ہدم (hiddam): The nullification of previous divorces by a new valid marriage and subsequent divorce.
محلل (muhallil): The second husband who marries a thrice-divorced woman to make her permissible for her first husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It depends on the husband's intention.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on hiddam illustrates how hadith and a fortiori reasoning can override a literal reading of a Quranic term.

The Hanafi View: Theft, Cutting, and No Liability – A Usul Dispute with the Shafi‘is
Hanafi view that cutting hand precludes liability if property destroyed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi and Shafi‘i positions on the liability of a thief when stolen property is destroyed, and apply the Hanafi usul principle that the hadd (punishment) overrides the daman (compensation) to similar cases.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, the hadd punishment abrogates the property guarantee; for Shafi‘is, both apply unless explicitly excluded.

This passage presents a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools regarding the liability of a thief when the stolen property is destroyed. The Hanafis argue that the sanctity ('isma) of the property is voided by the theft, so only the hand-cut is due, not compensation. The Shafi‘is object that the Quranic command to cut hands does not explicitly cancel liability. Understanding this dispute reveals how each school interprets textual commands (khusus) and applies legal maxims (like al-hadd wa al-daman la yajtami'an).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the ruling: cutting the hand is obligatory, no compensation is due if the property is destroyed by the thief.
2
State the Hanafi dalil
Theft voids the property's inviolability; the principle that punishment supersedes compensation overrides the default liability.
3
State the Shafi‘i objection
The Quranic text only commands cutting, not dropping compensation; thus both should apply.
Shafi‘is rely on the literal scope of the specific command.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis invoke the legal maxim that the hadd punishment and guarantee do not combine, derived from the overall objectives of shari‘ah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: in Hanafi fiqh, a thief who destroys the stolen property is not liable for its value; in Shafi‘i, he remains liable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرے مسئلہ قطع مع الضمان کا ہے اس بارے میں احناف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ سارق جب سرقت کرتا ہے تو جو مال اس کے ہاتھ لگتا ہے اس کی عصمتہ بحق السارق [؟] باطل ہو جاتی ہے لہذا مال اگر ہلاک ہو جائے یا سارق خود ہلاک کر دیوے تو اس صورت میں قطع ید واجب ہوگی ضمان مال واجب نہیں ہوگی تو شوافع نے اعتراض کیا کہ فاقطعوا میں لفظ قطع خاص ہے جس کا معنی اب انتہ الشتی ہے یہ ابطال عصمت پر دال نہیں ہے جس کی وجہ سے ضمان ساقط ہو جائے لہذا ابطال عصمتہ کے معنی کو لینا یہ لفظ خاص کے مقتضا پر ترک عمل ہے ۔ احناف اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں کہ انتقام ضمان جزاء بما کسا سے ثابت ہوتی ہے
The second issue is that of cutting with guarantee. In this regard, the Hanafi school is that when the thief steals, the inviolability of the property that comes into his hand is nullified by the right of the thief. Therefore, if the property perishes or the thief himself destroys it, then in that case cutting of the hand is obligatory, but the guarantee of the property is not obligatory. The Shafi‘is objected that in the verse 'so cut off' the word 'cut' is specific, meaning separation of the thing, and it does not indicate annulment of inviolability which would cause the guarantee to drop. Hence taking the meaning of annulment of inviolability is abandoning acting upon the specific. The Hanafis answer that the retribution of the guarantee is established by the principle that the punishment supersedes the compensation.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on the liability (damān) of stolen property when the thief's hand is cut. The key point: the sanctity ('isma) of the property is voided upon theft, so if the property is destroyed, only the hand is cut and no compensation is required. The Shafi‘is argue that the Quranic command 'so cut off their hands' (al-Ma'ida 5:38) only says to cut the hand, not to void the property's inviolability, so the thief should still be liable. The Hanafi response invokes a principle (possibly 'al-ḥadd wa al-ḍamān lā yajtamiʿān' or similar) that punishment takes precedence over compensation. The exact phrase 'جزاء بما کسا' may refer to a legal maxim that the penal sanction replaces the civil liability.

Key Terms
عصمة (‘isma): The inviolability or protected status of property that normally requires compensation if destroyed.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for certain crimes, such as the cutting of the hand for theft.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or compensation for loss or damage to property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Only compensation is required, hand is not cut.
D) Neither hand nor compensation applies.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi view that the hadd punishment abrogates compensation for stolen property destroyed by the thief is based on the usul principle that punishment and guarantee do not combine.

Dispute on Cutting the Thief's Hand Without Financial Guarantee
Refuting the Shafi'i objection that cutting hand requires guarantee of property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on whether cutting the hand nullifies property guarantee and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal using Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Hanafi: hand-cutting nullifies property inviolability; Shafi'i: text only commands cutting, so guarantee remains.

In this passage, we examine a key usul dispute: when the Quran commands cutting the thief's hand, does it also imply the forfeiture of property value? The Hanafis argue that the punishment of cutting suffices, while the Shafi'is insist on additional compensation. Understanding this dispute reveals how different schools weigh the implications of a specific command (خاص) and the role of broader principles.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its basis
Restate the Hanafi view: the thief is not liable for the property's value because its inviolability (عصمة) is nullified. Basis: the principle 'جزاء بما كسبا' (recompense according to what one earned).
The Hanafi use this Quranic principle to link the punishment to the crime comprehensively.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'is argue that the word 'قطع' in the verse 'فَاقْطَعُوا أَيْدِيَهُمَا' is specific (خاص) and only means severing the hand. It does not imply nullification of inviolability. Thus, the thief must still pay compensation if the property is consumed.
This objection relies on the usul principle that a specific command cannot be extended beyond its literal meaning.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the recompense (جزاء) includes both cutting and guarantee, but since the property is consumed, guarantee is not required because the property's sanctity is nullified at the moment of theft.
They also cite hadith evidence that the Prophet ﷺ cut hands without ordering compensation.
4
Derive the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, a Hanafi judge would not order the thief to pay the value of the stolen goods after cutting; a Shafi'i judge would order payment in addition to cutting.
This shows how a difference in usul principle leads to different actual rulings.
5
Evaluate the strength of each position
Assess which school's argument is stronger based on textual evidence and usul principles. The Hanafi position relies on a broader reading of the Quranic principle; the Shafi'i position adheres to the literal scope of the command.
No explicit tarjih is given in the passage, but the commentary supports the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرے مسئلہ قطع مع الضمان کا ہے اس بارے میں احناف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ سارق جب سرقت کرتا ہے تو جو مال اس کے ہاتھ لگتا ہے اس کی عصمہ بحق سارق میں باطل ہو جاتی ہے لہذا مال اگر ہلاک ہو جائے یا سارق خود بلاک کر دیوے تو اس صورت میں قطع ید واجب ہوگی ضمان مال واجب نہیں ہوگی تو شوافع نے اعتراض کیا کہ فاقطعوا‎ میں لفظ قطع خاص ہے جس کا معنی اب انتہ الشتی ہے یہ ابطال عصمت پر دال نہیں ہے جس کی وجہ سے ضمان ساقط ہو جائے لہذا ابطال عصمتہ کے معنی کو لینا یہ لفظ خاص کے مقتضا پر ترک عمل ہے ۔ احناف اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں کہ انتقام ضمان جزاء بما کسا سے ثابت ہوتی ہے
The second issue is that of cutting with guarantee. In this regard, the Hanafi school is that when a thief steals, the inviolability of the property that comes into his hand becomes nullified with respect to the thief. Therefore, if the property is destroyed or the thief himself consumes it, in that case cutting of the hand is obligatory, and guarantee of the property is not obligatory. The Shafi'is objected: In 'فَاقْطَعُوا' the word 'قطع' is specific (خاص) meaning 'severing of the hand'; it does not indicate nullification of inviolability that would cause guarantee to be dropped. So taking the meaning of nullification is abandoning acting upon the requirement of the specific word. The Hanafis answer: that the punishment of [cutting] and guarantee are proven by 'جزاء بما كسبا' [Quran 5:38].
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage addresses the dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding whether a thief is liable for compensation (ضمان) of the stolen property in addition to having his hand cut off. The Hanafi position is that when the thief takes the property, its inviolability (عصمة) becomes nullified for him, so if the property perishes, he is not required to pay its value; only the hand-cutting is obligatory. The Shafi'is object, arguing that the verse 'فَاقْطَعُوا أَيْدِيَهُمَا' only commands cutting the hand, and does not imply nullification of inviolability. They say that to infer such nullification from the verse is to ignore the specific wording. The Hanafis respond by citing the Quranic principle that the recompense for wrongdoing is according to what one has earned (جزاء بما كسبا), implying that both cutting and liability can be established. The argument is based on how to interpret the specific term 'قطع'—whether it carries implied meanings.

Key Terms
عصمة (isma): Inviolability or protected status of property; here it is said to be nullified with respect to the thief.
خاص (khass): A specific term that refers to a particular meaning without generality.
جزاء بما كسبا (jaza' bima kasaba): Recompense according to what one earned; a Quranic principle indicating that punishment fits the crime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that cutting the hand nullifies property inviolability, while the Shafi'i school requires additional compensation; the difference stems from interpreting the Quranic command 'قطع' as specific or implying broader effects.

The Minimum Number of Plural (Aqall al-Jamm') in Hanafi Usul
Dispute about whether plural applies to two or three, with proofs and refutations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum number of plural (aqall al-jamm') and evaluate the opposing proofs from Quran and hadith using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, true plural means three or more; two is dual, not plural.

The minimum number indicated by the Arabic plural form (جمع) is a foundational usul dispute with significant implications for interpreting legal texts. This lesson examines the Hanafi position that plural denotes three or more, contrasting it with the view that two suffices. We will analyze the proofs from each side and understand the Hanafi responses based on linguistic consensus (ijma' ahl al-lughah) and contextual interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Issue
What is the minimum number of individuals that a true Arabic plural (جمع) indicates? The dispute centers on whether plural includes two or requires three or more.
2
State the Hanafi Position and Primary Proof
Hanafi scholars, citing the consensus of linguists, assert that true plural indicates three or more. The existence of a separate dual form (تثنیہ) proves that two is not included.
3
Present the Opposing Proofs
The opposing school cites Quranic verses (inheritance verse 'fa in kāna lahu ikhwah', hearts verse 'fa qad safat qulūbukumā') and a hadith ('al-ithnāni fa mā fawqahumā jamā'ah') as evidence that plural can apply to two.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response to Each Proof
The inheritance verse is a special case by consensus; the hearts verse is metaphorical (مجاز); the hadith is interpreted contextually (inheritance, prayer, travel) and does not establish a linguistic rule.
5
Conclude the Thamarah al-Khilaf
In legal interpretation, Hanafi jurists require three or more for a plural unless there is explicit evidence (like consensus or clear context) for two, affecting rulings on witnesses, congregational prayer, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نساء تو یہ شخص ایک یا دو عورتوں سے نکاح کرتا ہے تو حانث نہیں ہوگا تین یا چار سے نکاح کرتا ہے تو حانث ہو جائیگا ۔ وعند البعض اثنان بعض حضرات کے نزدیک جمع کے افراد کم سے کم دو ہیں لقولہ تعالیٰ فان كان له اخوة جو لوگ اس کے قائل تھے کہ جمع کا اطلاق کم سے کم دو افراد پر صحیح ہے یہ ان کے دلائل میں پہلی فان کان له اخوۃ یعنی میت کے لئے اگر اخوۃ ہوں تو میت کی والدہ کو ثلث میراث سے محجوب کر کے سدس تک پہونچا دیں گے میت کے بھائی خواہ دو ہوں یا تین یا اس سے زائد تو والدہ میت کو ثلث سے سدس تک لے جانے میں برابر ہیں البتہ ایک بھائی کے ہونے میں وہ ثلث کی مستحق رہیگی تو لفظ اخوة جمع ہے دو پر اس کا اطلاق ہو رہا ہے۔ وقوله فقد صفت قلوبکما یہ ان کی دوسری دلیل ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اس آیت میں لفظ قلوب جمع ہے لیکن مراد دو قلب میں اس سے زائد نہیں ہیں کیونکہ لفظ کہا جو مضاف الیہ ہے یہ تشنہ ہے تو دو شخصوں کے دل بھی دو ہو سکتے ہیں زیادہ نہیں ہو سکتے کیونکہ ما جعل الله الرجل من قلبین فی جو نہ تو ایک شخص کا دل ایک ہی ہو سکتا ہے تو دوانسانوں کے دو دل ہوں گے کیا ضمیر خطا سے ام المؤمنین عائشہ اور حفصہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا مراد ہیں۔ وقوله عليه السلام الاثنان فما فوقهما جماعة یہ ان کی تیسری دلیل ہے یہ کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ دو اور دو سے زیادہ جماعت ہے اس قسم کا قول اگر کسی لغوی سے صادر ہو تو حجت ہو جاتا ہے اور جب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے تو بطریق اولی حجت ہوگا۔ ولنا اجماع اهل اللغة یہ دلیل جمہور ہے جو اس کے قائل نہیں کہ جمع کا اطلاق ثلثہ فصاعدا پر ہوتا ہے تو کہا ہمارے لئے دلیل اہل لغتہ کا اجماع ہے کہ انھوں نے واحد اور تشنہ اور جمع کے لئے الگ الگ مختلف صیغے مقرر کہتے ہیں تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جمع کا اطلاق حقیقی دو پر نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ دو کے لئے صیغہ تثنیہ کا مقرر کیا گیا ہے ولا نزاع فی الارث یہ ان مخالفین کے دلائل کا جواب ہے یہ ان کی دلیل خان کان لہ اخوۃ کا جواب ہے ۔ خلاصہ جواب یہ کہ یہ آیت میراث کے متعلق سے اس میں کوئی نزاع و اختلاف نہیں ہے کہ میراث اور وصیت میں جمع کی اقل مقدار دو ہوتی ہے لہذا اس کے ساتھ استدلال صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ کلام ما وراء الميراث والوصیۃ میں ہے ۔ وقولہ تعالیٰ فقد صفت قلوبکما تو یہاں قلوب کا اطلاق قلبین پر مجاز ہے جیسے جمع کا اطلاق واحد پر ہوتا ہے علی سبیل المجاز جیسے از قال لهم الناس میں تھا تو نزاع اطلاق حقیقی میں ہے نہ کہ مجازی میں والحدیث محمول الا یہ ان کی تیسری دلیل الاثنان فما فوقعا جماعۃ کا جواب ہے . حاصل جواب یہ کہ حدیث مواریث کے متعلق ہے اور میراث میں بالاتفاق جمع کی اقل مقدار دو سے شروع ہوتی ہے۔ او على سنية تقدم الامام يا به حدیث امام کے متعلق ہے کہ جب مقتدی دو ہوں تو امام کو مقتدیوں سے آگے بڑھ کر کھڑا ہونا چاہتے جیسے دو سے زائد مقتدیوں میں ہوتا ہے بخلاف اس کے مقتدی ایک ہو تو وہ امام کے جنب یمین پر کھڑا ہو گا نہ کہ امام کے پیچھے ۔ او على اجتماع الرفقة الم یا یہ حدیث رفقاء سفر کے متعلق ہے بعد قوۃ الاسلام فانه لما كان ال یعنی جب ابتداء میں اسلام کمزور حالت میں تھا تو رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ایک آدمی تنہا سفر کرے یا دو آدمی اکٹھے ہو کر سفر کریں اس سے نہی کر دی تھی اور فرمایا الواحد شیطان والاثنان شیطانان والثلثة ركب فلما ظهر قوة پس جب قوۃ اسلام ظاہر ہوگئی تو دو اشخاص کو سفر کرنیکی رخصت عطا فرمائی فرمایا الاثنان فما فوقهما جماعتہ تو اس حدیث کا تعلق مسائل اور احکام سے ہے وضع اور لغت کے ساتھ نہیں ہے اور یہ تاویلات اس لئے ضروری ہیں کہ اجماع اہل لغت اور حدیث کے مابین تخالف نہ ہونے پائے ولا تمسك لهم بنحو فعلنا یہ جمع کو اثنین پر اطلاق کرنے والوں کی ایک اور دلیل کا جواب ہے ۔ فعلنا کی وضع جمع کے لئے ہے اور ناضمیر جمع کے لئے موضوع ہے تو اس کا اطلاق دو نپر بھی ہوتا جیسے تین اور تین سے زائد پر ہوتا ہے تو جواباً کہا کہ ان کے ساتھ ان کا تمسک نہیں ہو سکتا لانہ مشترک یعنی صیغہ متکلم مع الغیر کا جمع اور تشنیہ میں مشترک ہے اس کی وضع جیسے جمع کے لئے۔ اسی طرح تثنیہ کے لئے بھی ہے لا ان المثنی جمع یعنی اس کا اطلاق اس بنا پر نہیں ہے مثنی فرد ہے جمع کا بلکہ بطریق الوضع للمثنی کے ہے لذات المثنی جمع یعنی اس کا اطلاق بایں لحاظ نہیں کہ مثنی بھی جمع ہے ۔ فيصح تخصيص المجمع تعقیب یعنی مصنف نے جو یہ کہا ہے کہ اقل مقدار جمع کی ثلثہ ہے ویہ اس پر تعقیب و تفریح ہے لہذا جمع جیسے الرجال دمانی معناہ اور وہ الفاظ جو معنی جمع میں جیسے الربط اور القوم ان کی تخصیص تین تک ہو سکتی ہے تین سے کم دوا ونر
Regarding women: if a person marries one or two women, he is not sinful; if he marries three or four, he becomes sinful. And according to some (certain scholars) two (is the minimum of plural): some scholars hold that the minimum number for plural is two, based on His saying: 'fa in kāna lahu ikhwah' (if he has brothers). Those who believe that the application of plural to at least two individuals is correct; this is their first proof: 'fa in kāna lahu ikhwah' means if the deceased has brothers, his mother is prevented from one-third and reduced to one-sixth. Whether the brothers are two, three, or more, it is equal in reducing the mother from one-third to one-sixth. However, if there is only one brother, she remains entitled to one-third. So the word 'ikhwah' is plural and applies to two. And His saying: 'fa qad safat qulūbukumā' (so your hearts became purified) is their second proof. The summary is that in this verse the word 'qulūb' is plural, but it means two hearts, not more, because the word 'kumā' (your dual) is dual, so the hearts of two persons are two, not more, since 'mā ja‘ala llāhu li rajulin min qalbayn' (Allah did not make for a man two hearts). So by the dual pronoun, the two hearts refer to the two persons – here the Mother of the Believers ‘A’ishah and Hafṣah (may Allah be pleased with them). And his saying (peace be upon him): 'al-ithnāni fa mā fawqahumā jamā‘ah' (two and above constitute a group) is their third proof: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said that two and more are a group. If such a statement comes from a linguist, it is a proof, and when the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) says it, it is even more a proof. And for us (the Hanafis) is the consensus of the linguists: the majority who do not hold that plural applies to three or more say our proof is the consensus of linguists that they have assigned distinct forms for singular, dual, and plural. From this it is known that the true application of plural cannot be to two, because for two the dual form is assigned. And there is no dispute in inheritance: this is a response to the opponents' proofs, especially their proof from 'fa in kāna lahu ikhwah'. The summary of the response is that this verse concerns inheritance, and there is no dispute that in inheritance and bequests the minimum of plural is two; therefore, using it as proof is not valid because the discussion is beyond inheritance and bequests. And His saying 'fa qad safat qulūbukumā' – here the application of 'qulūb' to two hearts is metaphorical, just as plural is applied to singular metaphorically, like in 'qāla lahumu n-nās' (the people said to them). So the dispute is about real application, not metaphorical. And the hadith 'al-ithnāni fa mā fawqahumā jamā‘ah' – the response is that this hadith is either concerning inheritance (where by consensus plural starts from two), or concerning the sunnah of the imam's precedence: when there are two followers, the imam should stand ahead as with more than two, unlike when there is one follower who stands to the right. Or concerning companions of a journey: after the strength of Islam, when initially Islam was weak, the Messenger forbade travelling alone or in pairs, saying 'al-wāhidu shayṭān, wal-ithnāni shayṭānān, wath-thalāthatu rakbbun' (one is a devil, two are devils, three are a riding group). When Islam became strong, he permitted two to travel, saying 'al-ithnāni fa mā fawqahumā jamā‘ah'. So this hadith relates to practical rulings, not linguistic categories. These interpretations are necessary to avoid conflict between the consensus of linguists and the hadith. And they cannot cling to something like 'fa‘alnā' (we did) – this responds to another proof of those who apply plural to two: 'fa‘alnā' is made for plural, and the plural pronoun is for plural, so it applies to two just as to three or more. The response is that they cannot cling to this because it is shared (mushtarak): the first person plural form is shared between plural and dual; it is made for both, not because the dual is a type of plural, but by way of being made for the dual. So the author says: the minimum of plural is three; this is the conclusion and clarification. Thus, plural like 'ar-rijāl' (men) has the meaning of three or more, and words that convey a collective meaning like 'ar-rabṭ' (the group) and 'al-qawm' (the people) can be specified to three, not less than two.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents a classic usul al-fiqh dispute regarding the minimum number indicated by the Arabic plural form (جمع). The Hanafi school, based on the consensus of linguists, maintains that the true plural denotes three or more, with two being reserved for the dual (تثنیہ). The opposing view, attributed to some scholars, argues that plural can apply to two, citing Quranic verses (e.g., 'ikhwah' for two brothers in inheritance, 'qulub' for two hearts) and a hadith ('two and above constitute a group'). The Hanafi commentator refutes each proof: (1) The inheritance verse is a special case by consensus where plural may start at two. (2) The word 'qulub' is used metaphorically, as the dual pronoun indicates two actual hearts. (3) The hadith is interpreted in multiple ways—concerning inheritance rules, the imam's position in prayer, or travel companions after Islam's strength—none of which establish a linguistic rule. Additionally, the argument from 'fa‘alnā' (we did) is dismissed because the form is shared between dual and plural. The author concludes that the minimum of plural is three, with exceptions only in specific contexts like inheritance and bequests by consensus.

Key Terms
جمع (jamm'): In this text, the plural form which in its true sense applies to three or more, not two.
تثنیہ (tathniyah): The dual form specifically for two individuals/items.
اقل جمع (aqall al-jamm'): The minimum number of individuals for a true plural; argued to be three in Hanafi usul.
جماعت (jamā'ah): Group; in the hadith, refers to two or more but Hanafi interprets it contextually.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, what is the minimum number for the true (haqiqi) application of the Arabic plural (جمع) in linguistic and legal usage?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) It depends on the context without a fixed minimum

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, relying on linguistic consensus, maintains that the true plural denotes three or more, with two being the distinct dual form; exceptions are context-specific and do not redefine the linguistic norm.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Isnad Haqiqi and Majazi: The Criterion of al-Mutakallim
Distinguishing real and metaphorical ascription of actions based on the speaker's belief

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion for distinguishing haqiqi from majazi isnad and evaluate the opposing 'aql-based view.

Core Idea
The speaker's belief, not rational objectivity, determines whether an ascription is real or metaphorical.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, understanding the distinction between real (haqiqi) and metaphorical (majazi) ascription (isnad) is crucial for interpreting legal and theological texts. The classification depends on the speaker's belief about who performed the action, not on objective reality or rational analysis. This lesson explores the criterion set by Sahib al-Miftah and contrasts it with an alternative view based on intellect.

Guided Path
1
Define isnad haqiqi and majazi
Start by identifying the two types of ascription as defined in the text: haqiqi when the speaker attributes an action to what he believes is the true doer; majazi when he attributes it to a non-doer due to a connection.
The definition hinges on the speaker's i'tiqad (belief).
2
Analyze the example 'anbat al-rabi' al-baqla'
Consider the example: a Muslim says it, knowing Allah is the true cause, so it is majazi. A materialist says it, believing spring is the cause, so it is haqiqi for him. This illustrates the criterion.
The same sentence can be haqiqi or majazi depending on the speaker's belief.
3
Compare with the 'aql-based criterion
Some scholars argue that the criterion is rational: if the attributed agent is rationally considered the doer, it is haqiqi; otherwise, majazi. The text refutes this by noting that a materialist's statement would be haqiqi despite being rationally false.
The opposing view fails to account for the liar's haqiqa.
4
Understand the liar analogy
The text gives the example of a liar saying 'Zaid came to me' intending literal meaning. The statement is haqiqa even though false. This shows that haqiqa does not require truthfulness; it requires the speaker's intention of literal meaning.
This bolsters the mutakallim-centered criterion.
5
Recognize the practical consequence (thamarah)
In interpreting texts, the classification affects how statements are understood. For example, a Muslim's statement attributing growth to spring is majazi, so the real agent is understood to be Allah. This guides legal reasoning.
The thamarah al-khilaf: different rulings in understanding agency.

Source Text

فان نسب المتكلم الا اگر متکلم یا فعل کی نسبت ایسے فاعل کی طرف کرتا ہے جو اس کے نزدیک اس فعل کا فاعل ہے ۔ تو یہ نسبتہ حقیقیہ کہلاتی ہے۔ اگر فعل کی نسبت غیر فاعل کی طرف کرتا ہے اس بنا پر کہ اس فعل کو اس منسوب الیہ کے ساتھ ملا لبستہ اور تعلق ہے تو یہ نسبتہ مجاز یہ ہے نحوا نبت الربيع البقل جب اس قسم کی عبارت مسلمان انسان بولتا ہے تو یقیناً انت کی نسبت جو ربیع کی طرف ہے ۔ یہ فاعل انبات کی طرف نہیں ہے کیونکہ انبات کا فاصل تو اللہ تعالیٰ ہے تو ربیع کی طرف جو استاد ہے ۔ متکلم مسلم کے نزدیک یہ نسبتہ الی غیر الفاعل ہے۔ البتہ فعل کو اس منسوب الیہ یعنی ربیع کے ساتھ ملابستہ و تعلق ہے کہ موسم ربیع میں نباتات کا آگاؤ اور نشوونما بالكثرة ہوتا ہے ۔ عندہ سے مراد عند المتکلم ہے۔ بعض حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ فعل کی نسبت ایسی شئی کی طرف کی جائے جو فاعل فی العقل ہو۔ یعنی عقلی لحاظ سے اس کا فاعل ہو تو یہ حقیقت ہے اگر غیر فاعل عند العقل کی طرف ہو تو وہ مجانہ ہے ۔ لیکن صاحب المفتاح کہتا ہے کہ عند العقل نہیں بلکہ عند المتكلم مراد ہے حتی تو قال الموحد الخ یعنی اگر موحد انسان انبت الربيع البقل کہہ تو یہ مجاز ہوگا۔ اور اسناد مجازی ہوگی کیونکہ موحد کے نزدیک فاصل انبات اللہ تعالیٰ ہے نہ کہ ربیع ۔ اگر یہی عبارت دھری انسان بولے تو اسناد حقیقی ہوگی کیونکہ دھری کے نزدیک انبات کا فاعل ربیع ہے ۔ اللہ تعالیٰ کو وہ متصرف مانتا نہیں ہے ۔ مع ان الربيع ليس فاعلاً فی العقل حالانکہ عقل کے نزدیک انبات کا فاعل ربیع نہیں ہے ۔ وہ دھری تو اس کلام میں جھوٹ بول رہا ہے کما اذا قال رجل جاءني زيد نفسه الجزیہ تو ایسے ہے کہ جیسے کوئی شخص کہہ کہ زید میرے پاس بنفس نفیس خود بخود آیا ہے. اور اس کے ساتھ معنی حقیقی کا ارادہ کرتا ہے اور حالانکہ زید نفس الامر میں اس کے پاس نہیں آیا تو یہ کلام حقیقتہ ہے ۔ باوجود اس کے کہ وہ جھوٹ صریح بول رہا ہے۔ لہذا فاعل عندہ یعنی عند المتکلم سے مراد یہ ہے کہ متکلم جب مخاطب کو یہ سمجھانا چاہیے کہ میرے نزدیک فاصل یہی ہے تو یہ کلام حقیقتہ ہے۔ جو خبر صادق اور کاذب دونوں کو شامل ہے ۔ (فصل) هذا الفصل في انواع علاقات المجاز چونکہ مجاز کے لئے ضروری تھا کہ اس کو معنی حقیقی کے ساتھ کوئی علاقہ ہو تو اس فصل میں ان علاقات کے اقسام پیش کئے اور یہ علاقات کتب سابقین میں بلا ضبط تھے ولکنی اور دتھا لیکن میں نے انھیں علی سبیل الحصر اور تقسیم عقلی کے طور پر وارد کیا ہے۔
If the speaker attributes an action to an agent that he believes to be the actual doer, then this ascription is called haqiqi (real). If he attributes the action to a non-doer due to some connection and relation of that action to the one attributed to, then it is a majazi (metaphorical) ascription. For example, the phrase 'anbat al-rabi' al-baqla' (The spring caused the herbage to grow). When a Muslim utters this phrase, he ascribes the action to the spring, but this is not to the actual doer because the real doer of making grow is Allah, so the ascription is to the spring. For the Muslim speaker, this is ascription to a non-doer. However, there is a connection between the action and the spring in that during spring season, plants grow abundantly. (The phrase 'when he' refers to 'according to the speaker') Some people say that the ascription of an action should be to something that is a doer in the intellect ('aql): if it is a doer in the intellect, it is haqiqi; if not, it is majazi. But the author of al-Miftah says that it is not by intellect but by the speaker (al-mutakallim). For example, if a monotheist (muwahhid) says 'anbat al-rabi' al-baqla', it is majaz because the true doer of making grow is Allah. But if a materialist (dahri) says the same phrase, it is haqiqi ascription because he believes the spring is the doer. Even though in intellect the spring is not the doer, the materialist is lying in that speech, just as if a man says 'Zaid came to me himself' intending its true meaning while Zaid did not actually come – his speech is haqiqa even though he is lying. Therefore, the intended meaning of 'when he' (al-fa'il 'indahu) is that when the speaker wants to inform the addressee that 'in my opinion this is the doer', then the speech is haqiqa, whether it is truthful or false. (Chapter) This chapter is on the types of relationships ('alaqat) of majaz. Since majaz requires a relationship to the real meaning, this chapter presents the types of these relationships. These relationships were not systematically collected in previous books, but I have presented them comprehensively and through rational division.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage discusses the distinction between real (haqiqi) and metaphorical (majazi) ascription (isnad) in language. The key point is that the classification depends on the speaker's belief (i'tiqad) rather than objective reality or even rational determination. The author explains that if the speaker attributes an action to an agent he believes to be the actual doer, the ascription is haqiqi. If he attributes it to a non-doer due to some connection, it is majazi. An example is given: 'Anbat al-rabi' al-baqla' (The spring caused the herbage to grow). A Muslim knows that Allah is the true Creator, so this ascription is majazi, based on the connection that plants flourish in spring. A materialist, however, believes the spring itself is the cause, so for him the ascription is haqiqi. The author refutes those who say the criterion is 'aql (intellect), citing Sahib al-Miftah who insists it is 'inda al-mutakallim (according to the speaker). This is supported by the analogy of a liar: if someone says 'Zaid came to me' intending the literal meaning, it is haqiqa even if he is lying, because sincerity is not a condition for haqiqa. The passage then introduces a new chapter on the types of relationships ('alaqat) that make majaz valid, a topic organized systematically by the author. This is crucial for understanding how metaphorical extension works in legal and theological discourse.

Key Terms
إسناد حقيقي (isnad haqiqi): Attribution of an action to an agent that the speaker believes is the actual doer.
إسناد مجازي (isnad majazi): Attribution of an action to an agent that the speaker knows is not the real doer, due to some connection.
عند المتكلم (inda al-mutakallim): According to the speaker's belief or intention, not objective reality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Miftah, what determines whether an ascription (isnad) is haqiqi or majazi?
A) The intellect ('aql) and rational analysis
B) The speaker's belief (i'tiqad) about the doer
C) The objective reality of who actually performed the action
D) The frequency of usage in the language

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the reality of ascription depends on the speaker's belief about the agent, not on objective or rational truth.
