Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute about the meaning of the conjunctive waw (و) in Arabic: whether it indicates mere conjunction (jama‘) or order (tartib). The author, representing the Hanafi position, begins by asserting that waw is for absolute conjunction, not order, citing transmission from language authorities and inductive evidence from usage. The example of the prohibition 'do not eat fish and drink milk' shows that combining is prohibited regardless of order, so order is not intended. Similarly, in the wudu verse, waw connects acts of ablution without implying sequence. The passage then addresses a proof from those who claim waw indicates order: the verse 'Indeed al-Safa and al-Marwa are among the symbols of Allah' and the Prophet's command to begin with what Allah began. The author refutes this, explaining that order in sa‘y (between Safa and Marwa) came from the Prophet's statement, not from the waw in the Quranic verse. The precedence of Safa in mention is due to its importance, not to impose obligation. Next, the passage discusses a claim that Imam Abu Hanifa himself considered waw to indicate order, based on the example of conditional divorce: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced.' According to Imam, only the first divorce occurs; the second and third are void because the wife becomes bā’in after the first, so waw must imply sequence. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say all three occur, indicating waw is for concurrence. The author refutes the claim by explaining that the difference between Imam and the Sahibayn in this case is not due to waw but to the principle of ta‘līq ‘alā sabīl al-ta‘āqub (suspension in sequence) according to Imam. When multiple suspended clauses follow a single condition, they are suspended sequentially, not simultaneously. At the moment the condition is fulfilled, the suspension becomes like an immediate pronouncement. In immediate divorce, if he says 'you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced' to a non-consummated wife, the first takes effect and the rest are void—this is because the locus for divorce is gone, not because of any order in waw. Therefore, the example does not prove that waw indicates order. The Sahibayn hold that the order is only in speech; at the moment of condition, all divorces occur together because the condition triggers them all simultaneously. Thus, the passage clarifies the Hanafi position that waw al-‘aṭf is for absolute conjunction, and any apparent evidence for order is refuted either by external factors (like the Prophet’s command) or by principles of suspension (ta‘līq) rather than by waw itself.

Key Terms
واو (waw): The letter waw used as a conjunctive particle (harf ‘ataf). According to this text, it indicates absolute conjunction (jama‘) without implying order (tartib).
ترتيب (tartib): Order or sequence. The text argues that waw does not imply tartib.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this lesson, why does the Prophet's command regarding Sa‘y not prove that waw indicates order?
A) Because the verse itself orders sequence, so no external proof is needed.
B) Because the order in Sa‘y comes from the Prophet's statement, not from the waw in the Quranic verse.
C) Because the Prophet's command is not authentic.
D) Because waw always indicates order, but only in this specific verse.

Key Takeaway
Waw al-‘aṭf in Arabic is fundamentally for conjunction, not sequence; any required order must come from an external indicator.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
Refuting the Claim That Imam Abu Hanifa Believed Waw Indicates Order: The Principle of Sequential Suspension
Dispute about the interpretation of Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in the case of conditional divorce is due to the principle of sequential suspension (ta‘līq ‘alā sabīl al-ta‘āqub) and not due to the meaning of waw, and apply this principle to similar cases.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on conditional triple talaq is based on ta‘līq mechanisms, not on waw indicating order.

Some scholars claimed that Imam Abu Hanifa considered waw to indicate order because, in a conditional divorce scenario, he ruled that only the first pronouncement takes effect, while the Sahibayn ruled that all three occur. This lesson dissects that argument and shows that the real cause is the Hanafi doctrine of sequential suspension (ta‘līq ‘alā sabīl al-ta‘āqub), not the particle waw.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
A man says to his non-consummated wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced.' The condition is entering the house, and there are three suspended talaq pronouncements.
Non-consummated wife becomes ba'in after first divorce, losing the locus for further divorces.
2
State the positions of Imam and Sahibayn
Imam Abu Hanifa: only the first divorce occurs; the second and third are void. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): all three divorces occur together.
This is the factual difference that the opponent cites.
3
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent argues: if waw were for mere conjunction (jama‘), all three divorces would occur at once upon condition. Since Imam says only one occurs, waw must indicate order.
Thus they attribute to Imam the view that waw is for order.
4
Analyze the Hanafi refutation
The passage responds: the difference is not due to waw but due to the principle of ta‘līq ‘alā sabīl al-ta‘āqub (sequential suspension). According to Imam, when multiple suspended clauses follow a single condition, they are suspended sequentially. At condition's realization, the first becomes immediate, then the second is suspended through the first, and after the first takes effect, the wife is no longer a locus for the second and third. Thus only one divorce occurs. This is analogous to immediate triple talaq to a non-consummated wife, where only the first takes effect regardless of waw.
Thus the ruling is based on the mechanism of suspension, not on the meaning of waw.
5
Confirm the Sahibayn's view
The Sahibayn hold that order is only in speech; at the moment the condition is realized, all suspended divorces occur simultaneously because the condition triggers them all at once. Thus all three take effect.
Their position is also independent of the meaning of waw.

ذکر کرتے ہیں جن کی طرف حاجہ شدیدہ ہوتی ہے اور ان کا نام حروف معانی ہے ان میں سے حروف عطف ہیں الواد به مطلق عطف کے لئے ہے یعنی ترتیب پر دال نہیں ہے بلکہ مطلق جمع کے لئے ہے۔ بالنقل عن ائمة اللغة ایک تو ائمہ لغہ سے ایسے منقول ہے داستقراء مواضع استعمالها اور اس کے مقام استعمال کا استقراء بھی اسی پر دال ہے کہ یہ مطلق عطف کے لئے ہے وھی بین الاسمين المختلفين یعنی یہ واو اسمین مختلفین کے اندر وہی فائدہ دیتی ہے جو الف تثنیہ بین الاسمين المتحدين فائدہ دیتا مثلاً جیسے آپ کہیں رجلان تو اس جیسا فائدہ ہوگا رجل وامراة میں ان مختلفین میں الف تشنہ کالا ناممکن نہیں ہے اس لئے واو عطف استعمال کی گئی ہے۔ وقولہم لا تاكل السمك ونشرب اللبن یہاں بھی مقصد یہی ہے۔ که لا تجمع بينهما خواہ مچھلی پہلے اور دودھ بعد میں یا اس کا بر عکس ہو دونوں ممنوع میں ترتیب نہیں ہے نلهذا لا يجب الترتیب چونکہ ایتہ وضور میں اعضاء ار ہو کے ادا کرنے کے حکم میں واو عطف استعمال ہوتی ہے جو مطلق اجتماع کو چاہتی ہے اس لئے ترتیب واجب نہیں ہے ۔
دامانی السعی یہ جواب ہے ان حضرات کے استدلال کا جو واؤ کے برائے ترتیب ہونے کے لئے پیش کرتے تھے استدلال یوں ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ان الصفا والمروة من شعائر اللہ تو صحابہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہم نے کہا باتما نبد ہم کس کے ساتھ ابتدا کریں تو نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ابدد ایما بدا اللہ اسی کے ساتھ ابتدا کہ وجس کے ساتھ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ابتدا کی ہے تو نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اسی آیت سے ترتیب سمجھی اور اسی کا حکم دیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ واو برائے ترتیب ہے خلاصہ جواب یہ کہ سعی بین الصفا و المروۃ کے اندر جو ترتیب ہے وہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے قول ابدوا بما بدا اللہ تعالیٰ کے ساتھ ہے۔ نہ کہ قرآن مجید کے ساتھ کیونکہ ان کا شعائر اللہ سے ہونا اس ترتیب کا متقاضی نہیں ہے ۔ وقولہ علیہ السلام ابد وا بما بدا الله تعالی بھی اس پر دال نہیں ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے جو ابتدا بالصفا فرمائی ہے۔ یہی تمہاری ہدایتہ کا موجب ہے لکن تقدیمہ لیکن جو صفا کو قرآن مجید میں مقد ما ذکر کیا گیا یہ کسی مصلحت سے خالی نہیں ہے مثلا تعظیم یا اس کی اہمیتہ وغیرہ ہو سکتی ہے اور یہ اہمیت اس کی اولویتہ کو تقاضا کرتی ہے نہ کہ وجوب کو البتہ وجوب ترتیب رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے لئے وحی غیر متلو سے ظاہر ہوئی اور ہمارے لئے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے قول ابدوا بما ابدا اللہ تعالیٰ سے بہر حال آیتہ جو مشتمل علی الود و العاطفہ ہے یہ موجب ترتیب نہیں ہے ۔ وزعم البعض انها للترتيب عند ابي حنيفة الخ بعض حضرات کا خیال ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک داو برائے ترتیب ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک برائے مقاز یقہ استدلالاً اپنے اس خیال پر بطور استدلال کے یہ مسئلہ پیش کرتے ہیں کہ جب ایک شخص اپنی بیوی غیر مدخولہ کو کہتا ہے
ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق وطالق وطالق تو امام کے نزدیک ایک طلاق اولی واقع ہوگی ثانیہ و ثالثہ واقع نہیں ہوگی تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ معطوفات بالترتیب واقع ہو رہے ہیں سہیلی کے ساتھ عورت بائنہ ہو چکی ہے اس کے بعد ثانیہ اور ثالثہ کے لئے وہ عورت محل طلاق نہیں ہی اگر ترتیب کے لئے نہ ہوتی تو پھر یہ تینوں طلاق مجتمعا دفعة واحدة واقع ہوتیں تو وہ مطلقہ بالثلث ہو جاتی جیسے ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق ثلثا میں تین واقع ہو جاتی ہے اور یہاں صورة مسطورہ میں ایسے نہیں ہوا تو معلوم ہوا کہ وا و صرف جمعیتہ اور اجتماع کے لئے نہیں ہے بلکہ ترتیب کے لئے ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک تینوں واقع ہو جاتی ہیں تو ان کے نزدیک واد برا سے مقارنته و اجتماع ہوئی. وهذا اى زعم ذلك باطل یہ خیال اس بعض کا باطل ہے کہ و او ترتیب کے لئے ہے بلکہ اصل وجہ یہ ہے کہ امام اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اختلاف کی وجہ یہ ہے ان عندہ امامت کے نزدیک کیا تعلق الثاني والثالث یعنی جیسے طالق ثانی اور ثالث شرط کے ساتھ متعلق بواسطة الاول ہو رہا ہے وقوع بھی ایسے ہی ہوگا یعنی اولیٰ پہلے اور ثانی وثالث جو اس کے واسطہ سے معلق تھیں وہ بعد میں کیونکہ امام کے نزدیک جب ایک شرط کے ساتھ متعدد اجزیہ کو معلق کیا جائے تو ان کی تعلیق علی سبیل التعاقب ہوتی ہے۔ صورة مذکورہ میں جب کہا ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق یہ شرط و جزا مل کر جملہ کا ما مستقله ہو چکا ہے جو اپنے ما بعد کی طرف محتاج نہیں ہے اور تعلیق طلاق بالدخول حاصل ہو چکی ہے اور اس کے بعد جب کہا وطالق یہ تو جملہ ناقصہ ہے افادہ معنی میں یہ محتاج الی الجملة الاولی ہے تو اس کی تعلیق بعد تعلیق الا ولی حاصل ہوگی اور اسی طرح ثالثہ وانت طالق اس کی تعلیق بالشرط بعد تعلیق الثانیہ حاصل ہوگی تو جیسے تعلیق ہے وقوع بھی ایسے ہوگا فان المعلق بالشرط کا لمنجن عند الشرط یعنی جو طلاق معلق بالشرط ہوتی ہے تو عند الشرط یعنی بوقت تحقق شرط کے اس کا حکم منجز کا ہو جاتا ہے مثلاً تجیز غیر مدخولہ کو کہتا انت طالق وطالق وطالق تو اس صورت میں غیر مدخولہ پہلے لفظ طالق کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو جاتی اور ثانی وثالث لغو ہو جاتی کیونکہ عورت جب پہلی کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو چکی ہے تو ثانی و ثالث کے لئے وہ محل نہیں رہی اس لئے لغو ہو جائیں گی اور تعلیق بالشرط میں جب شرط متحقق ہو تو گویا کہ اس وقت اس نے کہا ہے انت طالق و طالق وطالق کیونکہ معلق بالشرط بوقت تحقق شرط تنجیز کی مانند ہو جاتی ہے نہ یہ کہ یہاں ترتیب والو کو دخل ہے اس کو کوئی دخل نہیں ہے لہذا استدلال صحیح نہیں ہے ۔ وعندهما يقع جملة اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ تینوں طالق وطالق وطالق جملہ واقع ہو جائینگی اور عورت مطلقہ بالثلاث ہو جائے گی لان الترتيب في التكلم کیونکہ یہ ترتیب طالق وطالق وطالق میں صرف تکلم اور بولنے میں ہے۔ لانی صيرورته نطلیقا اس کے طلاق بننے میں تو ترتیب نہیں ہے کیونکہ طلاق بننا تو ہوگا اس وقت جب شرط متحقق ہوگی اس وقت تو کوئی
They mention those to which there is severe need, and their name is 'huruf al-ma'ani'. Among them are the conjunctive letters. The waw is for absolute conjunction, i.e., it does not indicate order, but rather absolute collection. It is transmitted from the imams of language, and the induction of its places of usage also indicates that it is for absolute conjunction, and it is between two different nouns, i.e., it gives the same benefit between two different nouns as the alif of dual gives between two identical nouns. For example, if you say 'rajulan', similarly there will be a benefit in 'rajul wa imra'a', since the alif of dual is impossible between two different nouns, so the conjunctive waw is used. And their statement 'la ta'kul al-samaka wa tashrab al-labana' also has the same purpose: that you do not combine both, whether the fish first and the milk after or the opposite; both are prohibited, no order. Hence order is not obligatory. Because in the verse of wudu, when the command to perform the actions of the limbs uses the conjunctive waw, which demands absolute combination, therefore order is not obligatory.
This is the answer to the argument of those who present that waw is for order. The argument is that Allah said 'Indeed al-Safa and al-Marwa are among the symbols of Allah.' The Companions said, 'With which shall we begin?' So the Prophet said, 'Begin with what Allah began.' So the Prophet understood order from this verse and ordered it, so it is known that waw is for order. The summary of the answer is that the order in sa'yi between Safa and Marwa is from the Prophet's statement 'Begin with what Allah began', not from the Qur'an, because their being from the symbols of Allah does not necessitate that order. And his statement 'Begin with what Allah began' does not indicate that Allah began with Safa. That is the cause of your guidance, but its precedence in the Qur'an is not devoid of some wisdom, like glorification or its importance, and this importance necessitates its priority, not obligation. Rather, the obligation of order was revealed to the Prophet through unrecited revelation (wahy ghayr matlu), and for us it is from the Prophet's statement 'Begin with what Allah began'. In any case, the verse which contains the conjunctive waw does not necessitate order.
And some claim that waw is for order according to Abu Hanifa, while according to the Sahibayn it is for concurrence. They argue on this claim by presenting the case when a man says to his non-consummated wife 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced.' According to Abu Hanifa, only the first divorce occurs, the second and third do not occur. So it is known that the conjuncts occur in order. Because after the first, the woman becomes separated (ba'in), and she is no longer a locus for divorce for the second and third. If waw were not for order, then all three divorces would occur together at once, and she would be triple-divorced, like if he said 'if you enter the house, you are triple divorced' where three occur. And here in the stated case it is not so, so it is known that waw is not for mere conjunction and collection, but for order. And according to the Sahibayn, all three occur, so for them waw indicates concurrence and combination.
And this claim is false. Rather, the real reason for the difference between Imam and the Sahibayn is that according to Imam, the relation of the second and third (divorce) to the condition is through the first (i.e., via the first), so occurrence will be similarly: the first first, and the second and third which were suspended through it will occur later. Because according to Imam, when multiple parts are suspended on one condition, their suspension is in a sequential manner. In the stated case, when he said 'If you enter the house, you are divorced', this condition and consequence have become a complete independent sentence, not needing what follows. And the suspension of divorce on entry is achieved. Then when he said 'and divorced', this is an incomplete sentence, needing the first sentence for meaning. So its suspension is after the first suspension. Similarly for the third 'and you are divorced', its suspension on the condition is after the suspension of the second. So as the suspension is, so is occurrence. Because the suspended upon condition becomes like an immediate pronouncement at the occurrence of the condition. For example, in an immediate pronouncement, if he says to a non-consummated wife 'you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced', the non-consummated wife becomes separated with the first word 'divorced', and the second and third become void because the woman, having become separated, is no longer a locus for divorce. And in conditional suspension, when the condition is realized, it is as if he said then 'you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced', because a conditional suspender at the time of the condition's realization becomes like an immediate pronouncement. It is not that the waw for order is involved; it has no role. Therefore the argument is not correct.
And according to the Sahibayn, all three 'divorced, and divorced, and divorced' occur together and the woman becomes triple-divorced. Because the order is only in speech; its becoming divorce has no order, because divorce occurs only at the moment the condition is realized, and at that moment there is no order.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute about the meaning of the conjunctive waw (و) in Arabic: whether it indicates mere conjunction (jama‘) or order (tartib). The author, representing the Hanafi position, begins by asserting that waw is for absolute conjunction, not order, citing transmission from language authorities and inductive evidence from usage. The example of the prohibition 'do not eat fish and drink milk' shows that combining is prohibited regardless of order, so order is not intended. Similarly, in the wudu verse, waw connects acts of ablution without implying sequence. The passage then addresses a proof from those who claim waw indicates order: the verse 'Indeed al-Safa and al-Marwa are among the symbols of Allah' and the Prophet's command to begin with what Allah began. The author refutes this, explaining that order in sa‘y (between Safa and Marwa) came from the Prophet's statement, not from the waw in the Quranic verse. The precedence of Safa in mention is due to its importance, not to impose obligation. Next, the passage discusses a claim that Imam Abu Hanifa himself considered waw to indicate order, based on the example of conditional divorce: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced.' According to Imam, only the first divorce occurs; the second and third are void because the wife becomes bā’in after the first, so waw must imply sequence. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say all three occur, indicating waw is for concurrence. The author refutes the claim by explaining that the difference between Imam and the Sahibayn in this case is not due to waw but to the principle of ta‘līq ‘alā sabīl al-ta‘āqub (suspension in sequence) according to Imam. When multiple suspended clauses follow a single condition, they are suspended sequentially, not simultaneously. At the moment the condition is fulfilled, the suspension becomes like an immediate pronouncement. In immediate divorce, if he says 'you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced' to a non-consummated wife, the first takes effect and the rest are void—this is because the locus for divorce is gone, not because of any order in waw. Therefore, the example does not prove that waw indicates order. The Sahibayn hold that the order is only in speech; at the moment of condition, all divorces occur together because the condition triggers them all simultaneously. Thus, the passage clarifies the Hanafi position that waw al-‘aṭf is for absolute conjunction, and any apparent evidence for order is refuted either by external factors (like the Prophet’s command) or by principles of suspension (ta‘līq) rather than by waw itself.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta‘liq): Suspension of a legal consequence (e.g., divorce) on the occurrence of a condition. The text discusses how multiple suspended clauses relate to a single condition.
التعليق على سبيل التعاقب (al-ta‘līq ‘alā sabīl al-ta‘āqub): Sequential suspension: when multiple suspended clauses are linked one after another under a single condition, each subsequent clause is suspended through the previous one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the actual reason for Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling that only one divorce occurs in the conditional triple talaq scenario?
A) He believes waw indicates order.
B) He applies the principle of sequential suspension (ta‘līq ‘alā sabīl al-ta‘āqub).
C) He follows a minority opinion.
D) He considers the condition invalid.

Key Takeaway
The difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in conditional divorce is rooted in the mechanism of sequential suspension, not in the meaning of the conjunctive waw.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Conditional Divorce and the Nature of Ta'liq: Sequential vs. Simultaneous Attachment
Analyzing the effect of conjunctive waw in conditional divorce formulas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the difference between sequential and simultaneous attachment in conditional divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) and explain why the particle waw is not the real basis of the Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
The real dispute in conditional multiple talaqs is not about the particle waw but about whether consequences attach sequentially or simultaneously to the condition.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi usul dispute: if a husband says, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced,' how many talaqs occur? While some might think the answer depends on the meaning of the conjunctive 'wa', the author explains that the deeper issue lies in the nature of ta'liq itself. We will trace the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and see how each school's view of sequential vs. simultaneous attachment leads to different rulings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Scenario
Read the conditional divorce formula: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced.' Note that the condition is stated once with multiple consequences (talaqs) joined by waw.
2
State the Disagreement
Identify the positions: Imam Abu Hanifa says one talaq occurs; Sahibayn say all three occur.
3
Refute the Oversimplification
Some claim the difference is about waw (sequence vs simultaneity). The author says this is wrong. Recognize the author's critique.
The passage calls this notion 'batil' (false).
4
Explore the Real Basis: Sequential vs. Simultaneous Ta'liq
According to Imam, the second and third talaqs are attached to the condition via the first talaq, forming a chain. The first makes the woman bain, voiding subsequent ones. According to Sahibayn, all consequences are attached directly to the condition at once; the sequence in utterance does not affect occurrence.
This is the key analytical insight.
5
Apply the Principle to Variants
Consider the case where consequences precede the condition (e.g., 'You are divorced, and divorced, and divorced, if you enter the house'). Here, all three occur by agreement because all are simultaneously attached to the delayed condition. Compare and confirm.

شرط کے ساتھ متعدد اجزیہ کو معلق کیا جائے تو ان کی تعلیق علی سبیل التعاقب ہوتی ہے۔ صورة مذکورہ میں جب کہا ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق یہ شرط و جزا مل کر جملہ کا ما مستقله ہو چکا ہے جو اپنے ما بعد کی طرف محتاج نہیں ہے اور تعلیق طلاق بالدخول حاصل ہو چکی ہے اور اس کے بعد جب کہا وطالق یہ تو جملہ ناقصہ ہے افادہ معنی میں یہ محتاج الی الجملة الاولی ہے تو اس کی تعلیق بعد تعلیق الا ولی حاصل ہوگی اور اسی طرح ثالثہ وانت طالق اس کی تعلیق بالشرط بعد تعلیق الثانیہ حاصل ہوگی تو جیسے تعلیق ہے وقوع بھی ایسے ہوگا فان المعلق بالشرط کا لمنجن عند الشرط یعنی جو طلاق معلق بالشرط ہوتی ہے تو عند الشرط یعنی بوقت تحقق شرط کے اس کا حکم منجز کا ہو جاتا ہے مثلاً تجیز غیر مدخولہ کو کہتا انت طالق وطالق وطالق تو اس صورت میں غیر مدخولہ پہلے لفظ طالق کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو جاتی اور ثانی وثالث لغو ہو جاتی کیونکہ عورت جب پہلی کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو چکی ہے تو ثانی و ثالث کے لئے وہ محل نہیں رہی اس لئے لغو ہو جائیں گی اور تعلیق بالشرط میں جب شرط متحقق ہو تو گویا کہ اس وقت اس نے کہا ہے انت طالق و طالق وطالق کیونکہ معلق بالشرط بوقت تحقق شرط تنجیز کی مانند ہو جاتی ہے نہ یہ کہ یہاں ترتیب والو کو دخل ہے اس کو کوئی دخل نہیں ہے لہذا استدلال صحیح نہیں ہے ۔ وعندهما يقع جملة اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ تینوں طالق وطالق وطالق جملہ واقع ہو جائینگی اور عورت مطلقہ بالثلاث ہو جائے گی لان الترتيب في التكلم کیونکہ یہ ترتیب طالق وطالق وطالق میں صرف تکلم اور بولنے میں ہے۔ لانی صیرورته نطلیقا اس کے طلاق بننے میں تو ترتیب نہیں ہے کیونکہ طلاق بننا تو ہوگا اس وقت جب شرط متحقق ہوگی اس وقت تو کوئی ترتیب نہیں ہے ۔ لہذا جو بوقت تكلم مرتب تھیں بوقت تحقق شرط تمام مجتمع ہو کر واقع ہوں گی یہ ایسے ہے کیا اذاکر ثلث صرات الخ یہ ایسے ہے جیسے غیر مدخولہ کے لئے اپنے قول اگر جزائیں بصورت تعدد مقدم کر دے اور شرط مؤخر مثلاً یوں کہہ غیر مدخولہ کو انت طالق وطالق وطالق ان دخلت الدار يقع المثلث اتفاقا کیونکہ اجزہ یہ جو ابتدا متوقفہ تھیں وہ تمام کی تمام دفعہ اس شرط مؤخر کے ساتھ معلق ہو جائینگی اور بوقت تحقق شرط تمام واقع ہو جائینگی
If you enter the house, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced; according to Imam, one first divorce occurs, the second and third do not occur. So it becomes known that these conjunctions occur sequentially; with the first, the woman becomes bain; after that, for the second and third, that woman is not a locus for divorce. If it were not for sequence, then these three divorces would occur collectively at once, and she would be triply divorced. And here in the stated case, it did not happen that way, so it is known that waw is not merely for conjunction and simultaneity but for sequence. And according to the two companions, all three occur, so in their view, waw indicates simultaneity. And this notion (of some) that waw is for sequence is false. Rather, the real reason for the difference between Imam and the two companions is that, according to Imam, the second and third are attached to the condition via the first; their occurrence follows the same pattern: the first occurs first, then the second and third which were attached through it occur later. Because according to Imam, when multiple consequences are attached to one condition, they attach successively. In the stated case, when he said 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' this condition and consequence together form an independent statement that does not need what follows. And the conditional divorce upon entry is established. After that, when he said 'and divorced,' this is an incomplete statement; in conveying meaning, it needs the first statement. So its attachment is after the first attachment. And similarly, the third 'you are divorced' attaches to the condition after the second attachment. So just as the attachment is, the occurrence is likewise. For indeed, that which is conditionally attached becomes like an immediate pronouncement at the occurrence of the condition. Thus, the conditionally attached divorce at the time of fulfilling the condition becomes like an immediate one. For example, if one says to a non-consummated wife 'You are divorced, and divorced, and divorced,' in that case, the non-consummated wife becomes bain with the first word of divorce, and the second and third are void. Because when the woman has become bain with the first, she is no longer a locus for the second and third, so they are void. And in the conditional, when the condition is fulfilled, it is as if at that moment he had said 'You are divorced, and divorced, and divorced' because the conditional at the time of condition fulfillment becomes like an immediate pronouncement. It is not that the waw has a role in sequence; it has no role. Therefore, the argument is correct. And according to the two companions, all three occur: the three 'talaq wa talaq wa talaq' occur together, and the woman becomes triply divorced, because the sequence is only in speech. Because the occurrence of divorce is not sequenced; it happens when the condition is fulfilled; at that time there is no sequence. Therefore, what was sequenced at the time of utterance occurs all together at the time of condition fulfillment. This is like if someone repeats the condition three times, e.g., says 'If you enter the house, you are divorced; if you enter the house, you are divorced; if you enter the house, you are divorced'; at the time of condition fulfillment (entering the house), all three divorces occur. Because the repetition and sequence were at the time of utterance, not at the time of condition fulfillment. Similarly here, three divorces occur. In this stated statement, where he said without repeating the condition with multiple consequences 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced'—and if he advances the consequences and delays the condition, e.g., says to a non-consummated wife 'You are divorced, and divorced, and divorced, if you enter the house,' it occurs as triple by agreement. Because the consequences that were initially suspended all become attached to this delayed condition at once, and at the time of condition fulfillment they all occur.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of a conditional divorce scenario where a person says to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced.' The author presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the effect of the conjunctive particle 'waw' (wa). The author first states and refutes a incorrect claim that the difference is about the meaning of waw (whether it indicates sequence or simultaneity). The true distinction, the author explains, lies in the nature of ta'liq (conditionality) according to each jurist. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that when multiple consequences are attached to a single condition, they attach successively. In the given formulation, the first 'taliq' forms an independent conditional sentence. The second and third 'taliq' are attached to the first clause; they do not form independent conditionals. Therefore, upon the condition's fulfillment, the first divorce takes effect, making the woman bain (irrevocably divorced). Since she is no longer a wife, the subsequent divorces have no effect. The Sahibayn, in contrast, hold that the sequence is only in utterance; the actual occurrence of divorce happens at the moment the condition is realized, and at that instant there is no sequence. Thus all three divorces occur simultaneously, and the woman becomes triply divorced. The author supports his explanation with examples: if a non-consummated wife is told 'You are divorced, and divorced, and divorced' (without condition), the first makes her bain and the rest are void. Similarly, in the conditional, upon condition fulfillment, it becomes analogous to that immediate pronouncement. The passage further discusses a variant: if the consequences are mentioned before the condition (e.g., 'You are divorced, and divorced, and divorced, if you enter the house'), all three occur by agreement because all consequences are simultaneously attached to the delayed condition.

Key Terms
وَاو (waw): The conjunctive particle; debated whether it indicates sequence or simultaneity in conditional divorce.
تَعْلِيق (ta'liq): Making a conditional divorce such that upon fulfillment of the condition, the talaq takes effect like an immediate pronouncement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Three
B) One
C) Two
D) None

Key Takeaway
The core of the dispute is whether multiple consequences of a single condition attach sequentially (Imam) or simultaneously (Sahibayn).

Simultaneous vs. Consecutive Emancipation: Ruling on Slave Marriages
Explaining the ruling on validity of nikah when two slave women are set free consecutively or simultaneously.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that consecutive emancipation (including 'waw' implying order) invalidates the second marriage, while simultaneous emancipation validates both.

Core Idea
Only the first slave wife becomes free; subsequent marriage to a slave while having a free wife is invalid.

This passage delves into a nuanced mas'ala concerning two slave women married without their master's permission. The key is the timing of their emancipation: whether the master frees them simultaneously or one after the other. Understanding the Hanafi analysis of the conjunctive particle 'waw' as implying sequentiality is crucial to grasping the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three scenarios: simultaneous emancipation, consecutive with two separate statements, and consecutive with a single statement using 'waw'.
2
Note the ruling for each
Record the ruling for each scenario: simultaneous = both valid; consecutive (both forms) = only the first valid.
3
Analyze the illa (reason)
The first woman becomes free immediately, making the second a marriage of a slave upon a free woman, which is invalid without permission.
The illa is the timing of freedom and the rule that marrying a slave while having a free wife is impermissible.
4
Examine the linguistic principle
Understand why 'waw' in a single statement implies order (tartib) in this context, leading to the same ruling as consecutive statements.
The text says 'because the waw is considered for sequence' (faj'altumuhu lil-tartib).
5
Compare formulations
Note the difference between Shams al-A'imma and Fakhr al-Islam: the latter introduces fuduli and requires husband's permission.
This is an intra-Hanafi variation; the passage seems to prefer Shams al-A'imma's view.

نان قبل اذا تزوج امتين الخ خلاصه سوال یہ کہ جب ایک شخص دو لونڈیوں کے ساتھ تزوج کرتا ہے بغیر اذن مولا هما ان لونڈیوں کے مولی کی رضا مندی کے بغیر تم اعتقها المولى معاً پھر ان دونوں لونڈیوں کو مولی معابیک وقت آزاد کرتا ہے مثلا کہتا ہے اعتقتكما تو صبح تکا حہما دونوں کا نکاح صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ و بكلامين منفصلين الگ کلاموں کے ساتھ ازاد کرتا ہے مثلا کہتا ہے اعتقت بده ثم قال پھر دوسری کے متعلق بعد زمان کہتا ہے اعتقت بذہ تو اس صورت میں نکاح اولی صیحیح ہو گا اور نکاح ثانیہ باطل کیونکہ ثانیہ کے اندر تزوج امتہ علی الحرۃ ہو رہا ہے جو صحیح نہیں کیونکہ پہلی کا نکاح تو ازاد ہوتے ہی منعقد ہو گیا اور ثانیہ اس وقت لونڈی ہے لہذا یہ باطل ہو جائے گا ۔ او بحرف العطف اگر کلامين منفصلین کے ساتھ نہیں ازاد کرتا بلکہ حرف عطف فی کلام واحد استعمال کرتا ہے کہتا اعتقت بده و بده بطل نکاح الثانية تو اس صورت عطف میں بھی پہلی معتقہ کا نکاح صحیح ہے اور ثانیہ کا باطل تو مقصود بالسوال یہی صورت عطف ہے کیونکہ یہاں خطف بالواو ہے فجعلتموه للترتيب کیونکہ پہلے بدھ کے ساتھ مشار الیہ اولاً ازاد ہوئی اس کا نکاح صحیح ہو گیا اس وقت دوسری غیر معتقہ ہے۔ تو لونڈی کا نکاح علی الحرہ صحیح نہیں ہے ۔ هكذا وضع المسألة الإ اصول شمس الائمہ ہیں مسئلہ مذکورہ کی وضع اسی طرح ہے جیسے ہم نے ذکر کی ہے واما فخر الاسلام البتہ فخرالاسلام کی وضع اس سے مختلف ہے وہ ھکذا کہ ایک شخص دو لونڈیوں کی تزویج بطور فضولی کے دوسرے شخص سے کر دیتا ہے بغیر ازن مولا هما وبغير اذن الزوج فقوله بغير اذن الزوج لاحاجة الى التقيد اس تقييد کی ضرورت نہیں ہے دعلی تقدیر اگر یہ تقیید لگائی جائے تو پھر ضروری ہے کہ زوج کی جانب سے کوئی فضولی آخر اس عقد نکاح کو قبول کرے کیونکہ ایک تصولی طرفین نکاح یعنی از طرف منکوحہ و نا کے متولی نہیں ہو
So if it is said [concerning] the issue of marrying two slave women... Summary of the question: When a person marries two slave women without the permission of their master, then the master frees both slave women at one time, e.g., says 'I freed both of you,' then the marriage of both becomes valid. And if he frees them with two separate statements, e.g., says 'I freed this one,' then later says 'I freed that one,' then in this case, the first marriage is valid and the second marriage is invalid, because in the second, there is marriage of a slave woman upon a free woman, which is not valid. Because the first's marriage was contracted upon her freedom, while the second at that time is a slave. So it becomes invalid. Or if he uses a conjunctive letter, not with two separate statements, but uses a conjunctive particle in a single statement: says 'I freed this one and that one,' then the marriage of the second is invalid. So in this case of conjunction as well, the first freed woman's marriage is valid, and the second's is invalid. The intended question is this case of conjunction, because here the waw is used, so you consider it for sequence. Because first, the referred-to earlier is freed first; her marriage becomes valid; at that time, the second is not freed. So the marriage of a slave woman upon a free woman is not valid. Thus is the formulation of the issue according to Shams al-A'imma. The formulation of the issue is as we have mentioned. As for Fakhr al-Islam, his formulation is different. He says: A person marries two slave women as a fuduli (unauthorized agent) to another person without the permission of their master and without the permission of the husband. His statement 'without the permission of the husband' — there is no need for this restriction. According to this estimation, if this restriction is made, then it is necessary that from the husband's side, another fuduli accepts this marriage contract, because one fuduli cannot manage both sides of the marriage (i.e., from the side of the women and the husband).
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage presents a mas'ala (legal issue) concerning the validity of the marriages of two slave women who married without their master's permission, and the effect of the master's subsequent emancipation. The author outlines three scenarios, referencing the formulations of Shams al-A'imma and Fakhr al-Islam. Scenario 1: If the master frees both slaves simultaneously with one statement (e.g., 'I freed both of you'), both marriages become valid because both were freed at the same time and thus were free at the moment of marriage validation. Scenario 2: If the master frees them with two separate statements (e.g., first 'I freed this one,' then later 'I freed that one'), only the first marriage is valid. The second is invalid because when the first is freed, she becomes free, and the second is still a slave; marrying a slave woman while having a free wife (tazawwuj amatin 'ala hurra) is impermissible without permission, and here the permission is not given. Scenario 3: If the master uses a conjunctive phrase in one sentence (e.g., 'I freed this one and that one'), the ruling is the same as consecutive emancipation: the first is valid, the second invalid. The author explains that this is because the waw here is understood to indicate order (tartib), so the first is freed first, making her free, and the second remains a slave at that moment. The author notes that this is the formulation of Shams al-A'imma, while Fakhr al-Islam has a different formulation involving fuduli marriage (unauthorized agency) and debates the necessity of permission from the husband.

Key Terms
عِتْق (itq): Emancipation of a slave; in this mas'ala, it retroactively validates or invalidates marriages depending on timing.
نِكَاح (nikah): Marriage contract; specifically marriage of slave women without master's permission, which is mawquf (suspended) until permission or emancipation.
فُضُولِيّ (fuduli): An unauthorized agent who acts without permission; in marriage, a fuduli contracts marriage on behalf of others without their consent.
مَوْقُوف (mawquf): Suspended or pending; a contract that is neither valid nor void until permission is given.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master frees two slave women who married without his permission by saying in one sentence 'I freed this one and that one,' what is the ruling on their marriages?
A) Both valid
B) Only the first valid
C) Only the second valid
D) Both invalid

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the timing of emancipation determines the validity of prior slave marriages; consecutive freeing, including by a single statement with 'and,' results in only the first marriage being valid.

The Waw Conjunction in Ratification: Simultaneity vs. Sequence
Case analysis of fuduli marriage ratification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that 'atf with waw may imply simultaneity to derive the ruling on simultaneous ratification of incompatible contracts.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, waw can indicate simultaneity, invalidating concurrent ratifications of incompatible sisters.

This passage examines a nuanced scenario: a fuduli marries two sisters to the same man in two separate contracts. The husband's ratification (ijaza) determines validity. The crucial usul question is: when the husband uses the particle waw to ratify both marriages, does the waw indicate absolute conjunction (allowing sequence) or simultaneous conjunction? The Hanafi school interprets it as simultaneous, leading to the invalidity of both marriages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the facts and ruling scenarios
First, understand the scenario: a fuduli contracts two sisters to one man in two separate contracts. Then consider the two ratification modes: separated (one after another) vs. simultaneous (using waw). Note the rulings for each.
The separate ratification makes the first valid and second void because the second sister becomes a sister-in-law.
2
Locate the specific wording of simultaneous ratification
The husband says: 'I validated the marriage of this and this' using the conjunction waw. Identify the exact Arabic phrase and the presence of 'atf (conjunction).
The phrase 'اجزت نکاح هذه وهذه' is the key.
3
Analyze the linguistic feature of 'atf with waw
In Hanafi usul, the letter waw as a conjunction can indicate either absolute conjunction (jam' la mujarrat) or simultaneous conjunction (qiran wa muqarana). Determine which one applies based on context.
The text states the waw is for 'qiran wa muqarana' (simultaneity), not for absolute conjunction.
4
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
Because the two sisters cannot be married simultaneously (they are mahram to each other), the waw must be interpreted as simultaneous. Therefore, both ratifications occur at once, and both marriages are void.
If the waw indicated only absolute conjunction, sequentiality could be imagined, allowing one to be valid.

وان زوجه الفضولی اختین بعقد ین اگر ایک فضولی کسی شخص کے ساتھ ایسی دو عورتوں کا نکاح جو آپس میں بہنیں ہیں دو عقدوں میں کر دیتا ہے ناجاز ھما متفرقا اگر خاوندان دونوں کا نکاح متفرقاً جائز قرار دیتا ہے ایک کا پہلے اور اُخریٰ کا بعد میں تو نکاح ثانیہ باطل ہے اور اولیٰ کا یعنی جس کے عقد کو پہلے جائز قرار دیا ہے وہ صحیح ہے دان اجازهما معاً اگر دونوں کو بیک وقت جائز قرار دیتا ہے کہتا ہے اجزت نکا حمما تو دونوں باطل ہیں اور اسی طرح اگر حرف عطف کے ساتھ دونوں کے نکاح کو جائز قرار دے کہ کہہ اجزت نکاح هذه وهذہ تو اس صورت میں بھی ہر ایک کا نکاح باطل ہو جاتے گا تو اس مسئلہ عطف میں آپ نے والد کو مطلق جمعیتہ کے لئے قرار نہیں دیا بلکہ قران و مقارنتہ کیلئے قرار دیا ہے تب تو دونوں کا نکاح باطل ہے اگر صرف جمعیتہ ہوئی اور مقارنہ ہوتی تو تعاقب کی صورت متصور کر کے ایک کا جائز ہو سکتا تھا
And if a fuduli marries two sisters to a person with two contracts: if the husband validates them separately, one first and the other later, the second marriage is void and the first is valid. If he validates both at once, saying 'I validated both marriages', both are void. Similarly, if he uses the conjunctive letter (waw) saying 'I validated the marriage of this and this', then in that case both marriages are void. So in this issue of 'atf, you did not consider the waw for absolute conjunction but for simultaneous conjunction. Then both marriages are void. If only conjunction (without simultaneity) occurred, then sequentiality could be imagined and one could be valid.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a fuduli (unauthorized agent) marries two sisters to the same man in two separate contracts. The key is the husband's ratification (ijaza). If he ratifies separately, the second is void because at the moment of second ratification the first marriage is already valid, making the second sister a sister-in-law. If he ratifies both together using 'waw' (and), the conjunction indicates simultaneity (qiran wa muqarana), so both are invalid because no sequence can be established. This analysis illustrates the Hanafi usul principle that the waw can indicate simultaneous conjunction unless context dictates otherwise.

Key Terms
فضولی (fuduli): An unauthorized agent who acts without permission in a contract.
إجازة (ijaza): Ratification or validation of a contract by the party concerned.
عطف ('atf): Grammatical conjunction, here referring to the use of 'waw' (and) in speech.
قران (qiran): Simultaneous conjunction; joining two things at the same time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a fuduli marries two sisters to one man with two separate contracts, and the man says 'I validate the marriage of this and this' using the waw, what is the ruling?
A) Both marriages are valid.
B) The first is valid, the second is invalid.
C) Both are invalid.
D) The second is valid, the first is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the interpretation of waw in legal context is guided by the prohibition of impossibility: when simultaneous application is impossible, waw indicates simultaneity, voiding concurrent acts.

Thumma's Delay: Speech or Ruling? An Intra-Hanafi Usul Dispute
Explaining thumma's meaning of order with delay and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Imam Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's interpretations of thumma's tarākhī and apply the practical consequence in a conditional divorce case.

Core Idea
Thumma indicates order with delay — but is the delay in the utterance or the legal effect? The answer changes divorce outcomes.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, even the meaning of a single particle like thumma can generate significant ikhtilaf among the school's founding Imams. This passage presents a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding whether the delay (tarākhī) implied by thumma pertains to the act of speech (takallum) or to the legal ruling (ḥukm). This is not merely a linguistic subtlety; it directly affects how conditional divorces are applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested element
Thumma is a conjunction meaning 'then', indicating both order (tartīb) and temporal delay (tarākhī). The dispute centers on the reference point of this delay.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the delay is in the speech: each utterance is separate with a pause in between.
Thus, each phrase is an independent statement.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn hold that the delay is in the ruling, not in speech. The utterances are connected without pause, but the legal effects are delayed.
This makes the entire speech a single connected statement.
4
Apply to a concrete example
The passage gives a conditional divorce: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced if you enter the house.' Work through the Sahibayn's analysis step-by-step.
Follow the text: all three are suspended on the one condition, then occur sequentially upon fulfillment.
5
Determine the practical consequence
For a consummated wife, all three divorces take effect. For a non-consummated wife, only the first takes effect (making her bāʾin), and the others become void.
The condition is the same, but the wife's status changes the number of effective divorces.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم للترتيب مع التراخی یعنی لفظ ثم ترتیب کے لئے ہے اور اس ترتیب میں ترافی بحسب الزمان بھی معتبر ہے ۔ راجع الى التكلم عندہ امام ابو حنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک یہ ترتیب مع التراخی راجع الی تکلم ہے یعنی ایک کلمہ بولا گویا کہ پھر ساکت ہو گیا پھر دوسرا کلمہ بولا والى الحكم عندهما صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ تراخی حکم میں ہے تکلم میں نہیں ہے بلکہ بلحاظ تکلم کے یہ کلام متصل ہے بدون اعتبارالسکوت فی الثانیہ فان قال انت طالق ثم طالق ثمطالق ان دخلت الدار فعند مما يتعلقن جميعا تو صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ تینوں طلاق دخول دار کی شرط کے ساتھ معلق ہو جائیں گی کیونکہ یہ ایک ہی کلام متصلہ ہے اور نہ کوئی فصل ہے اور نہ اعتبار سکوت اس لیے یہ تمام ایک ہی شرط جو کہ موخر ہے کے ساتھ معلق ہو جائے گی البتہ بوقت دخول دار کے يغزلن مرتبا یعنی ان طلاقوں کا نزول اور وقوع بالترتیب ہوگا اگر عورت مدخولہ ہوئی تو یکے بعد دیگرے تینوں واقع ہو جائیں گی کیونکہ مدخولہ علی الترتیب محل ثلاث ہو سکتی ہے۔ وان لم تكن مدخولا بها اگر عورت غیر مدخولہ نہوئی تو طلاق اول کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو جا گی۔ ثانی اور ثالث کا وہ محمل نہیں رہی ہے لہذا یہ لغو ہو جائیں گی تو بقع واحدہ تو یہ اس صورت میں تھا جب شرط مؤخر اور جزا متقدم متقی وكذا ان قدم الشرط اور اگر شرط مقدم اور جزا موخر ہو یعنی یوں
Thumma is for order with delay, meaning the word thumma is for order, and in that order, temporal delay is also considered. It refers to speech: according to Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), this order with delay refers to speech, meaning he spoke one word, then paused, then spoke another word. And according to them (the Sahibayn), this delay refers to the ruling, not to speech; rather, in terms of speech, it is connected speech without consideration of silence. Thus, if he says: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced if you enter the house,' then according to them all three divorces are suspended on the condition of entering the house, because it is one connected speech with no separation and no consideration of silence. Therefore, all are suspended on that single condition which is later. However, at the time of entering the house, they occur sequentially: if the woman is one who has been consummated, all three occur one after another, because a consummated wife can receive three divorces sequentially. And if she is not consummated, then with the first divorce she becomes irreversibly divorced (bāʾin); there remains no capacity for the second and third, so they become void. This was the case when the condition is later and the consequence is earlier. Similarly, if the condition is advanced and the consequence is later, i.e. like this: ...
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) in usul al-fiqh regarding the meaning of the Arabic particle thumma (ثم). Two positions are presented: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the delay (تراخي) indicated by thumma is in the speech (تكلم) — that is, there is a pause between utterances, making them separate statements. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the delay is in the ruling (حكم), not in speech; the words are connected without pause, but the legal effect is delayed. This difference has concrete fiqh consequences. The example given: a man says to his wife: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced if you enter the house.' According to the Sahibayn, since the speech is continuous, all three divorces are suspended on the single condition of entering the house. Upon entry, if the wife is consummated (مدخول بها), all three occur sequentially; if not consummated, only the first takes effect (making her irrevocably divorced) and the subsequent two are void. The passage ends by contrasting this case with one where the condition precedes the consequence, but the text is cut off. This illustrates how usul principles directly shape fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
ثم (thumma): A particle indicating order (ترتيب) along with temporal delay (تراخي).
تراخي (tarākhī): Temporal delay; the meaning associated with thumma that distinguishes it from fa (immediate succession).
تكلم (takallum): Speech; the act of uttering words. The reference point for Abu Hanifa's interpretation of thumma's delay.
حكم (ḥukm): Ruling; legal effect. The reference point for the Sahibayn's interpretation of thumma's delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only one divorce occurs, because the others are suspended on a condition that cannot be fulfilled.
B) All three divorces occur together upon entry to the house.
C) The first divorce makes her bāʾin, so the second and third are void.
D) No divorce occurs until all conditions are met.

Key Takeaway
The usul dispute over thumma's delay (speech vs. ruling) has direct fiqh consequences: it determines whether multiple conditional clauses are linked or independent.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Meaning of 'Thumma' in Conditional Talaq: Sequence with Delay
Explains Hanafi disagreement on whether 'thumma' implies delay in speech or in effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the meaning of 'thumma', distinguish the practical outcomes for conditional talaq, and apply the difference to scenarios involving consummated and non-consummated wives.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa sees delay in speech; Sahibayn see delay in legal effect — the ruling changes accordingly.

In this lesson, we examine a key dispute within the Hanafi school over the meaning of the word 'thumma' (then) in conditional divorce. The difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hinges on whether 'thumma' implies a temporal delay in the utterance itself or a delay in the legal ruling. This distinction leads to very different outcomes in practice, especially when combined with the wife's status and the order of condition and consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed term
The word 'thumma' (then) in Arabic generally indicates sequence with a temporal delay (tartib ma'a al-tarakhi). The dispute is over what this delay attaches to: the speech act or the legal ruling.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the delay refers to speech itself (tarakhi fi al-takallum). Each utterance is separate, with a valid silence between them. Thus, each 'taliq' is an independent statement.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the delay refers to the ruling (tarakhi fi al-hukm), not the speech. The speech is continuous, with no legally significant silence. Their proof is that 'thumma' links clauses in a single connected utterance.
4
Apply both positions to a conditional talaq
Consider: 'Inti taliq, thumma taliq, thumma taliq in dakhalti al-dar'. According to Sahibayn, all three are suspended on the condition because the speech is continuous. According to Abu Hanifa, the first 'taliq' is a complete utterance that occurs immediately (if the wife is non-consummated, she becomes ba'in).
This step shows the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Extend to advanced and postponed conditions
The passage also covers cases where the condition is advanced or postponed, and for consummated vs. non-consummated wives. Understand how each school's view leads to different numbers of immediate vs. suspended divorces.
The benefit (faa'ida) of suspension: if the wife is later remarried and the condition occurs, the suspended divorce takes effect.

ویدغو الباقی اور باقی دو لغو ہو جائیگی ۔ لعدم المحل چونکہ غیر مدخولہ ایک طلاق کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو جاتی ہے اور عدہ بھی اس پر نہیں ہے لہذا وہ محل طلاق نہیں رہی باقی لغو ہوں گی ۔ وان قدم الشرط اسی لفظ سے معلوم ہو رہا ہے کہ سابقہ بحث تقدیم جزا کی صورت میں ہے ۔ اگر شرط کو مقدم کرتا ہے اور جزا یعنی انت طالق ثم طالق ثم طالق کو مؤخر کرتا ہے تعلق الدولی تو سہیلی طلاق متعلق بالشرط ہو جائے گی وننزل الثاني یعنی ثم طالق جو کہا یہ فی الحال واقع ہو جائیں گی کیونکہ اس کا تعلق بالشرط نہیں ہے كا نہ قال تو گویا اس کا کہنا یوں ہو جائے گا ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق کہا اور اس کے بعد وہ ساکت و خاموش رہا پھر بعد از سکوت کہا وانت طالق تو یہ فی الحال واقع ہو جائے گی اور متعلق بالشرط نہیں ہوگی۔ ولفا الثالث اور ثالث لغو ہو جائے گی کیونکہ غیر مدخولہ بائنہ ہو چکی ہے ثالث کا محل نہیں رہی ۔ فائدہ تعلق الدول پہلی طلاق کے معلق بالشرط ہونے کا فائدہ اور نتیجہ یہ ہو گا کہ ان ملکھا ثانیا کہ وہ عورت اگر ثانیا اس کے ملک نکاح میں آئی اور وہ شرط دخول ار والی موجود ہوئی تو طلاق واقع ہو جائیگی ۔ وفي المدخول بها به تمام بحث غیر مدخولہ کے متعلق تھی اگر عورت مدخولہ ہو اور جزا مقدم على الشرط ہو یعنی یوں ہو انت طالق ثم طالق ثم طالق ان دخلت الدار تقدیم جزا کی قید یہاں بھی متن میں ذکر نہیں کی ۔ وجه عدم الذكر مرة سابقا نزل الاول والثانی پہلا اور دوسرا طالق في الحال واقع ہو جائے گا لعدم تعلقها بالشرط کیونکہ ان کا تعلق شرط کے ساتھ نہیں ہے گویا دو مرتبہ طالق بول کر ساکت ہو گیا ہے پھر اس کے بعد کہا ہے انت طالق ان دخلت الدار ولما كانت المرأه مدا خو لا بما ا ل چونکہ عورت مدخولہ ہے اس لیئے طلاق اول کے ساتھ بائنہ نہیں ہوگی محل طلاق باقی ہے اس کے بعد ثانیا جو ثم طالق کہا ہے واقع ہو جائے گی فیقع تطلیقتان -
Then (thumma) is for sequence with delay, meaning the word 'thumma' is for sequence and in this sequence delay in time is also considered. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this sequence with delay refers to speech, i.e., he uttered one word, then became silent, then uttered the second word. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), this delay is in the ruling, not in speech; rather, with respect to speech, this speech is continuous, without considering silence in the second [utterance]. For example, if he said 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced, if you enter the house', then according to the two, these three divorces are all suspended on the condition of entering the house, because it is one continuous speech, and there is no separation and no consideration of silence. Therefore, all are suspended on the single condition that is delayed. However, at the time of entering the house, they occur sequentially, i.e., the divorces descend and occur in order. If the woman is consummated, all three occur one after another because a consummated wife can be the locus for three divorces sequentially. And if she is not consummated, the first divorce makes her irrevocably separate, so the second and third have no locus and become void. That was one case: when the condition is postponed and the consequence is advanced. Similarly, if he advances the condition, i.e., says: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, then divorced, then divorced', the same ruling applies, and there is no difference between the two forms. Then [discussion] regarding the non-consummated wife: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, when the condition is advanced, only the first occurs. The author did not mention the advancing of the consequence. Its reason: because in this passage the word 'condition' appears in the text, so it indicates that the previous discussion was about the case when the consequence is advanced; therefore the text did not specify it. The first occurs: according to Imam, in the case of advancing the consequence upon a non-consummated wife, the first divorce occurs immediately because it is not related to the delayed condition, as if he said 'You are divorced' and then became silent, because 'thumma' is for delay in speech, so this 'You are divorced' occurs immediately and the non-consummated wife becomes irrevocably separate. The remaining two are void. Because a non-consummated wife becomes irrevocably separate with one divorce and she has no waiting period, so she is no longer a locus for divorce. And if he advances the condition, this phrase indicates that the previous discussion was about advancing the consequence. If he advances the condition and postpones the consequence, i.e., 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced', then the first divorce is suspended on the condition, and the second occurs immediately because it is not related to the condition, as if he said 'If you enter the house, you are divorced' and then remained silent, then after silence said 'and you are divorced', so this occurs immediately and is not suspended on the condition. And the third is void because the non-consummated wife has become irrevocably separate. The benefit of the suspension of the first divorce: if afterwards she comes into his possession (remarriage) and the condition of entering the house occurs, then the divorce occurs. And regarding the consummated wife: that completes the discussion. If the woman is consummated and the consequence is advanced over the condition, i.e., 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced, if you enter the house' – the qualification of advancing the consequence is not mentioned here either. The reason for not mentioning it again: the first and second occur immediately because they are not related to the condition, as if he uttered two divorces and became silent, then afterwards said 'You are divorced if you enter the house'. Since the woman is consummated, she does not become irrevocably separate with the first divorce; the locus for divorce remains. Then the second that he said as 'thumma taliq' occurs. So two divorces occur.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the meaning of the word 'thumma' (then) in conditional divorce statements. The key difference is: Abu Hanifa holds that 'thumma' implies a temporal delay in speech itself – each utterance is separate with a pause. The Sahibayn hold that 'thumma' implies a delay in the legal effect, but the speech is continuous without pause. This has practical consequences in examples like a man saying to his wife: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced, if you enter the house.' According to the Sahibayn, all three divorces are suspended on the condition because the speech is continuous. According to Abu Hanifa, only the first or last may be suspended depending on order. The passage then details various scenarios: with a non-consummated wife (ghair madkhul biha) and a consummated wife (madkhul biha), and when the condition is advanced (muqaddam) or postponed (mu'akhkhar). For a non-consummated wife, only one divorce occurs immediately because she becomes irrevocably separate (ba'in) with one, so subsequent divorces are void. For a consummated wife, where the consequence is advanced, the first two divorces occur immediately and the third is suspended; if the condition occurs, it falls. The passage also discusses the benefit of suspension: if the wife is remarried and the condition later occurs, the suspended divorce takes effect.

Key Terms
ثم (thumma): A particle meaning 'then', indicating sequence with a temporal delay.
ترتیب مع التراخی (tartib ma'a al-tarakhi): Sequence with delay; the order in which events occur with a lapse of time between them.
مدخولہ (madkhul biha): A woman with whom consummation has taken place, making her subject to three divorces sequentially.
غیر مدخولہ (ghair madkhul biha): A woman who has not been consummated; she becomes irrevocably separate (ba'in) with one divorce and cannot receive more divorces until remarriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if a man says to his consummated wife 'Inti taliq, thumma taliq, thumma taliq in dakhalti al-dar', how many divorces are suspended on the condition?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
The meaning of 'thumma' in conditional talaq is contested: Abu Hanifa interprets it as separation in speech, while the Sahibayn interpret it as delay in ruling with continuous speech, leading to different counts of immediate and suspended divorces.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Multiple Legal Meanings of 'على' in Hanafi Usul
Definition of 'على' and its dispute in divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three fiqhi meanings of the preposition 'على' (obligation, condition, and metaphorical substitution for 'ب') and apply the correct meaning in contracts and divorce scenarios based on Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, 'على' means obligation by reality, condition in pledges and divorce, but in pure contracts it shifts to 'ب' to avoid gharar.

The simple preposition 'على' (upon, on) carries multiple legal weights in Hanafi fiqh. It can indicate an obligation, a condition, or even serve as a substitute for the letter 'ب' (with/for) in contracts. Understanding which meaning applies is crucial for correct rulings in debts, pledges, sales, and divorce. In this lesson, we dissect these meanings using the Hanafi usul method, focusing on the distinction between pure transactions and those involving relinquishment, and examine the famous ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on divorce for money.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three meanings of 'على'
First, recognize that 'على' has three distinct legal uses: (1) obligation (wujūb) when referring to debts or duties; (2) condition (sharṭ) when used with pledges or divorce; (3) metaphorical meaning as 'ب' (bā') in pure transactions like sale and marriage.
The real meaning (haqīqah) according to Hanafi jurists is obligation, derived from the idea of something being 'upon' a person.
2
Understand the rule for pure transactions (mu'āwaḍāt muḥḍa)
In pure transactions (sale, lease, marriage), 'على' cannot retain its meaning of condition because that would introduce uncertainty (khaṭar) resembling gambling. Hence, it is interpreted metaphorically as 'ب' (with/for) by consensus.
These transactions are free from the element of relinquishment (isqāṭ), unlike divorce or manumission.
3
Analyze the dispute on divorce for money
In divorce for money (ṭalāq 'alā al-māl), the Sahibayn treat 'على' as 'ب' because the transaction is a mu'āwaḍah, so the woman owes a proportionate share. Imam Abu Hanifa insists on the real meaning of condition, so unless the full number of divorces is given, no payment is due.
The key principle: conditions are indivisible; considerations are divisible.
4
Apply the rule to a concrete case
Given the scenario: a wife says 'Divorce me three times for a thousand,' and the husband gives one divorce. According to Imam, she owes nothing; according to the Sahibayn, she owes one-third. Recognize how the meaning assigned to 'على' leads to different outcomes.
Practice by varying the scenario: what if the husband gives two divorces? Three?

‘Alī’ [is] for isti‘lā’ [highness] meaning that the word ‘alī is for highness, and according to the jurists, what is intended by it is obligation, like ‘alayhi daynun – debt is upon him, so it is as if the debt is above him and riding upon him, just as a rider is upon the mount, so debt is upon the debtor. Because of this analogy, according to the jurists, the word ‘alī is for obligation, and this meaning is the real meaning in their view. And it is also used for condition, i.e., the word ‘alī is also used for condition, meaning that what comes after it becomes a condition for what comes before it, like ‘yubāyi‘naka ‘alā an lā yushrikna billāhi shay’an’ – that is, we pledge allegiance to you on the condition of not associating anything with Allah. So the pledge had this condition that they acknowledge that they will not commit shirk, etc. If they do not acknowledge these things, then the pledge cannot be. And it is in pure transactions, i.e., those devoid of the meaning of relinquishment, meaning those in which there is no meaning of relinquishment. This is a distinction from divorce and manumission because in them there is relinquishment of ownership. So the word ‘alī in pure transactions takes the meaning of ‘bā’’ by consensus, but it is metaphorical, i.e., its meaning is not real, because permanence (luzūm) is suitable for attachment (ilṣāq). This is an explanation of the relationship of the metaphor: since ‘alī comes for permanence, and permanence is suitable for attachment, because in attachment and connection there is also a kind of permanence. The metaphorical meaning is intended in pure transactions, like sale, lease, marriage, because the real meaning is not possible there, for according to the jurists its meaning is condition, and pure transactions involve risk (khaṭar) and do not accept condition. Risk means uncertainty between two matters, which causes them to be undecided between occurring and not occurring. If they are suspended on a condition, if the condition occurs, the sale happens, otherwise not. In that case, the sale would be akin to gambling, which is undecided between winning and losing. To avoid resemblance to gambling, it should not be suspended on a condition. So if one says, ‘I sold you this slave on a thousand,’ its meaning is ‘for a thousand’ (bi’alf). Similarly, in divorce according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the word ‘alī also takes the meaning of ‘bā’’ because divorce for money from the woman's side is a transaction; therefore divorce for money falls under transactions, and here the word ‘alī takes the meaning of ‘bā’’. And according to him (Imam Abu Hanifa), it is for condition. He acts according to the original meaning because the original meaning of ‘alī is condition, so he acts upon it, because divorce can accept condition. Divorce can be suspended on a condition. So he interprets his word upon its real meaning, which is condition. So in the case where a woman says, ‘Divorce me three times for a thousand dirhams,’ and the husband gives one divorce, then the thousand is not owed according to him. Due to the previous difference between the two (Sahibayn) and Imam, there is a difference in the ruling of this issue. The principle is that the parts of a condition are not divided upon the parts of the conditioned; i.e., if the conditioned exists completely, the condition is incurred; if some parts of the conditioned exist, then the parts of the condition are not incurred in exchange, but rather the condition is not incurred at all. Unlike consideration, which is divided upon the parts of the counter-value: if the counter-value is complete, the complete consideration is due; if some part of the counter-value is present, then consideration is also due for that part. According to Imam, since the word ‘alī is for condition, and the conditioned was three divorces, since the conditioned is not present here, therefore the condition of a thousand is not incurred. And it cannot be that since one part of the conditioned is present, therefore some part of the condition
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and disputational lesson on the word 'على' ('alā). It starts by stating that 'على' originally denotes superiority ('alā'). However, Hanafi jurists have assigned it a specialized meaning of obligation (wujub) when used in legal contexts, e.g., 'alayhi daynun' (upon him is a debt). They consider this the real (haqiqah) meaning. Additionally, it is used for condition (shart), as in the Quranic pledge of allegiance 'yubayi'naka 'ala...' meaning on condition. The passage then explains a critical rule: in pure transactions (معاوضات محضہ), which are free from any element of relinquishment (isqat), 'على' is interpreted metaphorically as 'ب' (with/for). The reason is that if 'على' were taken in its real meaning of condition, it would introduce gharar (uncertainty) into the transaction, making it resemble gambling. Examples: sale, lease, marriage. However, divorce (and manumission) are different because they involve relinquishment of ownership. Here, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) treat 'على' as 'ب' because divorce for money is a transaction, but Imam Abu Hanifa treats it as condition because divorce can accept conditional suspension. The practical consequence is illustrated: if a woman says 'Divorce me three times for a thousand' and the husband gives only one divorce, according to Imam the thousand is not owed because the condition (three divorces) is not fulfilled and condition is indivisible, while according to the Sahibayn the thousand or its proportionate part is due because 'على' here means 'ب' and consideration is divisible.

Key Terms
على ('alā): A preposition with multiple legal meanings: originally for superiority, but in fiqh it signifies obligation (wujub), condition (shart), or substitute for 'ب' (with) in contracts.
وجوب (wujūb): Obligation; the quality of a command that is binding. Here, 'على' indicates that something is owed or required.
شرط (sharṭ): Condition; what must occur for a legal act to be valid or for an obligation to arise. Used with 'على' to express conditionality.
معاوضات محضہ (mu'āwaḍāt muḥḍa): Pure transactions (e.g., sale, lease, marriage) that involve exchange of consideration without any element of relinquishment (isqat).
خطر (khaṭar): Uncertainty (gharar) that leads to resemblance to gambling; a reason to avoid conditional contracts in pure transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) She owes the full thousand because the condition is fulfilled by one divorce.
B) She owes nothing because the condition (three divorces) is not fulfilled and condition is indivisible.
C) She owes one-third of the thousand because consideration is divisible.
D) She owes nothing because 'على' here means 'ب' and the transaction is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The meaning of 'على' in Hanafi fiqh depends on context: it can indicate obligation, condition, or substitute for 'ب' in pure transactions, and the correct identification is crucial for valid contracts and accurate rulings.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
The Particle 'على' in Contracts and Divorce: A Hanafi Usul Dispute
Explains the different meanings of 'على' in pure contracts and divorce, with a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing the meaning of 'على' in pure contracts versus divorce, and evaluate the ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on its interpretation in compensated divorce.

Core Idea
The particle 'على' can mean either condition or compensation; pure contracts force a metaphorical reading, while divorce allows the original conditional meaning.

This passage from the Sharh al-Talwiḥ/Tawḍīḥ tradition explores a subtle but consequential point of usul: the interpretation of the particle 'على' (ʿalā) in different legal contexts. While in pure contracts like sale it is universally interpreted as 'with' (باء) by metaphor, divorce introduces ambiguity. Imam Abu Hanifa holds to the literal (conditional) meaning; his two disciples analogize to contracts, treating it as compensation. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how context and analogy interact in Hanafi istinbāṭ.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish pure commutative contracts from contracts involving isqat
Identify the two categories: pure contracts (sale, lease, marriage) and contracts that involve dropping of ownership (divorce, emancipation). The distinction determines whether 'على' can retain its original meaning of condition.
Pure contracts cannot accept condition due to gharar (risk).
2
Identify the default meaning of 'على' according to Hanafi usul
The original meaning of 'على' is condition (shart). In pure contracts, this is impossible because it would introduce gambling-like uncertainty; hence it is interpreted metaphorically as 'with' (باء).
This is a consensus among Hanafis.
3
Trace the ikhtilaf in divorce for compensation
The Sahibayn analogize compensated divorce to pure contracts, treating 'على' as 'with' (compensation). Imam Abu Hanifa insists on the original conditional meaning because divorce can be conditional.
The key point: divorce accepts ta'liq, so there is no preventer (mani') from using the haqiqah.
4
Apply the principle of divisibility
In the example (three divorces on a thousand dirhams, but only one given), Abu Hanifa says no payment is due because parts of a condition are not divisible over parts of the conditioned. The Sahibayn say one-third is due because compensation is divisible.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical consequence of the dispute.

قمار کے مشابہت سے بچانے کے لئے معلق بالشرط نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ فاذا قال بعت منك هذا العبد على الفب تو اس کا معنی ہوگا بالف وكذا فی الطلاق عندهما صاحبین کے نزدیک طلاق میں بھی کلمہ علی بمعنی الباء ہوگا مسئلہ کے حکم میں اختلاف ہوا ہے ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ اجزاء شرط اجزار مشرو را پر منقسم نہیں ہوتے یعنی اگر مشرو ط ا مکمل طور پر موجود ہے تو شرط عائد ہو جائیگی اگر مشروط کے کچھ اجزا موجود ہوتے ہیں تو اس کے
